<noinclude>{{Short description|none}}
Each entry on this list of common misconceptions is worded as a correction; the misconceptions themselves are implied rather than stated. These entries are concise summaries; the main subject articles can be consulted for more detail.

{{Main|List of common misconceptions}}</noinclude>

=== Business === <!-- NOTE: Headers are done this way so that the transclusion works. Please do not "fixe" them. -->
* Federal [[Legal Tender Act|legal tender laws]] in the United States do not require that private businesses, persons, or organizations accept cash for payment, though it must be treated as valid payment for debts when tendered to a creditor.<noinclude><ref name="Treasury Department 2011">a. {{#invoke:cite web||date=January 4, 2011 |title=Legal Tender Status |url=http://www.treasury.gov/resource-center/faqs/Currency/Pages/legal-tender.aspx |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170124025750/https://www.treasury.gov/resource-center/faqs/Currency/Pages/legal-tender.aspx |archive-date=January 24, 2017 |access-date=January 27, 2017 |work=Resource Center |publisher=[[U.S. Department of the Treasury]]}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||date=June 17, 2011 |title=Is it legal for a business in the United States to refuse cash as a form of payment? |url=https://www.federalreserve.gov/faqs/currency_12772.htm |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170121155832/https://www.federalreserve.gov/faqs/currency_12772.htm |archive-date=January 21, 2017 |access-date=January 27, 2017 |website=Board of Governors of the Federal Reserve System |publisher=[[Federal Reserve System]]}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite web||title=What is A "Legal Tender Law"? And, is It a Problem? |url=https://www.forbes.com/sites/nathanlewis/2017/04/18/what-is-a-legal-tender-law-and-is-it-a-problem |archive-url=https://archive.today/20180603142035/https://www.forbes.com/sites/nathanlewis/2017/04/18/what-is-a-legal-tender-law-and-is-it-a-problem |archive-date=June 3, 2018 |website=[[Forbes]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Adidas]] is not an acronym for "All day I dream about sports", "All day I dream about soccer", or "[[A.D.I.D.A.S. (Korn song)|All day I dream about sex]]". The company was named after its founder [[Adolf Dassler|Adolf "Adi" Dassler]] in 1949. The earliest publication found of the latter [[backronym]] was in 1978, as a joke.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=VanHooker |first=Brian |date=October 27, 2020 |title=The True Story Behind Adidas' 'All Day I Dream About Sex' (And Other Bogus Brand Acronyms) |url=https://melmagazine.com/en-us/story/what-does-adidas-stand-for-bing-ford-spam |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230403225346/https://melmagazine.com/en-us/story/what-does-adidas-stand-for-bing-ford-spam |archive-date=April 3, 2023 |access-date=June 28, 2022 |website=[[MEL Magazine]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=April 23, 2018 |title=Pop Culture Dictionary: Adidas |url=https://www.dictionary.com/e/pop-culture/adidas/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231129052622/https://www.dictionary.com/e/pop-culture/adidas/ |archive-date=November 29, 2023 |access-date=June 22, 2024 |website=[[Dictionary.com]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* The letters "AR" in [[AR-15–style rifle|AR-15]] stand for "ArmaLite Rifle", reflecting the company [[ArmaLite]] that originally manufactured the weapon. They do not stand for "[[assault rifle]]".<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Myre |first=Greg |author-link=Greg Myre |date=February 28, 2018 |title=A Brief History Of The AR-15 |url=https://www.npr.org/2018/02/28/588861820/a-brief-history-of-the-ar-15 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230513122636/https://www.npr.org/2018/02/28/588861820/a-brief-history-of-the-ar-15 |archive-date=May 13, 2023 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |work=[[NPR]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Palma |first=Bethania |date=September 9, 2019 |title=Does 'AR' in AR-15 Stand for 'Assault Rifle'? |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/meaning-of-ar-in-ar-15-firearm/ |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[Snopes]]}}</ref></noinclude>
[[File:Coca Cola Flasche - Original Taste.jpg|thumb|upright]]
* The [[Coca-Cola#Contour bottle design|Coca-Cola bottle's contour bottle]] was not designed by famous industrial designer [[Raymond Loewy]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Bayley |first=Stephen |date=February 7, 2015 |title=The art of Coke |url=https://www.spectator.com.au/2015/02/happy-100th-birthday-to-a-pop-icon-the-coca-cola-bottle/ |access-date=June 19, 2024 |work=[[The Spectator]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=Barbara |date=May 2, 1999 |title=Was the Coca-Cola Bottle Design an Accident? |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/coke-bottle-design-accident/ |access-date=June 19, 2024 |website=[[Snopes]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* The common image of [[Santa Claus]] (Father Christmas) as a jolly large man in red garments was not created by [[the Coca-Cola Company]] as an advertising tool. Santa Claus had already taken this form in American popular culture by the late 19th century, long before Coca-Cola used his image in the 1930s.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=David |date=December 18, 2008 |title=Did Coca-Cola Invent the Modern Image of Santa Claus? |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/the-claus-that-refreshes/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://archive.today/20120524200646/http://www.snopes.com/holidays/christmas/santa/cocacola.asp |archive-date=May 24, 2012 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[Snopes]]}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||date=December 18, 2006 |title=Coca-Cola's Santa Claus: Not The Real Thing! |url=http://www.bevnet.com/news/2006/12-18-2006-white_rock_coke_santa_claus.asp |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121026092817/http://www.bevnet.com/news/2006/12-18-2006-white_rock_coke_santa_claus.asp |archive-date=October 26, 2012 |access-date=January 19, 2007 |work=BevNET.com}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Boissoneault |first=Lorraine |date=December 19, 2018 |title=A Civil War Cartoonist Created the Modern Image of Santa Claus as Union Propaganda |url=https://www.smithsonianmag.com/history/civil-war-cartoonist-created-modern-image-santa-claus-union-propaganda-180971074/ |access-date=June 21, 2024 |website=[[Smithsonian (magazine)|Smithsonian]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[Chevrolet Nova]] sold well in Latin American markets; [[General Motors]] did not rename the car. While ''no va'' does mean "doesn't go" in Spanish, ''nova'' was easily understood to mean "new".<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||author=Mikkelson, Barbara and David |date=March 19, 2011 |title=Don't Go Here |url=http://www.snopes.com/business/misxlate/nova.asp |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190614053144/https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/chevrolet-nova-name-spanish/ |archive-date=June 14, 2019 |access-date=October 3, 2015 |website=[[Snopes]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Netflix]] was not founded after its co-founder [[Reed Hastings]] was charged a $40 late fee by [[Blockbuster LLC|Blockbuster]]. Hastings made the story up to summarize Netflix's [[value proposition]]; Netflix's founders were actually inspired by [[Amazon (company)|Amazon]].<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite news||last=Rodriguez |first=Ashley |date=August 29, 2017 |title=Netflix was founded 20 years ago today because Reed Hastings was late returning a video |url=https://qz.com/1062888/netflix-was-founded-20-years-ago-today-because-reed-hastings-was-late-a-returning-video |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230404005112/https://qz.com/1062888/netflix-was-founded-20-years-ago-today-because-reed-hastings-was-late-a-returning-video |archive-date=April 4, 2023 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |work=[[Quartz (publication)|Quartz]]}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Keating |first=Gina |title=Netflixed: The Epic Battle for America's Eyeballs |date=September 24, 2013 |publisher=Portfolio |isbn=978-1-59184-659-8 |pages=3–4 |chapter=Prologue}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Carey |first=Alexis |date=January 18, 2020 |title=True story behind Netflix's rise – and the downfall of Blockbuster |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/entertainment/true-story-behind-netflixs-rise-and-the-downfall-of-blockbuster/HLRQWBNIF7ZFSXHF4L5RZ3JAEQ/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230404005839/https://www.nzherald.co.nz/entertainment/true-story-behind-netflixs-rise-and-the-downfall-of-blockbuster/HLRQWBNIF7ZFSXHF4L5RZ3JAEQ/ |archive-date=April 4, 2023 |access-date=June 28, 2022 |website=[[The New Zealand Herald]]}}
<br />d. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Castillo |first=Michelle |date=May 23, 2017 |title=Reed Hastings' story about the founding of Netflix has changed several times |url=https://www.cnbc.com/2017/05/23/netflix-ceo-reed-hastings-on-how-the-company-was-born.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171102211235/https://www.cnbc.com/2017/05/23/netflix-ceo-reed-hastings-on-how-the-company-was-born.html |archive-date=November 2, 2017 |access-date=July 1, 2022 |website=[[CNBC]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[PepsiCo]] in no real sense ever owned the "6th most powerful navy" in the world after a deal with the Soviet Union. In 1989, Pepsi acquired several decommissioned warships as part of a barter deal.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Lewis |first=Flora |author-link=Flora Lewis |date=May 10, 1989 |title=Foreign Affairs; Soviets Buy American |url=https://www.nytimes.com/1989/05/10/opinion/foreign-affairs-soviets-buy-american.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210105072423/https://www.nytimes.com/1989/05/10/opinion/foreign-affairs-soviets-buy-american.html |archive-date=January 5, 2021 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |work=[[The New York Times]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Musgrave |first=Paul |author-link=Paul Musgrave |date=November 27, 2021 |title=The Doomed Voyage of Pepsi's Soviet Navy |url=https://foreignpolicy.com/2021/11/27/pepsi-navy-soviet-ussr/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230118185742/https://foreignpolicy.com/2021/11/27/pepsi-navy-soviet-ussr/ |archive-date=January 18, 2023 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |work=[[Foreign Policy]]}}</ref></noinclude> The oil tankers were leased out or sold and the other ships sold for scrap.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Clarke |first=Kaiyah |date=May 24, 2022 |title=Fact Check: NO Pepsi Navy – U.S.-Soviet Deal Did NOT Make Pepsi The '6th Most Powerful Military In The World' |url=https://leadstories.com/hoax-alert/2022/05/fact-check-no-pepsi-navy-pepsi-was-not-the-6th-most-powerful-military-in-the-world.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230330115731/https://leadstories.com/hoax-alert/2022/05/fact-check-no-pepsi-navy-pepsi-was-not-the-6th-most-powerful-military-in-the-world.html |archive-date=March 30, 2023 |access-date=June 24, 2022 |website=[[Lead Stories]] |language=en-US}}</ref></noinclude> A follow-on deal involved another 10 ships.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Ewbank |first=Anne |date=January 12, 2018 |title=When the Soviet Union Paid Pepsi in Warships |url=https://www.atlasobscura.com/articles/soviet-union-pepsi-ships |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210207231805/https://www.atlasobscura.com/articles/soviet-union-pepsi-ships |archive-date=February 7, 2021 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[Atlas Obscura]]}}</ref></noinclude>

=== Fine arts ===
[[File:Italy-3090 - Caesar Augustus of Prima Porta (5375512570).jpg|thumb|upright|Classical sculptures were originally painted in colors.]]
* [[Ancient Greek sculpture|Ancient Greek]] and [[Roman sculpture]]s were [[Ancient Greek sculpture#Painting of sculpture|originally painted in colors]]; they appear white today only because the original pigments have deteriorated. Some well-preserved statues still bear traces of their original coloration.<noinclude><ref name="Brinkmann2008">a. {{#invoke:cite book||chapter-url=https://books.google.com/books?id=2gQesgryr8oC&q=ancient+Greek+sculptures+were+actually+brightly+painted|title=The Color of Life: Polychromy in Sculpture from Antiquity to the Present|last=Brinkmann|first=Vinzenz|date=2008|publisher=The J. Paul Getty Museum and the Getty Research Institute|isbn=978-0-89236-918-8|editor1-last=Panzanelli|editor1-first=Roberta|location=Los Angeles|pages=18–39|chapter=The Polychromy of Ancient Greek Sculpture|author-link=Vinzenz Brinkmann|editor2-last=Schmidt|editor2-first=Eike D.|editor3-last=Lapatin|editor3-first=Kenneth}} <br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||last1=Gurewitsch |first1=Matthew |date=July 2008 |title=True Colors: Archaeologist Vinzenz Brinkmann insists his eye-popping reproductions of ancient Greek sculptures are right on target |url=https://www.smithsonianmag.com/arts-culture/true-colors-17888/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200726002059/https://www.smithsonianmag.com/arts-culture/true-colors-17888/ |archive-date=July 26, 2020 |access-date=May 15, 2018 |website=Smithsonian.com |publisher=Smithsonian Institution}} <br />c. {{#invoke:cite news||last1=Prisco |first1=Jacopo |date=November 30, 2017 |title='Gods in Color' returns antiquities to their original, colorful grandeur |url=https://www.cnn.com/style/article/gods-in-color-ancient-world-polychromy/index.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220617005937/https://www.cnn.com/style/article/gods-in-color-ancient-world-polychromy/index.html |archive-date=June 17, 2022 |access-date=May 15, 2018 |work=CNN style}}</ref><ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Talbot |first=Margaret |date=October 22, 2018 |title=The Myth of Whiteness in Classical Sculpture |url=https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2018/10/29/the-myth-of-whiteness-in-classical-sculpture |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230411213143/https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2018/10/29/the-myth-of-whiteness-in-classical-sculpture |archive-date=April 11, 2023 |access-date=May 12, 2020 |magazine=The New Yorker |language=en}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Michelangelo]] was standing instead of lying down while painting the [[Sistine Chapel ceiling|ceiling]] of the [[Sistine Chapel]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Whiddington |first=Richard |date=February 20, 2024 |title=Art Bites: Michelangelo's Poem About How Much It Sucked to Paint the Sistine Chapel |url=https://news.artnet.com/art-world-archives/art-bites-michelangelo-sistine-chapel-poem-2435098 |access-date=June 25, 2024 |work=[[Artnet]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Michelangelo |url=https://www.thesistinechapel.org/michelangelo |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240509010714/https://www.thesistinechapel.org/michelangelo |archive-date=May 9, 2024 |access-date=June 25, 2024 |website=thesistinechapel.org}}</ref></noinclude>

=== Food and cooking ===
[[File:Salade nicoise.jpg|thumb|Seared tuna]]

* [[Searing]] does not seal in moisture in meat; it causes it to lose some moisture. Meat is seared [[Maillard reaction|to brown it]] and to affect its color, flavor, and texture.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||title=Does searing meat really seal in moisture? |url=http://www.cookthink.com/reference/7/Does_searing_meat_really_seal_in_moisture |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131214115343/http://www.cookthink.com/reference/7/Does_searing_meat_really_seal_in_moisture |archive-date=December 14, 2013 |access-date=August 29, 2009 |publisher=Cookthink.com}}

<br />b. {{#invoke:cite book||last=McGee |first=Harold |author-link=Harold McGee |title=On Food and Cooking |title-link=On Food and Cooking |publisher=Scribner |year=2004 |isbn=978-0-684-80001-1 |edition=2nd |page=161}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Braising]] meat does not add moisture; it causes it to lose some moisture. Moisture appears to be added when the gentle cooking breaks down [[connective tissue]] and [[collagen]], which lubricates and tenderizes fibers.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=The Truth About Braising |url=https://www.americastestkitchen.com/cooksillustrated/how_tos/6365-the-truth-about-braising |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221205035202/https://www.americastestkitchen.com/cooksillustrated/how_tos/6365-the-truth-about-braising |archive-date=December 5, 2022 |access-date=June 24, 2024 |website=[[America's Test Kitchen]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Lopez-Alt |first=J Kenji |author-link=J. Kenji López-Alt |url=https://archive.org/details/TFL-BHCTS/page/n1/mode/2up |title=The Food Lab: Better Home Cooking Through Science |publisher=[[W. W. Norton & Company]] |year=2015 |isbn=978-0-393-08108-4 |location=America |chapter=Soups, Stews, and the Science of Stock |access-date=June 24, 2024}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Mussels]] and clams that do not open when cooked can still be fully cooked and safe to eat.<noinclude><ref>{{cite magazine |last=Marino |first=Melissa |date=June 2007 |title=Blue Mussels: An Open and Shut Case |url=https://www.springbayseafoods.com.au/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/Blue-mussels-an-open-and-shut-case.pdf |magazine=FISH |publisher=[[Fisheries Research and Development Corporation]] |access-date=June 19, 2024 |archive-date=June 18, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240618222516/https://www.springbayseafoods.com.au/wp-content/uploads/2017/10/Blue-mussels-an-open-and-shut-case.pdf |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last1=Kruszelnicki |first1=Karl |author-link=Karl Kruszelnicki |date=October 29, 2008 |title=Mussel myth an open and shut case |url=https://www.abc.net.au/science/articles/2008/10/29/2404364.htm |access-date=June 18, 2024 |website=[[Australian Broadcasting Corporation]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Tomky |first=Naomi |date=April 2018 |title=A Guide to Clam Types and What to Do With Them |url=https://www.seriouseats.com/a-guide-to-clam-types-and-what-to-do-with-them |access-date=June 21, 2024 |website=[[Serious Eats]]}}</ref></noinclude>{{Better source needed|date=November 2024}}
* [[Twinkie]]s, an American snack cake generally considered to be "[[junk food]]", have a [[shelf life]] of around 25 days, despite the common claim (usually facetious) that they remain edible for decades.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Sagon |first=Candy |date=April 13, 2005 |title=Twinkies, 75 Years and Counting |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/articles/A46062-2005Apr12.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110628233728/http://www.washingtonpost.com/wp-dyn/articles/A46062-2005Apr12.html |archive-date=June 28, 2011 |access-date=August 30, 2011 |newspaper=The Washington Post}}</ref></noinclude> The official shelf life is 45 days. Twinkies normally remain on a store shelf for 7 to 10 days.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite news||last=Kelley |first=Tina |date=March 23, 2000 |title=Twinkie Strike Afflicts Fans With Snack Famine |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2000/03/23/nyregion/twinkie-strike-afflicts-fans-with-snack-famine.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110904052221/http://www.nytimes.com/2000/03/23/nyregion/twinkie-strike-afflicts-fans-with-snack-famine.html |archive-date=September 4, 2011 |access-date=February 10, 2012 |newspaper=The New York Times}}
b. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Greenfieldboyce |first=Nell |author-link=Nell Greenfieldboyce |date=October 15, 2020 |title=A Disturbing Twinkie That Has, So Far, Defied Science |url=https://www.npr.org/2020/10/15/923411578/a-disturbing-twinkie-that-has-so-far-defied-science |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201023011021/https://www.npr.org/2020/10/15/923411578/a-disturbing-twinkie-that-has-so-far-defied-science |archive-date=October 23, 2020 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[All Things Considered]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* Packaged foods, when properly stored, can safely be eaten past their "expiration" dates in the US. While some US states regulate [[expiration date]]s for some products, generally "use-by" and "best-by" dates are manufacturer suggestions for best quality.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||title=Food Product Dating |url=https://www.fsis.usda.gov/food-safety/safe-food-handling-and-preparation/food-safety-basics/food-product-dating |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201201111750/http://www.fsis.usda.gov/wps/portal/fsis/topics/food-safety-education/get-answers/food-safety-fact-sheets/food-labeling/food-product-dating/food-product-dating |archive-date=December 1, 2020 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[United States Department of Agriculture]]}}
b. {{#invoke:cite news||last=Abrahamian |first=Atossa Araxia |author-link=Atossa Araxia Abrahamian |date=September 19, 2013 |title=Harvard study finds food expiration labels are misleading |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-foodsafety-dates/harvard-study-finds-food-expiration-labels-are-misleading-idUSBRE98H15F20130918 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221213165333/https://www.reuters.com/article/us-usa-foodsafety-dates/harvard-study-finds-food-expiration-labels-are-misleading-idUSBRE98H15F20130918 |archive-date=December 13, 2022 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |work=[[Reuters]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* Storing bread in the refrigerator makes it [[staling|go stale]] faster than leaving it at room temperature.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Tana |first=Sara |date=July 26, 2021 |title=8 Food Storage Mistakes That Are Costing You Money |url=https://www.allrecipes.com/article/food-storage-mistakes/ |access-date=June 24, 2024 |website=[[Allrecipes.com]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Gritzer |first=Daniel |date=February 28, 2023 |title=Does Refrigeration Really Ruin Bread? |url=https://www.seriouseats.com/does-refrigeration-really-ruin-bread |access-date=June 24, 2024 |website=[[Serious Eats]]}}</ref></noinclude> It does, however, slow mold growth.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Olaechea |first=Carlos |date=June 14, 2023 |title=Refrigerating Bread Isn't Always Bad |url=https://www.eatingwell.com/article/8051533/refrigerating-bread-isnt-always-bad/ |access-date=July 6, 2024 |work=EatingWell}}</ref></noinclude>
[[File:Crystallized honey with close-up.jpg|thumb|Crystallized honey]]
* Crystallized [[honey]] is not spoiled. The crystals are formed by [[Crystallization#Cooling crystallization|low temperature crystallization]], a high glucose level, and the presence of pollen. The crystallization can be reversed by gentle heating.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Sertich Velie |first=Marissa |date=August 10, 2018 |title=The Serious Eats Guide to Sugar |url=https://www.seriouseats.com/the-serious-eats-guide-to-sugar-syrup-honey-natural-sweetners |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240527130509/https://www.seriouseats.com/the-serious-eats-guide-to-sugar-syrup-honey-natural-sweetners |archive-date=May 27, 2024 |access-date=June 24, 2024 |website=[[Serious Eats]]}}</ref><ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Pearson |first=Gwen |author-link=Gwen Pearson |date=March 7, 2014 |title=What Do You Do With Crystallized Honey? |url=https://www.wired.com/2014/03/crystalized-honey/ |access-date=June 24, 2024 |magazine=[[Wired (magazine)|Wired]] |archive-date=June 14, 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230614101914/https://www.wired.com/2014/03/crystalized-honey/ |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude>
* Seeds are not the spiciest part of [[chili pepper]]s. In fact, seeds contain a low amount of [[capsaicin]], one of several compounds which induce the [[Pungency|hot sensation (pungency)]] in mammals. The highest concentration of capsaicin is located in the [[Placentation#In plants|placental tissue]] (the [[pith]]) to which the seeds are attached.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=New Mexico State University – College of Agriculture and Home Economics (2005) |url=http://spectre.nmsu.edu/dept/academic.html?i=1274&s=sub |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070504035555/http://spectre.nmsu.edu/dept/academic.html?i=1274&s=sub |archive-date=May 4, 2007}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Tandon |first1=G L |last2=Dravid |first2=S V |last3=Siddappa |first3=G S |date=January 1964 |title=Oleoresin of Capsicum (Red Chilies)—Some Technological and Chemical Aspects |journal=[[Journal of Food Science]] |volume=29 |issue=1 |page=2 |doi=10.1111/j.1365-2621.1964.tb01683.x | issn=0022-1147 }}</ref></noinclude>
* Turkey meat is not particularly high in [[tryptophan]], and does [[postprandial somnolence#Turkey and tryptophan|not cause more drowsiness]] than other foods. Drowsiness after large meals such as Christmas or Thanksgiving dinner generally comes from overeating.<noinclude><ref name="Vreeman 2007">{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Vreeman |first1=Rachel C |last2=Carroll |first2=Aaron E |author-link2=Aaron Carroll |date=20 December 2007 |title=Medical myths |journal=[[The BMJ]] |volume=335 |issue=7633 |pages=1288–9 |doi=10.1136/bmj.39420.420370.25|pmid=18156231 |pmc=2151163 }}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Coffee roasting|Darker roasts]] of coffee do not always contain more [[caffeine]] than lighter roasts. When coffee is roasted, it expands and loses water. When the resultant coffee is [[Coffee preparation|ground and measured volumetrically]], the denser lighter roasts have more coffee per cup, meaning they contain more caffeine.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Caffeine Content of Coffee: Dark Roast vs. Light Roast |url=https://www.americastestkitchen.com/cooksillustrated/how_tos/8237-caffeine-content-of-coffee-dark-roast-vs-light-roast |access-date=June 24, 2024 |website=[[America's Test Kitchen]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Lipka |first=Mitch |date=March 27, 2014 |title=Your money: Getting the biggest caffeine buzz for your buck |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/markets/wealth/your-money-getting-the-biggest-caffeine-buzz-for-your-buck-idUSBREA2P197/ |access-date=June 24, 2024 |work=[[Reuters]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Bourbon whiskey]] does not have to be distilled in Kentucky.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Kiniry |first=Laura |date=June 13, 2013 |title=Where Bourbon Really Got Its Name and More Tips on America's Native Spirit |url=https://www.smithsonianmag.com/arts-culture/where-bourbon-really-got-its-name-and-more-tips-on-americas-native-spirit-145879/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240224041500/https://www.smithsonianmag.com/arts-culture/where-bourbon-really-got-its-name-and-more-tips-on-americas-native-spirit-145879/ |archive-date=February 24, 2024 |access-date=June 24, 2024 |work=[[Smithsonian (magazine)|Smithsonian]]}}</ref></noinclude> Bourbon is also distilled in states such as New York, California, Wyoming and Washington, as the legal requirement is only that it be made in the [[United States|US]]. However, Kentucky does produce the majority of bourbon.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Minnick |first=Fred |author-link=Fred Minnick |date=October 23, 2015 |title=Is Kentucky the Home of Bourbon? |url=https://whiskymag.com/articles/is-kentucky-the-home-of-bourbon/ |access-date=June 24, 2024 |work=Whisky Magazine |issue=131}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Carroll |first=James R |date=May 9, 2024 |title=Congress resolution marks bourbon's unique status |url=https://www.courier-journal.com/story/politics-blog/2014/05/09/bourbon-recognized-as-distinct-us-product-50-years-ago/8911567/ |access-date=June 24, 2024 |work=[[Courier Journal]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* Using mild soap on [[Seasoning (cookware)|well-seasoned]] [[cast-iron cookware]] will not damage the seasoning.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Sullivan |first=Michael |date=September 12, 2023 |title=How to Clean and Season Cast-Iron Cookware |url=https://www.nytimes.com/wirecutter/guides/how-to-clean-cast-iron-skillet/ |access-date=June 24, 2024 |website=[[Wirecutter (website)|Wirecutter]]}}</ref></noinclude> This is not because modern soaps are gentler than older soaps.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=McManus |first=Lisa |date=February 15, 2022 |title=Is It OK to Use Soap on Cast Iron? |url=https://www.americastestkitchen.com/articles/5037-is-it-ok-to-use-soap-on-cast-iron |access-date=June 24, 2024 |website=[[America's Test Kitchen]]}}</ref></noinclude>

[[File:8hosomak8.jpg|thumb|Kappa-maki contains cucumber and no seafood]]

* [[Sushi]] does not mean raw seafood; some sushi, such as [[kappamaki]], contains no seafood. The word refers to the vinegar-prepared rice the dish contains.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last1=Mikkelson |first1=Barbara |title=Sushi Definition |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/if-you-knew-sushi/ |access-date=June 19, 2024 |website=[[Snopes]]|date=October 5, 2002 }}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Allspice]] is not a mix of spices.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Francis |first=Ali |date=December 1, 2021 |title=Allspice Is the Berry—Yes, Berry—That Can Do It All |url=https://www.bonappetit.com/story/what-is-allspice |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240408202233/https://www.bonappetit.com/story/what-is-allspice |archive-date=April 8, 2024 |access-date=June 24, 2024 |website=[[Bon Appetit]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Mincey |first=Rai |date=February 24, 2021 |title=What is Allspice? |url=https://www.allrecipes.com/article/what-is-allspice/ |access-date=June 24, 2024 |website=[[Allrecipes.com]]}}</ref></noinclude> It is a single spice, so called because it seems to combine the flavours and scents of many spices, especially [[cinnamon]], [[nutmeg]], [[clove]]s and [[black pepper]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Allspice: Etymology |url=https://www.oed.com/dictionary/allspice_n?tab=etymology |access-date=June 24, 2024 |website=[[Oxford English Dictionary]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Monosodium glutamate]] has not been found to cause [[headaches]] and other feelings of discomfort, known as "[[Chinese restaurant syndrome]]" in placebo-controlled trials.<noinclude><ref name="FDAQnA">{{#invoke:cite web||title=Questions and Answers on Monosodium glutamate (MSG) |url=https://www.fda.gov/food/ingredientspackaginglabeling/foodadditivesingredients/ucm328728.htm |publisher=U.S. Food and Drug Administration |date=19 November 2012 |access-date =4 February 2014}}</ref><ref name="Ob2016">{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Obayashi|first1=Y|last2=Nagamura|first2=Y|title=Does monosodium glutamate really cause headache?: a systematic review of human studies|journal=[[The Journal of Headache and Pain]]|date=17 May 2016|volume=17|page=54|doi=10.1186/s10194-016-0639-4|pmid=27189588|pmc=4870486|issue=1|doi-access=free}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite AV media||url=http://www.businessinsider.com/msg-ingredients-side-effects-2014-6|first=Will|last=Wei|date=16 June 2014|title=The Truth Behind Notorious Flavor Enhancer MSG|work=Business Insider|type=Podcast|access-date=13 November 2017}}</ref><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite journal||last=Zanfirescu|first=A.|date=May 2019|title=A Review of the Alleged Health Hazards of Monosodium Glutamate|journal=Comprehensive Reviews in Food Science and Food Safety|volume=18|issue=4|pages=1111–34|doi=10.1111/1541-4337.12448|pmid=31920467|pmc=6952072 }}{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Tarasoff|first=L.|date=December 1993|title=Monosodium L-glutamate: A double-blind study and review|journal=Food and Chemical Toxicology|volume=31|issue=12|pages=1019–35|doi=10.1016/0278-6915(93)90012-N|pmid=8282275}}<br />b. {{#invoke:cite journal||last=Freeman |first=M. |date=October 2006 |title=Reconsidering the effects of monosodium glutamate: A literature review |journal=Journal of the American Academy of Nurse Practitioners |volume=18 |issue=10 |pages=482–86 |doi=10.1111/j.1745-7599.2006.00160.x |pmid=16999713 |s2cid=21084909 }}{{#invoke:cite news||title=Is MSG (Monosodium Glutamate) bad for your health?|url=https://examine.com/nutrition/is-msg-bad-for-your-health/|newspaper=Examine.com|date=February 23, 2022}}</ref></noinclude>  Although there are reports of MSG sensitivity among a subset of the population, this has not been demonstrated in trials.<noinclude><ref name = "freeman">{{#invoke:cite journal|| author = Freeman, Matthew | s2cid = 21084909| title = Reconsidering the effects of monosodium glutamate: A literature review| journal = Journal of the American Academy of Nurse Practitioners| volume = 18| pages = 482–86| year = 2006| doi = 10.1111/j.1745-7599.2006.00160.x| pmid=16999713| issue = 10}}</ref></noinclude>

==== Food and drink history ====
* [[Steak tartare]] was not invented by Mongol warriors who tenderized horse meat under their saddles.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Smith |first=Craig S |author-link=Craig S. Smith |date=April 6, 2005 |title=The Raw Truth: Don't Blame the Mongols (or Their Horses) |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2005/04/06/dining/the-raw-truth-dont-blame-the-mongols-or-their-horses.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220426025745/https://www.nytimes.com/2005/04/06/dining/the-raw-truth-dont-blame-the-mongols-or-their-horses.html |archive-date=April 26, 2022 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |work=[[The New York Times]]}}</ref></noinclude> It is likely named after the French [[tartar sauce]], evolving from an early 20th century French dish where the sauce was served with steaks.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Jack |first=Albert |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=uCzTNVCS45AC&pg=PT141 |title=What Caesar Did for My Salad: The Curious Stories Behind Our Favorite Foods |date=2011-09-06 |publisher=Penguin |isbn=978-1-101-55114-1 |page=143 |language=}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Marco Polo]] did not introduce [[pasta]] to Italy from China.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Dickie |first=John |author-link=John Dickie (historian) |title=Delizia!: The Epic History of the Italians and Their Food |publisher=[[Free Press (publisher)|Free Press]] |year=2008 |isbn=978-0-7432-7799-0 |location=New York |page=48}}</ref></noinclude> The misconception originated as promotional material in the ''Macaroni Journal'', a newsletter published by an association of American pasta makers.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last1=Serventi |first1=Silvano |title=Pasta: The Story of a Universal Food |last2=Sabban |first2=Françoise |date=2002 |publisher=[[Columbia University Press]] |isbn=0-231-12442-2 |location=New York |page=10 |translator-last=Shugaar |translator-first=Antony |trans-title=La Pasta: Storia e cultura di un cibo universale}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Spice]]s were not used in the Middle Ages to mask the flavor of rotten meat before refrigeration. Spices were an expensive luxury item; those who could afford them could afford good meat, and there are no contemporaneous documents calling for spices to disguise the taste of bad meat.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Freedman |first=Paul |author-link=Paul Freedman |title=Writing Food History: A Global Perspective |publisher=[[Berg Publishers]] |year=2012 |isbn=978-1-84788-809-9 |editor-last=Claflin |editor-first=Kyri |location=London |page=24 |editor-last2=Scholliers |editor-first2=Peter}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Dalby |first=Andrew |author-link=Andrew Dalby |url=https://archive.org/details/dangeroustastess0000dalb |title=Dangerous Tastes: The Story of Spices |publisher=[[University of California Press]] |year=2000 |isbn=978-0-520-23674-5 |page=156}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Jotischky |first=Andrew |title=A Hermit's Cookbook: Monks, Food and Fasting in the Middle Ages |publisher=Bloomsbury |year=2011 |isbn=978-1-4411-5991-5 |page=170}}
<br />d. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Krondl |first=Michael |title=The Taste of Conquest: The Rise and Fall of the Three Great Cities of Spice |publisher=Ballantine Books |year=2007 |isbn=978-0-345-48083-5 |page=6}}</ref></noinclude><!-- See [[Spice#Function]] -->
* [[Catherine de' Medici#Culinary legend|Catherine de' Medici's cooks]] did not introduce Italian foods and techniques to the French royal court, laying the foundations for the development of French [[haute cuisine]].<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Ketcham Wheaton |first=Barbara |author-link=Barbara Ketcham Wheaton |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=OTzZT_3DQTcC |title=Savoring the Past: The French Kitchen and Table from 1300 to 1789 |publisher=[[Atria Publishing Group]] |year=2011 |isbn=978-1-4391-4373-5 |pages=43–51 |access-date=July 7, 2024}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Mennell |first=Stephen |author-link=Stephen Mennell |url=https://archive.org/details/allmannersoffood0000menn |title=All Manners of Food: Eating and Taste in England and France from the Middle Ages to the Present |publisher=[[University of Illinois Press]] |year=1996 |isbn=978-0-252-06490-6 |edition=2nd |pages=65–66, 69–71 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |url-access=registration}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Campanini |first=Antonella |url=https://thenewgastronome.com/caterina-de-medici-a-gastronomic-myth/ |title=The New Gastronome: The Illusive Story Of Catherine de' Medici: A Gastronomic Myth |date=December 18, 2018 |access-date=September 19, 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201229142651/https://thenewgastronome.com/caterina-de-medici-a-gastronomic-myth/ |archive-date=December 29, 2020 |url-status=live}} Summarizing {{#invoke:cite book||last1=Campanini |first1=Antonella |title=La Table de la Renaissance: Le mythe italien |last2=Bienassis |first2=Loïc |publisher=Presses universitaires de Rennes |year=2018 |isbn=978-2-7535-7406-9 |editor1-last=Quellier |editor1-first=Florent |chapter=La reine à la fourchette et autres histoires. Ce que la table française emprunta à l'Italie: analyse critique d'un mythe |editor2-last=Briost |editor2-first=Pascal}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Whipped_cream#Crème_Chantilly|Whipped cream]] was not invented by [[François Vatel]] in 1661 and later named at the [[Château de Chantilly]] where it was notably served; similar recipes are attested at least a century earlier in France and England.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=July 15, 2021 |title=Histoire – La chantilly, un dessert de légende |url=https://www.rtbf.be/article/histoire-la-chantilly-un-dessert-de-legende-10648168 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240103030348/https://www.rtbf.be/article/histoire-la-chantilly-un-dessert-de-legende-10648168 |archive-date=January 3, 2024 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[RTBF]] |language=fr}}</ref><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Tebben |first=Maryann Bates |url=https://archive.org/details/saucesglobalhist0000tebb |title=Sauces: A Global History |publisher=[[Reaktion Books]] |year=2014 |isbn=978-1-78023-413-7 |location=London |pages=99–100 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |url-access=registration}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||title=Histoire de la Crème Chantilly |url=http://www.domainedechantilly.com/domaine-de-chantilly/cr%C3%A8me-chantilly/histoire-de-la-cr%C3%A8me-chantilly |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130416042751/http://www.domainedechantilly.com/domaine-de-chantilly/cr%C3%A8me-chantilly/histoire-de-la-cr%C3%A8me-chantilly |archive-date=April 16, 2013 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[Château de Chantilly]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Dom Pérignon (monk)|Dom Pérignon]] did not invent [[champagne]]. Wine naturally starts to bubble after being pressed, and bubbles at the time were considered a flaw which Pérignon worked unsuccessfully to eliminate.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Foreman |first=Amanda |date=December 9, 2021 |title=The Many Inventors of Champagne |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/the-many-inventors-of-champagne-11639083414 |access-date=June 26, 2024 |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last1=Kladstrup |first1=Don |title=Champagne: How the World's Most Glamorous Wine Triumphed Over War and Hard Times |last2=Kladstrup |first2=Petie |publisher=[[William Morrow and Company]] |year=2005 |isbn=978-0-06-073792-4 |location=New York |chapter=Chapter 1: The Monarch and the Monk}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Potato_chip#History|Potato chips]] were not invented by a frustrated [[George Speck]] in response to a customer, sometimes given as [[Cornelius Vanderbilt]], complaining that his French fries were too thick and not salty enough.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=Barbara |date=November 10, 2000 |title=Potato Chip Origin |url=https://www.snopes.com//fact-check/potato-chips/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220121063450/https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/potato-chips/ |archive-date=January 21, 2022 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[Snopes]] |language=}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Fox |first1=William S. |last2=Banner |first2=Mae G. |date=April 1983 |title=Social and Economic Contexts of Folklore Variants: The Case of Potato Chip Legends |journal=Western Folklore |volume=42 |issue=2 |pages=114–126 |doi=10.2307/1499968 |jstor=1499968}}</ref></noinclude> Recipes for potato chips were published as early as 1817.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=McElwain |first=Aoife |date=June 17, 2019 |title=Did Tayto really invent cheese and onion crisps? |url=https://www.irishtimes.com/life-and-style/food-and-drink/did-tayto-really-invent-cheese-and-onion-crisps-1.3915726 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190617083013/https://www.irishtimes.com/life-and-style/food-and-drink/did-tayto-really-invent-cheese-and-onion-crisps-1.3915726 |archive-date=June 17, 2019 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |newspaper=[[The Irish Times]] |language=}}</ref></noinclude> The misconception was popularized by a 1973 advertising campaign by the St. Regis Paper Company.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Burhans |first=Dirk E |title=Crunch!: A History of the Great American Potato Chip |publisher=[[University of Wisconsin Press]] |year=2008 |isbn=978-0-299-22770-8 |location= |pages=17–20 |chapter=Creation Myths}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[George Washington Carver]] was not the inventor of [[Peanut_butter#History|peanut butter]].<noinclude><ref name="Krampner 2013">{{#invoke:cite book||last=Krampner |first=Jon |author-link=Jon Krampner |title=Creamy and Crunchy: An Informal History of Peanut Butter, the All-American Food |publisher=[[Columbia University Press]] |year=2013 |isbn=978-0-231-16233-3 |page=42}}</ref></noinclude> The first peanut butter related patent was filed by [[John Harvey Kellogg]] in 1895, and peanut butter was used by the [[Inca]]s centuries prior to that.<noinclude><ref name="NPB">{{#invoke:cite web||title=Who Invented Peanut Butter? |url=http://nationalpeanutboard.org/peanut-info/who-invented-peanut-butter.htm |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161125044806/http://nationalpeanutboard.org/peanut-info/who-invented-peanut-butter.htm |archive-date=November 25, 2016 |access-date=June 24, 2022 |website=[[National Peanut Board]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Wheeling |first=Kate |date=January 2021 |title=A Brief History of Peanut Butter |url=https://www.smithsonianmag.com/innovation/brief-history-peanut-butter-180976525/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220618202032/https://www.smithsonianmag.com/innovation/brief-history-peanut-butter-180976525/ |archive-date=June 18, 2022 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[Smithsonian (magazine)|Smithsonian]] |language=}}</ref></noinclude> Carver did compile hundreds of uses for peanuts, in addition to uses for pecans, and sweet potatoes.<noinclude><ref name="NPB" /><noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Cannon |first=William |date=February 6, 2017 |title=A True Renaissance Man |url=https://www.americanscientist.org/article/a-true-renaissance-man |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230403223244/https://www.americanscientist.org/article/a-true-renaissance-man |archive-date=April 3, 2023 |access-date=June 24, 2022 |website=[[American Scientist]]}}</ref></noinclude> An opinion piece by [[William F. Buckley Jr.]] may have been the source of the misconception.<noinclude><ref name="Krampner 2013" /></noinclude>

[[File:fortune cookie broken 20040628 223252 1.jpg|thumb|[[Fortune cookie]]s are rarely found in China]]

* [[Fortune cookie]]s are not found in [[Chinese cuisine]], despite their presence in [[American Chinese cuisine|Chinese restaurants in the United States]] and other Western countries. They originated in Japan and were introduced to the US by the Japanese.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Lee |first=((Jennifer 8)) |author-link=Jennifer 8. Lee |date=January 16, 2008 |title=Solving a Riddle Wrapped in a Mystery Inside a Cookie |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2008/01/16/dining/16fort.html |url-access=subscription |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120418163729/http://www.nytimes.com/2008/01/16/dining/16fort.html |archive-date=April 18, 2012 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |work=[[The New York Times]] |language=}}</ref></noinclude> In China, they are considered American, and are rare.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=Barbara |date=May 21, 2008 |title=Origin of Fortune Cookies |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/inscrutable-cookie/ |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[Snopes]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Julius Caesar]] did not invent [[Caesar_salad#History|Caesar salad]]. Its creator was [[Caesar Cardini]], an Italian-American restaurateur, in [[Tijuana|Tijuana, Mexico]], in 1924.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Birrell |first=Nicki |date=July 4, 2024 |title=Caesar Centenary: What's the story behind the famous salad? |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/lifestyle/caesar-centenary-whats-the-story-behind-the-famous-salad/B4A3ERCRQBHGRG2TGZVBFQIYVY/ |access-date=July 10, 2024 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last1=O'Conner |first1=Patricia T |author-link=Patricia T. O'Conner |title=Origins of the Specious: Myths and Misconceptions of the English Language |last2=Kellerman |first2=Stewart |author-link2=Stewart Kellerman |publisher=[[Random House]] |year=2009 |isbn=978-1-4000-6660-5 |location=New York |page=75}}{{sfn whitelist|CITEREFO'ConnerKellerman2009}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Hydrox]] is not a knock-off of [[Oreos]]. Hydrox, invented in 1908, predates Oreos by four years and was initially more popular than Oreos. The name "Hydrox" being said to sound like a laundry detergent contributed to its market decline.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=LeClair |first=Catherine |date=August 5, 2020 |title=How the Oreo cookie went from unknown knock-off to the world's most popular cookie, as a result of a sibling rivalry between baker brothers |url=https://www.businessinsider.com/how-the-oreo-went-from-knock-off-to-worlds-favorite-2020-8 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220706050254/https://www.businessinsider.com/how-the-oreo-went-from-knock-off-to-worlds-favorite-2020-8 |archive-date=July 6, 2022 |access-date=July 6, 2022 |website=Business Insider}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Rhoades |first=Christopher |date=January 19, 2008 |title=The Hydrox Cookie Is Dead, and Fans Won't Get Over It |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/SB120069573721101481 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150312205018/https://www.wsj.com/articles/SB120069573721101481 |archive-date=March 12, 2015 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* The difference between the taste of "banana-flavored" candy and a real banana is not due to the former being specifically designed to replicate the taste of [[Gros Michel banana]]s, the [[cultivar]] that dominated the American banana market before the rise of [[Cavendish banana]]s. All banana cultivars derive their flavor from a complex mix of many compounds, while a single compound, [[isoamyl acetate]], gives banana candy its flavor. Isoamyl acetate naturally occurs in bananas as well as many other fruits and fermented beverages.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||author1=Technical Resources International, Inc |date=November 1994 |title=Summary of Data For Chemical Selection: Isoamyl Acetate |url=https://ntp.niehs.nih.gov/ntp/htdocs/chem_background/exsumpdf/isoamylacetate_508.pdf |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230522181820/https://ntp.niehs.nih.gov/ntp/htdocs/chem_background/exsumpdf/isoamylacetate_508.pdf |archive-date=May 22, 2023 |access-date=2 April 2023 |website=[[National Toxicology Program]] |publisher=[[United States Department of Health and Human Services]]}}</ref></noinclude> It is more concentrated in Gros Michel bananas than in Cavendish bananas, but its use in candy production was due to its simple production, not any specific resemblance to a banana's flavor.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Baraniuk |first=Chris |title=The secrets of fake flavours |url=https://www.bbc.com/future/article/20140829-the-secrets-of-fake-flavours |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240321175603/https://www.bbc.com/future/article/20140829-the-secrets-of-fake-flavours |archive-date=March 21, 2024 |access-date=2022-07-30 |website=BBC |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Mayer |first=Johanna |date=September 27, 2017 |title=Why Don't Banana Candies Taste Like Real Bananas? |url=https://www.sciencefriday.com/articles/why-dont-banana-candies-taste-like-real-bananas/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240204090031/https://www.sciencefriday.com/articles/why-dont-banana-candies-taste-like-real-bananas/ |archive-date=February 4, 2024 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[Science Friday]]}}</ref></noinclude>

==== Microwave ovens ====

[[File:Weibolu.jpg|thumb|alt=A microwave oven, c. 2005]]

* [[Microwave oven]]s are not tuned to any specific [[Resonance|resonant frequency]] for [[Properties of water|water molecules]] in the food.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last1=Soltysiak |first1=Michal |title=2011 IEEE MTT-S International Microwave Symposium |last2=Celuch |first2=Malgorzata |last3=Erle |first3=Ulrich |date=June 2011 |isbn=978-1-61284-754-2 |pages=1–4 |chapter=Measured and simulated frequency spectra of the household microwave oven |doi=10.1109/MWSYM.2011.5972844}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||author=Bloomfield |first=Louis |author-link=Lou Bloomfield |title=Question 1456 |url=http://www.howeverythingworks.org/page1.php?QNum=1456 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131017005928/http://www.howeverythingworks.org/page1.php?QNum=1456 |archive-date=October 17, 2013 |access-date=February 9, 2012 |publisher=How Everything Works}}</ref></noinclude> They cook food via [[dielectric heating]] of polar molecules, notably water and fats.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Baird |first=Christopher S. |date=15 October 2014 |title=Why are the microwaves in a microwave oven tuned to water |url=http://wtamu.edu/~cbaird/sq/2014/10/15/why-are-the-microwaves-in-a-microwave-oven-tuned-to-water/ |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=Science Questions with Surprising Answers |publisher=[[West Texas A&M University]] |place=Canyon, TX}}</ref></noinclude>
* Microwave ovens do not cook food from the inside out. 2.45&nbsp;GHz microwaves can only penetrate approximately {{convert|1-1.5|in|cm|sp=us|abbr=off}} into most foods. The inside portions of thicker foods are mainly heated by heat conducted from the outer layers.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Microwave Technology Penetration Depths |url=http://www.pueschner.com/en/microwave-technology/penetration-depths |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230304055814/https://www.pueschner.com/en/microwave-technology/penetration-depths |archive-date=March 4, 2023 |access-date=June 1, 2018 |website=pueschner.com |publisher=Püschner GMBH + CO KG MicrowavePowerSystems |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Cooking with Microwave Ovens |url=https://www.fsis.usda.gov/food-safety/safe-food-handling-and-preparation/food-safety-basics/cooking-microwave-ovens#3 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=Food Safety and Inspection Service |publisher=[[U.S. Department of Agriculture]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last1= |first1= |date=December 12, 2017 |title=Resources for You (Radiation-Emitting Products): Microwave Oven Radiation |url=https://www.fda.gov/Radiation-EmittingProducts/ResourcesforYouRadiationEmittingProducts/ucm252762.htm |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141124165841/http://www.fda.gov/Radiation-EmittingProducts/ResourcesforYouRadiationEmittingProducts/ucm252762.htm |archive-date=November 24, 2014 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[Food and Drug Administration]] |publisher=[[FDA Center for Devices and Radiological Health]] |language=}}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[radiation]] produced by a microwave oven is non-ionizing, similar to visible light or radio waves. It therefore does not have the cancer risks associated with [[ionizing radiation]] such as [[X-ray]]s and [[radioactive decay|high-energy particles]], nor does it render the food radioactive. All microwave radiation dissipates as heat. Long-term [[animal testing on rodents|rodent studies]] to assess cancer risk have so far failed to identify any [[carcinogen]]icity from <span class="nowrap">2.45&nbsp;GHz</span> microwave radiation even with chronic exposure levels (i.e. large fraction of life span) far larger than humans are likely to encounter from any leaking ovens. The risk of injury from direct exposure to microwaves is not cumulative, but instead the result of a high-intensity exposure resulting in tissue burns, in much the same way that a high-intensity laser can burn.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal|| doi= 10.2307/3579874 | last1= Frei | first1= MR | last2= Jauchem | first2= JR | last3= Dusch | first3= SJ | last4= Merritt | first4= JH | last5= Berger | first5= RE | last6= Stedham | first6= MA | title= Chronic, low-level (1.0 W/kg) exposure of mice prone to mammary cancer to 2450 MHz microwaves | journal= Radiation Research | volume= 150 | issue= 5 | pages= 568–76 | year= 1998 | pmid= 9806599 | jstor= 3579874 | bibcode= 1998RadR..150..568F }}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal|| last1= Frei | first1= MR | last2= Berger | first2= RE | last3= Dusch | first3= SJ | last4= Guel | first4= V | last5= Jauchem | first5= JR | last6= Merritt | first6= JH | last7= Stedham | first7= MA | title= Chronic exposure of cancer-prone mice to low-level 2450 MHz radiofrequency radiation | journal= Bioelectromagnetics | volume= 19 | issue= 1 | pages= 20–31 | year= 1998 | pmid= 9453703 | doi= 10.1002/(SICI)1521-186X(1998)19:1<20::AID-BEM2>3.0.CO;2-6 }}</ref></noinclude>
* Microwaving food does not significantly reduce its [[Nutrition|nutritive value]] more than other ways of heating and may preserve it better than other cooking processes due to shorter cooking times.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Komaroff |first=Anthony L |author-link=Anthony L. Komaroff |date=June 12, 2015 |title=Ask the doctor: Microwave's impact on food |url=https://www.health.harvard.edu/staying-healthy/ask-the-doctor-microwaves-impact-on-food |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230414011052/https://www.health.harvard.edu/staying-healthy/ask-the-doctor-microwaves-impact-on-food |archive-date=April 14, 2023 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=Harvard Health Publishing |publisher=[[Harvard University]]}}</ref></noinclude>

=== Film and television ===

[[File:Humphrey Bogart in Casablanca trailer.jpg|thumb|Humphrey Bogart in Casablanca]]

* [[Ronald Reagan]] was never seriously considered for the role of Rick Blaine in the 1942 film ''[[Casablanca (film)|Casablanca]]'', eventually played by [[Humphrey Bogart]]. An early studio press release mentioned Reagan, but the studio already knew that Reagan was unavailable because of his upcoming military service.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Harmetz |first=Aljean |author-link=Aljean Harmetz |url=https://archive.org/details/roundupusualsusp00harm |title=Round Up the Usual Suspects: The Making of ''Casablanca'' – Bogart, Bergman, and World War II |date=1992 |publisher=Hyperion |isbn=978-1-56282-761-8 |page=[https://archive.org/details/roundupusualsusp00harm/page/72 72] |url-access=registration}}</ref></noinclude> Indeed, the producer had always wanted Bogart for the part.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Sklar |first=Robert |author-link=Robert Sklar |url=https://archive.org/details/cityboyscagneybo0000skla |title=City Boys: Cagney, Bogart, Garfield |publisher=[[Princeton University Press]] |year=1992 |isbn=978-0-691-04795-9 |location=New Jersey |page=[https://archive.org/details/cityboyscagneybo0000skla/page/135 135]}}

<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=Barbara and David P. |date=August 17, 2007 |title=The Blaine Truth |url=http://www.snopes.com/movies/films/reagan.asp |access-date=March 25, 2012 |website=[[Snopes]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Walt Disney Animation Studios|Walt Disney Studios]]' ''[[Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs (1937 film)|Snow White and the Seven Dwarfs]]'' was not the first animated film to be feature-length. ''[[El Apóstol]]'', a [[Lost film|lost]] 1917 [[Cinema of Argentina|Argentine]] silent film that used [[cutout animation]], is considered the first.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Maher |first=John |date=October 8, 2020 |title=10 Tragically, Irretrievably Lost Pieces of Animation History |url=https://www.vulture.com/article/lost-animation-works-history.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220622053517/https://www.vulture.com/article/lost-animation-works-history.html |archive-date=June 22, 2022 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[Vulture (website)|Vulture]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Sisterson |first=Dennis |date=March 28, 2017 |title=Magic Wilderness: El Apóstol & Peludópolis |url=https://www.skwigly.co.uk/magic-wilderness-el-apostol/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211203212625/https://www.skwigly.co.uk/magic-wilderness-el-apostol/ |archive-date=December 3, 2021 |access-date=June 22, 2022 |website=[[Skwigly (magazine)|Skwigly]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Bendazzi |first=Giannalberto |author-link=Giannalberto Bendazzi |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=Pjk9DwAAQBAJ |title=Twice the First: Quirino Cristiani and the Animated Feature Film |publisher=CRC Press |year=2017 |isbn=978-1-351-37179-7 |page=36 |chapter=The First Feature Length Animated Film in History |quote=On the other hand, the movie was not ''widely'' successful, and appealed to a small portion of the population. It was strictly for a Buenos Aires audience: nobody in the provinces even saw it because it was not distributed there. And likewise, given the subject, it was not possible to export the film to other nations, not even to a close cousin similar to Uruguay. |access-date=March 19, 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230403231830/https://books.google.com/books?id=Pjk9DwAAQBAJ |archive-date=April 3, 2023 |url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude> The misconception comes from ''Snow White'' ''and the Seven Dwarves'' being the first feature-length film to be animated on [[Cel|cels.]]<noinclude><ref>{{Cite web |title=Snow White colored animation celluloid |url=https://americanhistory.si.edu/collections/nmah_1821662 |access-date=September 23, 2023 |website=National Museum of American History}}</ref></noinclude>
* The 1939 film ''[[The Wizard of Oz (1939 film)|The Wizard of Oz]]'' was not the first film in [[Color motion picture film|color]]. [[Kinemacolor]] was used starting in 1902, and the first [[Technicolor]] process debuted in 1917.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Higgins |first=Scott |date=2000 |title=Demonstrating Three-Colour Technicolor: "Early Three-Colour Aesthetics and Design" |journal=Film History |volume=12 |issue=4 |pages=358–383 |doi=10.2979/FIL.2000.12.3.358 |doi-broken-date=November 1, 2024 |issn=0892-2160 |jstor=3815345}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=February 28, 2022 |title=First Color Movie – Everything You Need to Know |url=https://www.nfi.edu/first-color-movie/ |access-date=June 18, 2024 |publisher=Nashville Film Institute}}</ref></noinclude>

=== Language ===
{{See also|List of common misconceptions about language learning}}

[[File:Chinese word for crisis.svg |thumb|right|[[Chinese word for "crisis"]] ]]
* The [[Chinese word for "crisis"]] ({{lang|zh|危机}}) is not composed of the symbols for "danger" and "opportunity"; the first does represent danger, but the second instead means "[[inflection point]]" (the original meaning of the word "crisis").<noinclude><ref name="Zimmer 2007">{{#invoke:cite web||last=Zimmer |first=Benjamin |author-link=Benjamin Zimmer |date=March 27, 2007 |title=Crisis = danger + opportunity: The plot thickens |url=http://itre.cis.upenn.edu/~myl/languagelog/archives/004343.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210126033612/http://itre.cis.upenn.edu/~myl/languagelog/archives/004343.html |archive-date=January 26, 2021 |access-date=January 19, 2009 |work=[[Language Log]]}}</ref><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Adams |first=Cecil |author-link=Cecil Adams |date=November 3, 2000 |title=Is the Chinese word for "crisis" a combination of "danger" and "opportunity"? |url=https://www.straightdope.com/21343499/is-the-chinese-word-for-crisis-a-combination-of-danger-and-opportunity |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160122133148/http://www.straightdope.com/columns/read/2363/is-the-chinese-word-for-crisis-a-combination-of-danger-and-opportunity |archive-date=January 22, 2016 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[The Straight Dope]]}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Mair |first=Victor H. |author-link=Victor H. Mair |year= |title=danger + opportunity ≠ crisis: How a misunderstanding about Chinese characters has led many astray |url=http://pinyin.info/chinese/crisis.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210202015118/http://www.pinyin.info/chinese/crisis.html |archive-date=February 2, 2021 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=pinyin.info}}</ref></noinclude> The misconception was popularized mainly by campaign speeches by [[John F. Kennedy]].<noinclude><ref name="Zimmer 2007" /></noinclude>
* The [[Phonological history of Spanish coronal fricatives|pronunciation of coronal fricatives in Spanish]] did not arise through imitation of a [[lisping]] king. Only one Spanish king, [[Peter of Castile]], is documented as having a lisp, and the current pronunciation originated two centuries after his death.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last1=Oldfield |first1=Molly |last2=Mitchinson |first2=John |author-link2=John Mitchinson (researcher) |date=May 5, 2011 |title=QI: Quite interesting facts about Spain |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/men/the-filter/qi/8495579/QI-Quite-interesting-facts-about-Spain.html |url-access=subscription |url-status=live |archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/archive/20220111/https://www.telegraph.co.uk/men/the-filter/qi/8495579/QI-Quite-interesting-facts-about-Spain.html |archive-date=January 11, 2022 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |work=[[The Daily Telegraph]]}}{{cbignore}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Erichsen |first=Gerald |date=January 11, 2019 |title=Did a Royal Edict Give Spaniards a Lisp? |url=https://www.thoughtco.com/where-did-spaniards-get-their-lisp-3078240 |access-date=2020-05-01 |website=ThoughtCo |publisher=[[Dotdash Meredith]] |language=}}</ref></noinclude>
* The correct way to say "no problem" in Spanish is "no problema", not "no problemo".

* [[Sign language]]s are not the same worldwide. Aside from the [[pidgin]] [[International Sign]], each country generally has its own native sign language, and some have more than one.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite book||url=http://www.ethnologue.com/subgroups/deaf-sign-language |title=Ethnologue: Languages of the World |series=Ethnologue |publisher=SIL International |year=2013 |editor1-last=Lewis |editor1-first=M. Paul |edition=17th |contribution=Deaf sign language |access-date=December 3, 2013 |editor2-last=Simons |editor2-first=Gary F. |editor3-last=Fennig |editor3-first=Charles D. |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131126034146/http://www.ethnologue.com/subgroups/deaf-sign-language |archive-date=November 26, 2013 }}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite book||last1=Supalla |first1=Ted |author-link1=Ted Supalla |title=Language, Gesture, and Space |last2=Webb |first2=Rebecca |publisher=Psychology Press |year=2013 |isbn=978-1-134-77966-6 |editor1-last=Reilly |editor1-first=Judy Snitzer |pages=333–52 |chapter=The grammar of international sign: A new look at pidgin languages. |access-date=February 16, 2017 |editor2-last=Emmorey |editor2-first=Karen |editor2-link=Karen Emmorey |chapter-url=https://books.google.com/books?id=xAKXpO7mCE0C&pg=PA333 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230121033603/https://books.google.com/books?id=xAKXpO7mCE0C&pg=PA333 |archive-date=January 21, 2023 |url-status=live}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Omar |first=Hasuria Che |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=L38_jNlkADAC&pg=PA293 |title=The Sustainability of the Translation Field |publisher=ITBM |year=2009 |isbn=978-983-42179-6-9 |page=293 |access-date=February 21, 2017 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230121033603/https://books.google.com/books?id=L38_jNlkADAC&pg=PA293 |archive-date=January 21, 2023 |url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude>

* The word "[[gringo]]" did not originate during the [[Mexican–American War]] (1846–1848) as a corruption of "Green, go home!", in reference to the green uniforms of American troops.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=April 27, 2018 |title=Where does the word "Gringo" come from? |url=https://www.theyucatantimes.com/2018/04/where-does-the-word-gringo-come-from/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220322024754/https://www.theyucatantimes.com/2018/04/where-does-the-word-gringo-come-from/ |archive-date=March 22, 2022 |access-date=June 11, 2022 |website=The Yucatan Times}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Sayers |first=William |date=May 20, 2009 |title=An Unnoticed Early Attestation of gringo 'Foreigner': Implications for Its Origin |url=https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/full/10.1080/14753820902937946 |journal=Bulletin of Spanish Studies |volume=86 |issue=3 |pages=323–330 |doi=10.1080/14753820902937946}}</ref></noinclude> The word originally simply meant "foreigner", and is probably a corruption of the Spanish word ''griego'' for "Greek" (along the lines of the idiom "It's [[Greek to me]]").<noinclude><ref name="Ramirez 2013">{{#invoke:cite web||last=Ramirez |first=Aida |date=August 7, 2013 |title=Who, Exactly, Is A Gringo? |url=https://www.npr.org/sections/codeswitch/2013/08/07/209266300/who-exactly-is-a-gringo |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211222134905/https://www.npr.org/sections/codeswitch/2013/08/07/209266300/who-exactly-is-a-gringo |archive-date=December 22, 2021 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=[[NPR]]}}</ref><ref>{{cite encyclopedia |title=Gringo |encyclopedia=[[American Heritage Dictionary of the English Language]] |publisher=[[Houghton Mifflin Harcourt]] |url=http://education.yahoo.com/reference/dictionary/entry/gringo |access-date=July 7, 2024 |date= |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130514193349/http://education.yahoo.com/reference/dictionary/entry/gringo |archive-date=May 14, 2013}}</ref></noinclude>

==== English language ====
{{Main|List of common false etymologies|Common English usage misconceptions}}
* ''[[Irregardless]]'' is a word. It appears in numerous dictionaries along with other [[Nonstandard dialect|nonstandard]], [[slang]], or [[Colloquialism|colloquial]] terms.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Is 'Irregardless' a Real Word? |url=https://www.merriam-webster.com/words-at-play/is-irregardless-a-real-word-heh-heh |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220516122641/https://www.merriam-webster.com/words-at-play/is-irregardless-a-real-word-heh-heh |archive-date=May 16, 2022 |access-date=June 11, 2022 |publisher=[[Merriam-Webster]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Definition: irregardless |url=http://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/irregardless |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140508042618/http://www.merriam-webster.com/dictionary/irregardless |archive-date=May 8, 2014 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |publisher=[[Merriam-Webster]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* It is permissible to [[Preposition stranding#Controversy|end a sentence with a preposition]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Prepositions, Ending a Sentence with |url=https://www.merriam-webster.com/grammar/prepositions-ending-a-sentence-with |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240410213705/https://www.merriam-webster.com/grammar/prepositions-ending-a-sentence-with |archive-date=April 10, 2024 |access-date=May 23, 2024 |publisher=[[Merriam-Webster]]}}</ref></noinclude> The supposed rule against it originated in an attempt to imitate Latin, but modern linguists agree that it is a natural and organic part of the English language.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Thompson |first=Oliver |date=February 28, 2024 |title=Why Merriam-Webster says it's OK to end a sentence in a preposition |url=https://www.cbc.ca/radio/asithappens/sentence-preposition-webster-1.7127397 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240313084307/https://www.cbc.ca/radio/asithappens/sentence-preposition-webster-1.7127397 |archive-date=March 13, 2024 |access-date=June 16, 2024 |work=[[Canadian Broadcasting Corporation]]}}</ref></noinclude> Similarly, modern [[Style manual|style and usage manuals]] allow [[Split infinitive#Current views|split infinitives]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Fogarty |first=Mignon |author-link=Mignon Fogarty |title=The Ultimate Writing Guide for Students |publisher=Henry Holt & Company |year=2011 |isbn=978-0-8050-8944-8 |location=New York |pages=17–18}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[African American Vernacular English]] speakers do not simply [[Habitual be|replace "is" with "be"]] across all tenses, with no added meaning. In fact, AAVE speakers use "be" to mark a [[habitual aspect|habitual]] [[grammatical aspect]] not explicitly distinguished in Standard English.<noinclude><ref>a. {{Cite thesis |last=Jackson |first=Janice Eurana |title=Linguistic aspect in African-American English-speaking children: An investigation of aspectual "be" |date=1998 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |degree=Dissertation |publisher=[[University of Massachusetts Amherst]] |url=https://www.proquest.com/docview/304446674 |isbn=978-0-591-96032-7 |id={{ProQuest|304446674}} |archive-date=July 8, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240708184000/https://www.proquest.com/docview/304446674 |url-status=live }}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||title=African American English |url=https://www.pbs.org/speak/education/curriculum/high/aae/#aaegram |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120930015421/http://www.pbs.org/speak/education/curriculum/high/aae/#aaegram |archive-date=September 30, 2012 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |publisher=[[PBS]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* "[[420 (cannabis culture)|420]]" did not originate from the Los Angeles police or penal code for marijuana use.<noinclude><ref name="snopes420">{{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=Barbara |date=June 13, 2008 |title=420 |url=http://www.snopes.com/language/stories/420.asp |url-status=live |archive-url=https://swap.stanford.edu/20091019112947/http://www.snopes.com/language/stories/420.asp |archive-date=October 19, 2009 |access-date=June 17, 2011 |website=[[Snopes]]}}</ref></noinclude> [[California Penal Code]] section 420 prohibits the obstruction of access to public land.<noinclude><ref name="snopes420" /><noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date= |title=Title 11. Of Crimes Against the Public Peace [403 - 420.1]: 420 |url=https://leginfo.legislature.ca.gov/faces/codes_displaySection.xhtml?lawCode=PEN&sectionNum=420. |access-date=July 7, 2024 |website=leginfo.legislature.ca.gov}}</ref></noinclude> The use of "420" started in 1971 at [[San Rafael High School]], where a group of students would go to smoke at 4:20&nbsp;pm.<noinclude><ref name="snopes420" /></noinclude>

* ''[[Xmas]]'' did not originate as a secular plan to "take Christ out of Christmas".<noinclude>{{sfn|O'Conner|Kellerman|2009|pages=77, 145}}</noinclude> ''X'' represents the Greek letter [[Chi (letter)|chi]], the first letter of {{lang|grc|Χριστός}} ({{transl|grc|''Christós''}}), "Christ" in Greek,<noinclude><ref name="xmaschi">{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.crivoice.org/symbols/xmasorigin.html|title=The Origin of "Xmas"|access-date=June 10, 2011|publisher=CRI / Voice, Institute|author=Bratcher, Dennis|date=December 3, 2007|ref=Bra07|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130530044125/http://www.crivoice.org/symbols/xmasorigin.html|archive-date=May 30, 2013|url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude> as found in [[Chi Rho|the chi-rho symbol (ΧΡ)]] since the 4th century. In English, "X" was first used as a [[scribal abbreviation]] for "Christ" in 1021.<noinclude><ref>{{Cite OED |term=X |id=9635674512 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |date=1921}}</ref><ref>{{Cite OED |term=Xmas |id=7290422930 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |date=2020}}</ref></noinclude>
* The word ''crap'' did not originate as a [[back-formation]] of British plumber [[Thomas Crapper]]'s [[aptronym|apt surname]].<noinclude><ref name="Harper 2010">{{#invoke:cite web||last=Harper |first=Douglas |date=2010 |title=Crap |url=http://www.etymonline.com/index.php?term=crap |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140427083257/http://www.etymonline.com/index.php?term=crap |archive-date=April 27, 2014 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |work=[[Online Etymology Dictionary]]}}</ref></noinclude> The word ''crap'' ultimately comes from [[Medieval Latin]] ''crappa''.<noinclude><ref name="Harper 2010" /><noinclude><ref>{{cite encyclopedia |title=Crap |encyclopedia=[[American Heritage Dictionary of the English Language]] |publisher=[[Houghton Mifflin Harcourt]] |url=http://education.yahoo.com/reference/dictionary/entry/crap |access-date=June 17, 2011 |date=2001 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130121195235/http://education.yahoo.com/reference/dictionary/entry/crap |archive-date=January 21, 2013}}</ref></noinclude>
* The word ''[[fuck]]'' did not originate in the Middle Ages as an [[acronym]].<noinclude><ref name="Sheidlower 2009">{{#invoke:cite book||last=Sheidlower |first=Jesse |author-link=Jesse Sheidlower |title=[[The F-Word (book)|The F-Word]] |publisher=[[Oxford University Press]] |year=2009 |isbn=978-0-19-539311-8 |edition=3rd |location=New York |chapter=Introduction}}</ref></noinclude> Proposed acronyms include "fornicating under consent of king" or "for unlawful carnal knowledge", used as a sign posted above adulterers in the stocks. Nor did it originate as a corruption of "pluck yew" (an idiom falsely attributed to the English for drawing a [[longbow]]).<noinclude><ref name="Sheidlower 2009" /><ref name="fuckingcitation">a. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=Barbara |date=July 8, 2007 |title=What the Fuck? |url=http://www.snopes.com/language/acronyms/fuck.asp |url-status=live |archive-url=https://www.webcitation.org/67BKzr94Z?url=http://www.snopes.com/language/acronyms/fuck.asp |archive-date=April 25, 2012 |access-date=June 17, 2011 |website=[[Snopes]]}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=Barbara |date=July 9, 2007 |title=Pluck Yew |url=http://www.snopes.com/language/apocryph/pluckyew.asp |url-status=live |archive-url=https://www.webcitation.org/67BKzr94Z?url=http://www.snopes.com/language/acronyms/fuck.asp |archive-date=April 25, 2012 |access-date=June 17, 2011 |website=[[Snopes]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Sheidlower |first=Jesse |author-link=Jesse Sheidlower |date=Autumn 1998 |title=Revising the F-Word |journal=Verbatim: The Language Quarterly |volume=23 |issue=4 |pages=18–21}}</ref></noinclude> It is most likely derived from [[Middle Dutch]] or other [[Germanic languages]], where it either meant "to thrust" or "to copulate with" (''fokken'' in Middle Dutch), "to copulate", or "to strike, push, copulate" or "penis".<noinclude><ref name="fuckingcitation" /></noinclude> Either way, these variations would have been derived from the Indo-European root word ''-peuk'', meaning "to prick".<noinclude><ref name="fuckingcitation" /></noinclude>
* The expression "[[rule of thumb]]" did not originate from an English law allowing a man to beat his wife with a stick no thicker than his thumb, and there is no evidence that such a law ever existed.<noinclude><ref name="Kelly 1994">{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Kelly |first=Henry Ansgar |date=September 1994 |title=''Rule of Thumb'' and the Folklaw of the Husband's Stick |url=http://csswashtenaw.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/Rule_of_Thumb.pdf |url-status=live |journal=Journal of Legal Education |volume=44 |issue=3 |pages=341–65 |jstor=42893341 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150924122340/http://csswashtenaw.org/wp-content/uploads/2013/07/Rule_of_Thumb.pdf |archive-date=September 24, 2015 |access-date=May 23, 2024}}</ref></noinclude> The expression originates from the late seventeenth century from various [[Craft|trades]] where quantities were measured by comparison to the width or length of a thumb.<noinclude><ref name="Kelly 1994" />{{sfn|O'Conner|Kellerman|2009|pp=123–126}}
* The term "[[blue law]]s", denoting laws banning certain activities on specific days, did not originate from such laws being originally written on blue paper.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=David |date=March 11, 2001 |title=Why Are Blue Laws Called 'Blue Laws'? |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/what-are-blue-laws/ |access-date=June 25, 2024 |website=[[Snopes]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Cheung |first=Iva |date=May 25, 2015 |title=Sacré Bleu! Why Is Blue the Most Profane Color? |url=https://slate.com/human-interest/2015/05/why-do-we-associate-the-color-blue-with-swearing.html |access-date=June 25, 2024 |work=[[Slate (magazine)|Slate]]}}</ref></noinclude>
