* The word ''the'' was never pronounced or spelled "ye" in [[Old English|Old]] or [[Middle English]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Brians |first=Paul |date=2011 |title=Common Errors in English Usage – Ye |url=http://public.wsu.edu/~brians/errors/ye.html |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130531122316/http://public.wsu.edu/~brians/errors/ye.html |archive-date=May 31, 2013 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |work=Common Errors in English Usage |publisher=[[Washington State University]]}}</ref></noinclude> The confusion, seen in the [[stock phrase|common stock phrase]] "[[ye olde]]", derives from the use of the character [[Thorn (letter)|thorn]] (þ), which in Middle English represented the sound now represented in Modern English by "th".<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Harper |first=Douglas |date=2001–2010 |title=Etymology Online |url=http://www.etymonline.com/index.php?term=ye |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140427082431/http://www.etymonline.com/index.php?term=ye |archive-date=April 27, 2014 |access-date=June 24, 2011 |work=Online Etymology Dictionary}}</ref></noinclude> This evolved as early printing presses substituted the word ''the'' with "yͤ", a "y" character with a superscript "e".<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Hill |first=Will |title=The Routledge Handbook of the English Writing System |date=30 June 2020 |publisher=[[Taylor & Francis]] |isbn=978-0-367-58156-5 |pages=6, 15 |chapter=Chapter 25: Typography and the printed English text |chapter-url=https://arro.anglia.ac.uk/id/eprint/703215/1/25HillFinalDV.pdf |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220710022857/https://arro.anglia.ac.uk/id/eprint/703215/1/25HillFinalDV.pdf |archive-date=July 10, 2022 }}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[anti-Italian]] slur ''[[wop]]'' did not originate from an acronym for "without papers"<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Zimmer |first=Ben |author-link=Ben Zimmer |date=April 23, 2018 |title='Wop' Doesn't Mean What Andrew Cuomo Thinks It Means |url=https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2018/04/wop-doesnt-mean-what-andrew-cuomo-thinks-it-means/558659/ |access-date=June 22, 2024 |work=[[The Atlantic]]}}</ref></noinclude> or "without passport";<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Harper |first=Douglas |date=October 25, 2017 |title=Ingenious Trifling |url=http://www.etymonline.com/baloney.php |access-date=June 16, 2024 |website=[[Online Etymology Dictionary]]}}</ref>{{sfn|O'Conner|Kellerman|2009|pages=77, 145}}</noinclude> it is actually derived from the term ''[[guappo]]'' (roughly meaning ''[[Thuggee|thug]]''), from the Spanish ''guapo''.<noinclude><ref>{{Cite American Heritage Dictionary|wop}}</ref></noinclude>

=== Law, crime, and military ===
[[File:ViolentCrimeInTheUS1960-2022.png|thumb|Violent crime rates in the United States declined between 1991 and 2022.]]
* [[Crime drop|Crime rates are declining]] for most types of crime, beginning in the mid to late 1980s and early 1990s.<noinclude><ref name=cj>{{cite journal|last1=Farrell|first1=Graham|last2=Tilley|first2=Nick|last3=Tseloni|first3=Andromachi|title=Why the Crime Drop?|journal=Crime and Justice|date=September 2014|volume=43|issue=1|pages=421–490|doi=10.1086/678081|s2cid=145719976|url=http://eprints.whiterose.ac.uk/97466/1/Farrell%20Tilley%20Tseloni%202014%20Why%20the%20Crime%20Drop%20%28C%26J%20vol43%29.pdf|archive-date=December 15, 2021|access-date=October 7, 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211215225328/https://eprints.whiterose.ac.uk/97466/1/Farrell%20Tilley%20Tseloni%202014%20Why%20the%20Crime%20Drop%20%28C%26J%20vol43%29.pdf|url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude> In Europe, [[crime statistics]] show this is part of a broader pattern of crime decline since the late [[Middle Ages]], with a reversal from the 1960s to the 1980s and 1990s, before the decline continued.<noinclude><ref name=tonry-1-2>{{Cite journal |url=https://scholarship.law.umn.edu/faculty_articles/511 |last=Tonry |first=Michael |title=Why Crime Rates Are Falling Throughout the Western World, 43 Crime & Just. 1 (2014) |journal=Crime & Just |date=January 2014 |pages=1–2 |archive-date=May 23, 2020 |access-date=October 7, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200523194607/https://scholarship.law.umn.edu/faculty_articles/511/ |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude> [[Crime in the United States|In the United States]], between 1993 and 2022, the rate of violent crime per 100,000 people fell by almost 50%, and the rate of property crime fell by more than half.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Gramlich |first=John |date=November 20, 2020 |title=What the data says (and doesn't say) about crime in the United States |url=https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2020/11/20/facts-about-crime-in-the-u-s/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210218051336/https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2020/11/20/facts-about-crime-in-the-u-s/ |archive-date=February 18, 2021 |access-date=February 19, 2021 |website=[[Pew Research]]}}</ref></noinclude> The number of gun homicides also decreased.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=October 21, 2015 |title=Gun homicides steady after decline in '90s; suicide rate edges up |url=https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2015/10/21/gun-homicides-steady-after-decline-in-90s-suicide-rate-edges-up/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190903161457/https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2015/10/21/gun-homicides-steady-after-decline-in-90s-suicide-rate-edges-up/ |archive-date=September 3, 2019 |access-date=September 4, 2019 |website=[[Pew Research]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* Despite parents of many cultures having been regarded as having the right, if not duty, to [[Corporal punishment in the home|physically punish misbehaving children]] to teach appropriate [[behavior]] such as by [[spanking]], many studies consistently find that [[corporal punishment]] may have the opposite effect in the long run, decreasing long-term [[obedience (human behavior)|obedience]],<noinclude><ref name=Gershoff2010>{{cite journal |author=Gershoff, Elizabeth T. |date=Spring 2010 |title=More Harm Than Good: A Summary of Scientific Research on the Intended and Unintended Effects of Corporal Punishment on Children |url=http://scholarship.law.duke.edu/lcp/vol73/iss2/3/ |journal=[[Law & Contemporary Problems]] |publisher=[[Duke University School of Law]] |volume=73 |issue=2 |pages=31–56 |author-link=Elizabeth Gershoff |archive-date=June 20, 2017 |access-date=December 18, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170620170605/http://scholarship.law.duke.edu/lcp/vol73/iss2/3/ |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude> while increasing the chances of [[aggressive]] behavior, [[Depression (mood)|depression]], [[anxiety]], [[suicide]], and [[physical abuse]].<noinclude><ref>{{cite journal |last1=Gershoff |first1=Elizabeth T. |last2=Grogan-Kaylor |first2=Andrew |title=Spanking and Child Outcomes: Old Controversies and New Meta-Analyses |journal=Journal of Family Psychology |date=2016 |doi=10.1037/fam0000191 |pmid=27055181 |volume=30 |issue=4 |pages=453–469 |pmc=7992110 |url=http://local.psy.miami.edu/faculty/dmessinger/c_c/rsrcs/rdgs/emot/spanging.meta.2016.jFamPsych.pdf |archive-date=April 18, 2024 |access-date=December 18, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240418063144/https://local.psy.miami.edu/faculty/dmessinger/c_c/rsrcs/rdgs/emot/spanging.meta.2016.jFamPsych.pdf |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="Afifi">{{cite journal | last1=Afifi | first1=T. O. | last2=Mota | first2=N. P. | last3=Dasiewicz | first3=P. | last4=MacMillan | first4=H. L. | last5=Sareen | first5=J. | title=Physical Punishment and Mental Disorders: Results From a Nationally Representative US Sample | journal=Pediatrics | publisher=American Academy of Pediatrics (AAP) | volume=130 | issue=2 | date=2 July 2012 | issn=0031-4005 | doi=10.1542/peds.2011-2947 | pmid=22753561 | pages=184–192| s2cid=21759236 | doi-access=free }}</ref><ref>{{Cite journal |last=Gershoff |first=E. T. |title=The strength of the causal evidence against physical punishment of children and its implications for parents, psychologists, and policymakers. |url=https://psycnet.apa.org/manuscript/2018-33351-006.pdf |journal=American Psychologist |date=2018 |volume=73 |issue=5 |pages=626–638 |doi=10.1037/amp0000327 |pmid=29999352 |pmc=8194004 |archive-date=September 23, 2024 |access-date=December 18, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240923102122/https://psycnet.apa.org/manuscript/2018-33351-006.pdf |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude> See also [[Spanking#Alternatives to spanking|Alternatives to spanking]].
* Chewing gum is not punishable by [[caning]] in Singapore. Although importing and selling chewing gum [[Chewing gum sales ban in Singapore|has been illegal in Singapore]] since 1992, and [[Caning in Singapore|corporal punishment]] is still an applicable penalty for certain offenses in the country, the two facts are unrelated; chewing gum-related offenses have always been only subject to fines and incarceration, and the possession or consumption of chewing gum itself is not illegal.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Benedictus |first=Leo |date=March 23, 2015 |title=Gum control: how Lee Kuan Yew kept chewing gum off Singapore's streets |url=http://www.theguardian.com/lifeandstyle/shortcuts/2015/mar/23/gum-control-how-lee-kuan-yew-kept-chewing-gum-off-singapores-streets |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230210125248/https://www.theguardian.com/lifeandstyle/shortcuts/2015/mar/23/gum-control-how-lee-kuan-yew-kept-chewing-gum-off-singapores-streets |archive-date=February 10, 2023 |access-date=July 9, 2022 |website=[[The Guardian]] |language=en}}<br />b. {{#invoke:cite journal||last=Rajah |first=Jothie |date=January 1, 2014 |title=Flogging Gum: Cultural Imaginaries and Postcoloniality in Singapore's Rule of Law |url=https://ro.uow.edu.au/ltc/vol18/iss1/10 |url-status=live |journal=Law Text Culture |volume=18 |issue=1 |pages=135–165 |doi=10.14453/ltc.558 |issn=1322-9060 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230310232148/https://ro.uow.edu.au/ltc/vol18/iss1/10/ |archive-date=March 10, 2023 |access-date=July 9, 2022}}<br />c. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Brown |first=Lauren |date=March 1, 2012 |title=How To Travel In Singapore Without Getting Caned |url=https://www.businessinsider.com/singapore-rules-laws-etiquette-gum-drugs-2012-2 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221021083211/https://www.businessinsider.com/singapore-rules-laws-etiquette-gum-drugs-2012-2 |archive-date=October 21, 2022 |access-date=July 9, 2022 |website=[[Business Insider]] |language=en-US}}</ref></noinclude>
* Employees of the international police organization [[Interpol]] cannot conduct investigations, arrest criminals or use [[fake passport]]s.{{Clarification needed|reason=Are the interpol agents or the criminals the ones with the passports?|date=June 2024}} Interpol's role is facilitating international communication between [[Law enforcement agency|law enforcement agencies]] of [[sovereign state]]s.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Gilsinan |first=Kathy |date=2014-05-12 |title=Interpol at 100: Does the World's Police Force Work? |url=https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2014/05/interpol-the-global-police-force-that-isnt/362086/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230416134627/https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2014/05/interpol-the-global-police-force-that-isnt/362086/ |archive-date=April 16, 2023 |access-date=2022-04-02 |website=[[The Atlantic]] |language=}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Lee |first=Michael |title=Interpol hopes physical border security will solve virtual borders |url=https://www.zdnet.com/article/interpol-hopes-physical-border-security-will-solve-virtual-borders/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230129045835/https://www.zdnet.com/article/interpol-hopes-physical-border-security-will-solve-virtual-borders/ |archive-date=January 29, 2023 |access-date=2022-04-07 |website=[[ZDNet]] |language=en}}</ref></noinclude>
* No cases have been proven of strangers [[Poisoned candy myths|killing or permanently injuring children by intentionally hiding]] poisons or sharp objects such as razor blades in candy or apples during Halloween trick-or-treating and the belief has been "thoroughly debunked". However, in at least one case, adult family members have spread this story to cover up [[filicide]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Brunvand |first=Jan Harold |author-link=Jan Harold Brunvand |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=9xOb-19lXx8C |title=Encyclopedia of Urban Legends |date=2012-01-01 |publisher=[[ABC-CLIO]] |isbn=978-1-59884-720-8 |page=288 |language=en |access-date=November 10, 2018 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230121033601/https://books.google.com/books?id=9xOb-19lXx8C |archive-date=January 21, 2023 |url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude>
* There has never been a documented case of [[Black cat#Adoption and Black Cat Day|pet black cats being tortured or ritually sacrificed]] around Halloween. Where violent deaths of black cats have been documented around Halloween, the death has usually been ascribed to natural predators, such as coyotes, eagles, or raptors.<noinclude><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.dcourier.com/main.asp?SectionID=74&SubsectionID=114&ArticleID=86024 |author=Boks, Ed |title=The truth about black cats and Halloween |location=Prescott, Arizona |work=[[The Daily Courier (Arizona)|The Daily Courier]] |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120322011039/http://www.dcourier.com/main.asp?SectionID=74&SubsectionID=114&ArticleID=86024 |archive-date=2012-03-22 |date=2010-10-06 |access-date=2010-10-10 }}</ref></noinclude>
* It is not necessary to wait 24 hours before filing a [[missing person]] report. When there is evidence of violence or of an unusual absence, it is important to start an investigation promptly.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite news||last1=Sparks |first1=Preston |last2=Cox |first2=Timothy |date=November 17, 2008 |title=Missing persons usually found |url=http://chronicle.augusta.com/stories/2008/11/17/met_483813.shtml |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131214111833/http://chronicle.augusta.com/stories/2008/11/17/met_483813.shtml |archive-date=December 14, 2013 |access-date=May 21, 2011 |newspaper=[[Augusta Chronicle]]}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||title=FAQs: Question: Do you need to wait 24&nbsp;hours before reporting a person missing? |url=http://www.missingpersons.gov.au/nmpcc/faqs.aspx#a1 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080923232230/http://www.missingpersons.gov.au/nmpcc/faqs.aspx#a1 |archive-date=September 23, 2008 |access-date=May 22, 2011 |publisher=National Missing Persons Coordination Center, [[Australian Federal Police]]}}<br />c. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Vongkiatkajorn |first=Kanyakrit |title=NYPD: How The Police Handles Missing Persons Cases |url=https://themissingny.nycitynewsservice.com/part-two/nypd-explainer/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230404005845/https://themissingny.nycitynewsservice.com/part-two/nypd-explainer/ |archive-date=April 4, 2023 |access-date=June 25, 2022 |website=[[NYCity News Service]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=June 3, 2013 |title=Report or find a missing person |url=https://www.gov.uk/report-missing-person |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140122170802/https://www.gov.uk/report-missing-person |archive-date=January 22, 2014 |access-date=August 18, 2013 |website=[[Gov.uk]]}}</ref></noinclude> Criminology experts say the first 72 hours in a missing person investigation are the most critical.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Why the first 72 hours in a missing persons investigation are the most critical, according to criminology experts |url=https://abcnews.go.com/US/72-hours-missing-persons-investigation-critical-criminology-experts/story?id=58292638 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230312194816/https://abcnews.go.com/US/72-hours-missing-persons-investigation-critical-criminology-experts/story?id=58292638 |archive-date=March 12, 2023 |access-date=June 11, 2022 |website=[[ABC News (United States)|ABC News]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Perry Mason moment]]s, in which a person on trial for a crime is suddenly exonerated by newly introduced revelations, are exceptionally rare in real-life court proceedings, despite their ubiquity in [[legal drama]]. The vast majority of evidence is unveiled in pretrial [[Discovery (law)|discovery]]; should new revelations occur, a trial is usually [[stay of proceedings|stayed]] until both the prosecution and defense can review it.<noinclude><ref>{{Bluebook journal|first=Douglas|last=Abrams|title=References to Television Shows in Judicial Opinions and Written Advocacy (Part I)|volume=75|journal=J.Mo.B.|page=25|pin=27|year=2019|url=https://scholarship.law.missouri.edu/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?article=1959&context=facpubs|quote=... [W]ell prepared counsel normally anticipate the course of the trial in the relatively few cases that do not end with pretrial settlement or plea bargain, and because contemporary procedure emphasizes pretrial discovery and favors conferences with the court outside the jury's presence or earshot when surprise does surface.}}</ref></noinclude>

==== United States ====
[[File:Arrest rates from 2012 to 2018 in Texas.png|thumb|Immigrants had lower arrest rates than citizens in Texas, 2012–2018 ]]
* Undocumented immigrants in the US have substantially lower [[Crime in the United States#Arrests by immigration status|crime rates]] than US-born citizens.<noinclude><ref>Immigrants are less likely to commit crimes than U.S.-born Americans, studies find MARCH 8,  ALL THINGS CONSIDERED Jasmine Garsd https://www.npr.org/2024/03/08/1237103158/immigrants-are-less-likely-to-commit-crimes-than-us-born-americans-studies-find {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240516223924/https://www.npr.org/2024/03/08/1237103158/immigrants-are-less-likely-to-commit-crimes-than-us-born-americans-studies-find |date=May 16, 2024 }}</ref><ref name="Light 2020" /> Compared to undocumented immigrants, US-born citizens are more than twice as likely to be arrested for violent crimes, 2.5 times more likely to be arrested for [[Drug-related crime|drug crimes]], and over 4 times more likely to be arrested for property crimes.<noinclude><ref name="Light 2020">{{cite journal |last1=Light |first1=Michael T. |last2=He |first2=Jingying |last3=Robey |first3=Jason P. |title=Comparing crime rates between undocumented immigrants, legal immigrants, and native-born US citizens in Texas |journal=Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences |date=2020 |volume=117 |issue=51 |pages=32340–32347 |doi=10.1073/pnas.2014704117 |doi-access=free|pmid=33288713 |pmc=7768760 |bibcode=2020PNAS..11732340L }}</ref></noinclude> Immigrants are 60% less likely to be incarcerated than US-born citizens.<noinclude><ref>The mythical tie between immigration and crime
 Stanford Institute for Economic Policy Research (SIEPR) Krysten Crawford  July 21, 2023 https://siepr.stanford.edu/news/mythical-tie-between-immigration-and-crime {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240521185535/https://siepr.stanford.edu/news/mythical-tie-between-immigration-and-crime |date=May 21, 2024 }}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[First Amendment to the United States Constitution]] generally prevents only government restrictions on the freedoms of [[Freedom of religion in the United States|religion]], [[Freedom of speech in the United States|speech]], [[Freedom of the press in the United States|press]], [[Freedom of assembly|assembly]], or [[Right to petition in the United States|petition]],<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last1=Willingham |first1=AJ |date=September 6, 2018 |title=The First Amendment doesn't guarantee you the rights you think it does |url=https://www.cnn.com/2017/04/27/politics/first-amendment-explainer-trnd/index.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190301225218/https://www.cnn.com/2017/04/27/politics/first-amendment-explainer-trnd/index.html |archive-date=March 1, 2019 |access-date=March 1, 2019 |work=CNN}}</ref></noinclude> not restrictions imposed by other entities unless they are [[state actor|acting on behalf of the government]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last1=McGregor |first1=Jena |date=August 8, 2017 |title=The Google memo is a reminder that we generally don't have free speech at work |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/on-leadership/wp/2017/08/08/the-google-memo-is-a-reminder-that-we-generally-dont-have-free-speech-at-work/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200125155407/https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/on-leadership/wp/2017/08/08/the-google-memo-is-a-reminder-that-we-generally-dont-have-free-speech-at-work/ |archive-date=January 25, 2020 |access-date=March 1, 2019 |newspaper=[[The Washington Post]] |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last1=Dunn |first1=Christopher |date=April 28, 2009 |title=Column: Applying the Constitution to Private Actors (New York Law Journal) |url=http://www.nyclu.org/oped/column-applying-constitution-private-actors-new-york-law-journal |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131202234721/http://www.nyclu.org/oped/column-applying-constitution-private-actors-new-york-law-journal |archive-date=December 2, 2013 |access-date=January 27, 2017 |publisher=New York Civil Liberties Union}}</ref></noinclude> Other laws may limit the ability of private businesses and individuals to restrict the speech of others.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last1=Berman-Gorvine |first1=Martin |date=May 19, 2014 |title=Employer Ability to Silence Employee Speech Narrowing in Private Sector, Attorneys Say |url=https://www.bna.com/employer-ability-silence-n17179890580/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190331165028/https://www.bna.com/employer-ability-silence-n17179890580/ |archive-date=March 31, 2019 |access-date=March 1, 2019 |work=Bloomberg BNA}}</ref></noinclude>
* In the United States, a defendant may not have their case dismissed simply because they were not read their [[Miranda warning|Miranda rights]] at the time of their arrest. Miranda warnings cover the rights of a person when they are taken into custody and then interrogated by law enforcement.<noinclude><ref>Imwinkelried and Blinka, ''Criminal Evidentiary Foundations'', 2d ed. (Lexis 2007) {{ISBN|978-1-4224-1741-6}} at 620.</ref></noinclude> If a person is not given a Miranda warning before the interrogation is conducted, statements made by them during the interrogation may not be admissible in a trial. The prosecution may still present other forms of evidence, or statements made during interrogations where the defendant ''was'' read their Miranda rights, to get a conviction.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=September 10, 2021 |title=Can a case be dismissed if a person is not read his/her Miranda rights? |url=http://www.mirandawarning.org/casedismissedifnotreadmirandarights.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220714054454/http://www.mirandawarning.org/casedismissedifnotreadmirandarights.html |archive-date=July 14, 2022 |access-date=September 10, 2021 |work=Patrick Barone}}</ref></noinclude>
* The United States does not require police officers to identify themselves as police in the case of a sting or other undercover work, and police officers may lie when engaged in such work.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=March 12, 1998 |title=Snopes on Entrapment |url=http://www.snopes.com/risque/hookers/cop.asp |access-date=August 29, 2009 |website=Snopes.com}}</ref></noinclude> Claiming [[entrapment]] as a defense instead focuses on whether the defendant was improperly induced by undue pressure from government agents (possibly including civilians and [[informants]] acting under police direction) to commit crimes they would not have otherwise committed.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last1=Larson |first1=Aaron |title=What is Entrapment |url=https://www.expertlaw.com/library/criminal-law/what-entrapment |website=ExpertLaw |access-date=June 18, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171026002224/https://www.expertlaw.com/library/criminal-law/what-entrapment |archive-date=October 26, 2017 }}</ref></noinclude>
* It is not illegal in the US to [[Shouting fire in a crowded theater|shout "fire" in a crowded theater]]. Although this is often given as an example of speech that is not protected by the First Amendment, it is not now nor has it ever been binding law. The phrase originates from Justice [[Oliver Wendell Holmes Jr.]]'s [[legal opinion|opinion]] in the [[United States Supreme Court]] case ''[[Schenck v. United States]]'' in 1919, which held that the defendant's speech in opposition to the draft during World War I was not protected free speech. However, that case was not about shouting "fire" and the decision was later overturned by ''[[Brandenburg v. Ohio]]'' in 1969.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Timm |first=Trevor |date=2012-11-02 |title=It's Time to Stop Using the 'Fire in a Crowded Theater' Quote |url=https://www.theatlantic.com/national/archive/2012/11/its-time-to-stop-using-the-fire-in-a-crowded-theater-quote/264449/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230815121915/https://www.theatlantic.com/national/archive/2012/11/its-time-to-stop-using-the-fire-in-a-crowded-theater-quote/264449/ |archive-date=August 15, 2023 |access-date=2020-06-20 |website=The Atlantic |language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Volokh |first=Eugene |date=2015-05-11 |title=Shouting fire in a crowded theater |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/volokh-conspiracy/wp/2015/05/11/shouting-fire-in-a-crowded-theater/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230320072905/https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/volokh-conspiracy/wp/2015/05/11/shouting-fire-in-a-crowded-theater/ |archive-date=March 20, 2023 |access-date=2020-06-20 |newspaper=Washington Post |language=en}}</ref></noinclude>
* The US Armed Forces have generally forbidden military enlistment as a form of [[deferred adjudication]] (that is, an option for convicts to avoid jail time) since the 1980s.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=May 8, 2012 |title=5 Military Myths Busted |url=https://www.military.com/join-armed-forces/military-myths.html |access-date=June 23, 2024 |website=[[Military.com]]}}</ref></noinclude> US Navy protocols discourage the practice, while the other four branches have specific regulations against it.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Powers |first=Rod |date=November 24, 2019 |title=Can a Judge Order Someone to Join the Military or Go to Jail? |url=https://www.thebalance.com/join-the-military-or-go-to-jail-3354033 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171230172616/https://www.thebalance.com/join-the-military-or-go-to-jail-3354033 |archive-date=December 30, 2017 |access-date=December 30, 2017 |website=[[The Balance (website)|The Balance]]}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Schogol |first=Jeff |date=February 3, 2006 |title=Judge said Army or jail, but military doesn't want him |url=https://www.stripes.com/news/judge-said-army-or-jail-but-military-doesn-t-want-him-1.44417 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171230172757/https://www.stripes.com/news/judge-said-army-or-jail-but-military-doesn-t-want-him-1.44417 |archive-date=December 30, 2017 |access-date=December 30, 2017 |website=[[Stars and Stripes (newspaper)|Stars and Stripes]]}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Garnett |first=Benjamin |date=January 21, 2022 |title=Guest columnist: Time to join military or go to jail is over |url=https://www.state-journal.com/opinion/guest-columnist-time-to-join-military-or-go-to-jail-is-over/article_4d29ce28-7926-11ec-9399-3389a56455a2.html |access-date=June 23, 2024 |website=[[The State Journal (Kentucky)]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Last meal]] requests do not have to be fulfilled.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=David |date=October 30, 2014 |title=Death Row Inmate Asks for a Child As His Last Meal, Texas DOC Plan to Grant Request? |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/texas-two-misstep/ |access-date=June 25, 2024 |website=[[Snopes]]}}</ref></noinclude> States have various restrictions on what can be requested, up to not permitting them at all.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Beam |first=Christopher |date=November 10, 2009 |title=I'll Have 24 Tacos and the Filet Mignon |url=https://slate.com/news-and-politics/2009/11/can-a-prisoner-request-anything-for-his-last-meal.html |access-date=June 25, 2024 |work=[[Slate (magazine)|Slate]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* Although popularly known as the "red telephone", the [[Moscow–Washington hotline]] was never a telephone line, nor were red phones used. The first implementation of the hotline used [[Teleprinter|teletype]] equipment, which was replaced by facsimile (fax) machines in 1988. Since 2008, the hotline has been a secure computer link over which the two countries exchange email.<noinclude><ref name="richardson">Paul E. Richardson, "The hot line (is a Hollywood myth)", in: ''Russian Life'', September/October issue 2009, pp. 50–59.</ref></noinclude> Moreover, the hotline links the [[Moscow Kremlin|Kremlin]] to the [[The Pentagon|Pentagon]], not the [[White House]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Clavin |first=Tom |title=There Never Was Such a Thing as a Red Phone in the White House |date=June 18, 2013 |journal=[[Smithsonian (magazine)|Smithsonian]] |url=http://www.smithsonianmag.com/history/there-never-was-such-a-thing-as-a-red-phone-in-the-white-house-1129598/ |access-date=September 21, 2014 |archive-date=November 10, 2017 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171110003236/https://www.smithsonianmag.com/history/there-never-was-such-a-thing-as-a-red-phone-in-the-white-house-1129598/ |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||date=December 13, 2019 |title=Jimi Hendrix cleared of blame for UK parakeet release |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/uk-england-50755015 |access-date=June 26, 2024 |work=[[BBC]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* Likewise, the [[nuclear football]], the briefcase used by presidents to launch nuclear attacks, does not contain a [[Nuclear button|large red button]] to launch an attack. Rather, its primary use is to confirm the president's identity, and to facilitate communication with [[the Pentagon]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Kaplan |first=Fred |date=February 11, 2021 |title=How Close Did the Capitol Rioters Get to the Nuclear "Football"? |url=https://slate.com/news-and-politics/2021/02/nuclear-football-vice-president-pence.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240514011723/https://slate.com/news-and-politics/2021/02/nuclear-football-vice-president-pence.html |archive-date=May 14, 2024 |access-date=June 25, 2024 |work=[[Slate (magazine)|Slate]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Dobbs |first=Michael |date=October 2014 |title=The Real Story of the "Football" That Follows the President Everywhere |url=https://www.smithsonianmag.com/history/real-story-football-follows-president-everywhere-180952779/ |access-date=June 25, 2024 |work=[[Smithsonian (magazine)|Smithsonian]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Craw |first=Victoria |date=January 4, 2018 |title=The nuclear button: Real or fake news? |url=https://www.nzherald.co.nz/world/the-nuclear-button-real-or-fake-news/HTBD2HA4576V6TASNVQQLMCLRE/ |access-date=June 25, 2024 |work=[[The New Zealand Herald]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Twinkies]] were not [[Twinkie defense|claimed to be the cause]] of San Francisco mayor [[George Moscone]]'s and supervisor [[Harvey Milk]]'s murders. In the trial of [[Dan White]], the defense successfully argued White's diminished capacity as a result of depression. While eating Twinkies was cited as evidence of this depression, it was never claimed to be the cause of the murders.<noinclude><ref name="Twinkie">{{#invoke:cite news||first=Carol |last=Pogash |title=Myth of the 'Twinkie defense' |url=http://www.sfgate.com/cgi-bin/article.cgi?f=/c/a/2003/11/23/INGRE343501.DTL |newspaper=[[San Francisco Chronicle]] |page=D-1 |date=November 23, 2003 |access-date=March 20, 2007 |archive-date=June 11, 2012 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120611032604/http://www.sfgate.com/cgi-bin/article.cgi?f=%2Fc%2Fa%2F2003%2F11%2F23%2FINGRE343501.DTL |url-status=live |quote=The "Twinkie defense" is so ingrained in our culture that it appears in law dictionaries, in sociology textbooks, in college exams and in more than 2, 800 references on Google. Only a few of them call it what it is: a myth.}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=David |date=October 30, 1999 |title=The Twinkie Defense: Debunking the Myths and Misinformation |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/the-twinkie-defense/ |access-date=June 18, 2024 |quote="Twinkie defense" is now a widespread and commonly-recognized term. It is also a term based on something that never happened.}}</ref></noinclude>
* Neither the [[Italian-American Mafia|Mafia]] nor other criminal organizations regularly use or have used [[cement shoes]] to drown their victims.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||author=Colleen Long |date=May 5, 2016 |title=Cops seek killer of man who washed ashore in 'cement shoes' |url=https://philadelphia.cbslocal.com/2016/05/05/cops-seek-killer-of-man-who-washed-ashore-in-cement-shoes/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220518100829/https://philadelphia.cbslocal.com/2016/05/05/cops-seek-killer-of-man-who-washed-ashore-in-cement-shoes/ |archive-date=May 18, 2022 |access-date=August 11, 2018 |work=[[CBS 3 Philadelphia]] |agency=[[Associated Press]]}}</ref></noinclude> There are only two documented cases of this method being used in murders: one in 1964 and one in 2016 (although, in the former, [[Ernest Rupolo|the victim]] had concrete blocks tied to his legs rather than being enclosed in cement).<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=May 5, 2016 |title='Cement shoes' found on NYC corpse |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-36215804#:~:text=%22Cement%20shoes%22%20as%20they%20are,was%20a%20known%20gang%20member. |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230403234806/https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-36215804#:~:text=%22Cement%20shoes%22%20as%20they%20are,was%20a%20known%20gang%20member. |archive-date=April 3, 2023 |access-date=August 5, 2021 |work=[[BBC News]]}}</ref></noinclude> The French Army did use cement shoes on Algerians killed in [[death flights]] during the [[Algerian War]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=November 20, 2012 |title=Après deux ans de polémique, l'État "enterre" le général Bigeard |url=https://www.france24.com/fr/20121120-polemique-cendres-encore-brulantes-general-bigeard-reposeront-frejus-algerie-torture-indochine |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220706010636/http://www.france24.com/fr/20121120-polemique-cendres-encore-brulantes-general-bigeard-reposeront-frejus-algerie-torture-indochine |archive-date=July 6, 2022 |access-date=June 25, 2022 |website=[[France 24]] |language=fr}}</ref></noinclude>
* Embalming is not legally required in the United States.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=Barbara |date=June 9, 1999 |title=Have People Been Buried Alive? |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/just-dying-to-get-out/ |website=[[Snopes]]}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Slominski |first=Elena |date=August 29, 2023 |title=Life of the death system: shifting regimes, evolving practices, and the rise of eco-funerals |journal=Sustainability: Science, Practice and Policy |volume=19 |issue=1 |page=7 |doi=10.1080/15487733.2023.2243779 |doi-access=free |bibcode=2023SSPP...1943779S }}</ref></noinclude> The [[Federal Trade Commission]] passed a rule in 1984 forbidding making this claim, to prevent the funeral industry from promoting the misconception for financial gain.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Chiappelli |first1=Jeremiah |last2=Chiappelli |first2=Ted |date=December 2008 |title=Drinking Grandma: The Problem of Embalming |journal=Journal of Environmental Health |volume=71 |issue=5 |pages=25–26 |jstor=26327817 |pmid=19115720 }}</ref></noinclude>

=== Literature ===
{{Main|q:Misquotations|l1 = Wikiquote:Misquotations}}
* Many quotations are incorrect or attributed to people who never uttered them, and quotations from obscure or unknown authors are often attributed to more famous figures. Commonly misquoted individuals include [[Mark Twain]], [[Albert Einstein]], [[Adolf Hitler]], [[Winston Churchill]], [[Abraham Lincoln]], [[William Shakespeare]], [[Bill Gates]], [[Steve Jobs]], [[Confucius]], [[Sun Tzu]], and the [[Buddha]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last1=Knowles |first1=Elizabeth |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=jxFQqDLav6wC |title=What They Didn't Say: A Book of Misquotations |date=October 26, 2006 |publisher=OUP Oxford |isbn=978-0-19-150054-1 |language=en |access-date=January 26, 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240523005717/https://books.google.com/books?id=jxFQqDLav6wC |archive-date=May 23, 2024 |url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Mary Shelley]]'s 1818 novel ''[[Frankenstein]]'' is named after the fictional scientist [[Victor Frankenstein]], who created the sapient creature in the novel, not the creature itself, which is never named in the novel and is now usually called [[Frankenstein's monster]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||date=September 12, 2018 |title=200th anniversary of Mary Shelley's Frankenstein |url=https://anulib.anu.edu.au/news-events/news/200th-anniversary-mary-shelleys-frankenstein |access-date=June 22, 2024 |work=[[Australian National University]]}}</ref></noinclude> However, as later adaptations started to refer to the monster itself as Frankenstein, this usage became well-established, and some no longer regard it as erroneous.<noinclude><ref name=Evans>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Evans|first=Bergen|author-link=Bergen Evans|title=Comfortable Words|quote=All dictionaries now recognize "a Frankenstein" as any monstrous creation that threatens to destroy its creator.|url=https://archive.org/details/comfortablewords00evan|url-access=registration|date=1962|location=New York City|publisher=[[Random House]]}}</ref><ref name=Garner>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Garner|first=Bryan A.|title=A dictionary of modern American usage|date=1998|publisher=Oxford University Press|location=New York|isbn=978-0-19-507853-4|url=https://archive.org/details/dictionaryofmode00garn |quote=Today this ubiquitous usage must be accepted as standard}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Ernest Hemingway]] did not author the [[flash fiction]] story "[[For sale: baby shoes, never worn]]".<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Haglund |first=David |date=January 31, 2013 |title=Did Hemingway Really Write His Famous Six-Word Story? |url=https://slate.com/culture/2013/01/for-sale-baby-shoes-never-worn-hemingway-probably-did-not-write-the-famous-six-word-story.html |access-date=June 23, 2024 |website=[[Slate (magazine)|Slate]]}}</ref></noinclude> The story was not attributed to him until decades after he died.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Churchwell |first=Sarah |date=June 23, 2019 |title=For sale, baby shoes, never worn — the myth of Ernest Hemingway's short story |url=https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/for-sale-baby-shoes-never-worn-the-myth-of-ernest-hemingways-short-story-pws8jz6qh |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230405045819/https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/for-sale-baby-shoes-never-worn-the-myth-of-ernest-hemingways-short-story-pws8jz6qh |archive-date=April 5, 2023 |access-date=April 5, 2023 |website=The Times}}</ref></noinclude>

=== Music ===
{{See also|Mondegreen#In songs}}

==== Classical music ====
* The [[Interval (music)|musical interval]] [[tritone]] was not banned by the Catholic Church and was not associated with devils during the Middle Ages.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Sorensen |first=Jon |date=February 10, 2014 |title=Did the Vatican Outlaw "The Devil In Music?" |url=https://www.catholic.com/magazine/online-edition/did-the-vatican-outlaw-the-devil-in-music |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220708145933/https://www.catholic.com/magazine/online-edition/did-the-vatican-outlaw-the-devil-in-music |archive-date=July 8, 2022 |access-date=July 8, 2022 |website=[[Catholic Answers]]}}</ref><ref>{{cite journal |last1=Smith |first1=F. J. |title=Some aspects of the tritone and the semitritone in the ''Speculum Musicae'': the non-emergence of the ''diabolus in musica'' |journal=Journal of Musicological Research |date=1979 |volume=3 |issue=1–2 |pages=63–74 [70] |doi=10.1080/01411897908574507}}</ref></noinclude> Early medieval music used the tritone in Gregorian chant for certain modes.<noinclude><ref name="Grove">{{cite encyclopedia |year=2001 |title=Tritone |encyclopedia=[[Grove Music Online]] |publisher=[[Oxford University Press]] |location=Oxford |url=https://www.oxfordmusiconline.com/grovemusic/view/10.1093/gmo/9781561592630.001.0001/omo-9781561592630-e-0000028403 |last=Drabkin |first=William |doi=10.1093/gmo/9781561592630.article.28403 |isbn=978-1-56159-263-0 |url-access=subscription |access-date=May 23, 2024 |archive-date=May 23, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240523005715/https://www.oxfordmusiconline.com/grovemusic/display/10.1093/gmo/9781561592630.001.0001/omo-9781561592630-e-0000028403 |url-status=live}} {{Grove Music subscription}}</ref></noinclude> [[Guido of Arezzo]] ({{circa|991|1033}}) was the first theorist to discourage the interval.<noinclude><ref name="Grove" />
* [[Death of Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart|Mozart did not die from poisoning]], and was not poisoned by his colleague [[Antonio Salieri]] or anyone else.<ref>{{Cite book| edition = 1st| publisher = [[HarperCollins]]| isbn = 978-0-06-019046-0| last = Solomon| first = Maynard| author-link = Maynard Solomon| title = Mozart: A Life| location = New York| year = 1995| url = https://archive.org/details/mozartlife0002solo| url-access = registration| oclc = 31435799|page=587}}</ref> The rumor originated soon after Salieri's death and was dramatized in [[Alexander Pushkin]]'s play ''[[Mozart and Salieri (play)|Mozart and Salieri]]'' (1832), and later in the 1979 play ''[[Amadeus (play)|Amadeus]]'' by [[Peter Shaffer]] and the subsequent 1984 film ''[[Amadeus (film)|Amadeus]]''.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Was Mozart actually poisoned by Salieri? |url=https://www.classicfm.com/composers/mozart/guides/did-salieri-murder-mozart-mythbuster/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230403230244/https://www.classicfm.com/composers/mozart/guides/did-salieri-murder-mozart-mythbuster/ |archive-date=April 3, 2023 |access-date=April 12, 2021 |website=Classic fm}}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[minuet in G major, BWV Anh. 114|minuet in G major]] by [[Christian Petzold (composer)|Christian Petzold]] is commonly attributed to [[Johann Sebastian Bach]], although the piece was identified in the 1970s as a movement from a harpsichord suite by Petzold. The misconception stems from ''[[Notebook for Anna Magdalena Bach]]'', a book of sheet music by various composers (mostly Bach) in which the minuet is found.<noinclude><ref>a. {{Cite Grove |last=Wolff |first=Christoph |title=Bach. III. 7. Johann Sebastian Bach. Works}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Williams |first=Peter F. |title=J.S. Bach: A Life in Music |publisher=[[Cambridge University Press]] |year=2007 |page=158}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Schulenberg |first=David |title=The Keyboard Music of J.S. Bach |year=2006 |page=448}}
<br />d. {{#invoke:cite journal||last=Schulze |first=Hans-Joachim |author-link=Hans-Joachim Schulze |year=1979 |title=Ein 'Dresdner Menuett' im zweiten Klavierbüchlein der Anna Magdalena Bach. Nebst Hinweisen zur Überlieferung einiger Kammermusikwerke Bachs. |journal=[[Bach-Jahrbuch]] |volume=65 |pages=45-64, 54-58, 64 |doi=10.13141/bjb.v19791376}}</ref></noinclude> Compositions that are doubtful as works of Bach are cataloged as "[[BWV Anh.]]", short for "[[Bach-Werke-Verzeichnis]] Anhang" ("Bach works catalogue annex"); the minuet is assigned to BWV Anh. 114.
* [[Mozart effect|Listening to Mozart]] or classical music does not enhance intelligence (or [[IQ]]). A study from 1993 reported a short-term improvement in [[Spatial visualization ability|spatial reasoning]].<noinclude><ref name="Rauscher-Shaw-Ky-1993">{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Rauscher|first1=Frances H.|last2=Shaw|first2=Gordon L.|last3=Ky|first3=Catherine N.|year=1993|title=Music and spatial task performance|url=http://www.uwosh.edu/psychology/faculty-and-staff/frances-rauscher-ph.d/Rauscher_ShawKy_1993.pdf/view|journal=[[Nature (journal)|Nature]]|volume=365|issue=6447|page=611|doi=10.1038/365611a0|pmid=8413624|bibcode=1993Natur.365..611R|s2cid=1385692|access-date=May 23, 2024|archive-date=January 23, 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210123151744/https://www.uwosh.edu/psychology/faculty-and-staff/frances-rauscher-ph.d/Rauscher_ShawKy_1993.pdf/view}}</ref><ref name="pryse-phillips">{{#invoke:cite book||title=Companion to Clinical Neurology |author=William Pryse-Phillips |year=2003 |isbn=0-19-515938-1 |publisher=Oxford University Press}}, p. 611 defines the term as "Slight and transient improvement in spational[sic] reasoning skills detected in normal subjects as a result of exposure to the music of Mozart, specifically his sonata for two pianos (K448)."</ref></noinclude> However, the weight of subsequent evidence supports either a null effect or short-term effects related to increases in mood and arousal, with mixed results published after the initial report in ''Nature''.<noinclude><ref name="bridgett">{{#invoke:cite journal||title=Effects of listening to Mozart and Bach on the performance of a mathematical test |pmid=10939064|author1=Bridgett, D.J. |author2=Cuevas, J.|journal=Perceptual and Motor Skills |volume=90|issue=3 Pt 2|year=2000 |pages=1171–1175 |doi=10.2466/pms.2000.90.3c.1171|s2cid=35762220}}</ref><ref name="thompson">{{#invoke:cite journal||author1=Thompson, W.F. |author2=Schellenberg, E.G. |author3=Husain, G. |title=Arousal, mood, and the Mozart effect |journal=Psychological Science |volume=12|issue=3|pages=248–251 |pmid=11437309|year=2001|doi=10.1111/1467-9280.00345 |s2cid=17641225}}</ref><ref name="JonesWest2006">{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Jones|first1=Martin H.|last2=West |first2=Stephen D.|last3=Estell|first3=David B. |title=The Mozart effect: Arousal, preference, and spatial performance |journal=Psychology of Aesthetics, Creativity, and the Arts |volume=S|issue=1|year=2006|pages=26–32|doi=10.1037/1931-3896.S.1.26}}</ref><ref name="Steele2000">{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Steele |first1=Kenneth M.|title=Arousal and mood factors in the "Mozart effect"|journal=Perceptual and Motor Skills|volume=91|issue=1 |year=2000|pages=188–190 |doi=10.2466/pms.2000.91.1.188|pmid=11011888|s2cid=21977655 |url=http://www1.appstate.edu/~kms//documents/Arousal.pdf |access-date=2015-11-04|archive-date=2017-01-06|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170106155327/http://www1.appstate.edu/~kms/documents/Arousal.pdf}}</ref></noinclude>

* The "[[Minute Waltz]]" takes, on average, two minutes to play as originally written.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||author1=Frédéric Chopin |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=0jQ5lDhToBQC&pg=PR6 |title=Piano works |author2=Joseph Banowetz |publisher=Alfred Music Publishing |year=2000 |isbn=978-0-7692-9854-2 |page=6 |access-date=October 2, 2010}}</ref></noinclude> Its name comes from the adjective ''[[wikt:minute#Adjective|minute]]'', meaning "small", and not the noun spelled the same.<noinclude><ref name="Hinson2004">{{#invoke:cite book||author=Maurice Hinson|title=The Pianist's Dictionary|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=ov6znsHlhboC&pg=PA114|access-date=October 2, 2010|year=2004|publisher=Indiana University Press|isbn=978-0-253-21682-3|page=114|quote=This piece bears an erroneous nickname since the story long associated with this nickname presumes the pianist is supposed to play the piece in one minute. The word "minute" means small or little waltz.}}</ref></noinclude>

==== Popular music ====
* "[[Edelweiss (song)|Edelweiss]]" is not the national anthem of Austria, but an original composition created for the 1959 musical ''[[The Sound of Music]]''.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=How Do You Solve a Problem Like Maria? |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/pressoffice/pressreleases/stories/2006/07_july/11/maria_facts.shtml |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140427083144/http://www.bbc.co.uk/pressoffice/pressreleases/stories/2006/07_july/11/maria_facts.shtml |archive-date=April 27, 2014}} BBC.</ref></noinclude> The Austrian national anthem is "[[Land der Berge, Land am Strome]]" ("Land of the Mountains, Land by the River [<nowiki/>[[Danube]]]").<noinclude><ref name="Vilain2010">{{#invoke:cite book||last=Vilain|first=Robert|author-link=Robert Vilain|title=Words and Music|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=9gNrhgXpPyYC&pg=PA24|year=2010|publisher=MHRA|isbn=978-1-907322-08-2|pages=24, 28|access-date=May 14, 2017|archive-date=January 21, 2023|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230121033602/https://books.google.com/books?id=9gNrhgXpPyYC&pg=PA24|url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[The Beatles]]' 1965 appearance at [[Shea Stadium]] was not the first time that a rock concert was played at a large, outdoor sports stadium in the United States; such venues were employed by [[Elvis Presley]] in the 1950s and the Beatles themselves in 1964.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last1=Krell |first1=David |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=p9f9DwAAQBAJ&pg=PT208 |title=The New York Mets in Popular Culture: Critical Essays |publisher=McFarland |year=2020 |isbn=978-1-4766-8010-1 |access-date=May 23, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240523005712/https://books.google.com/books?id=p9f9DwAAQBAJ&pg=PT208#v=onepage&q&f=false |archive-date=May 23, 2024 |url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[The Monkees]] did not outsell the Beatles' and [[the Rolling Stones]]' combined record sales in 1967. [[Michael Nesmith]] originated the claim in a 1977 interview as a prank.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||date=September 18, 2017 |title=In 1977 Mike Nesmith Fooled the World: When The Monkees Sold More Records Than The Beatles and Rolling Stones Combined |url=https://flashbak.com/in-1977-mike-nesmith-fooled-the-world-when-the-monkees-sold-more-records-than-the-beatles-and-rolling-stones-combined-386535/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180620102100/https://flashbak.com/in-1977-mike-nesmith-fooled-the-world-when-the-monkees-sold-more-records-than-the-beatles-and-rolling-stones-combined-386535/ |archive-date=June 20, 2018 |access-date=November 9, 2017 |work=Flashbak |language=en-US}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[The Rolling Stones]] were not performing "[[Sympathy for the Devil]]" at the 1969 [[Altamont Free Concert]] when [[Killing of Meredith Hunter|Meredith Hunter]] was stabbed to death by a member of the local [[Hells Angels]] chapter that was serving as security. The stabbing occurred later as the band was performing "[[Under My Thumb]]".<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Cruickshank |first=Douglas |date=January 14, 2002 |title=Sympathy for the Devil |url=http://www.salon.com/2002/01/14/sympathy/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160303203823/http://www.salon.com/2002/01/14/sympathy/ |archive-date=March 3, 2016 |access-date=June 25, 2006 |website=Salon.com}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine |last=Burks |first=John |date=February 7, 1970 |title=Rock & Roll's Worst Day |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/news/story/5934386/rock__rolls_worst_day |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090422123137/http://www.rollingstone.com/news/story/5934386/rock__rolls_worst_day |archive-date=April 22, 2009 |access-date=September 13, 2008 |magazine=Rolling Stone}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Concept album]]s did not begin with rock music in the 1960s. The format had already been employed by singers such as [[Frank Sinatra]] in the 1940s and 1950s.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Elicker |first=Martina |title=Word and Music Studies: Essays on the Song Cycle and on Defining the Field |publisher=Rodopi |year=2001 |isbn=978-90-420-1565-4 |pages=231–234 |chapter=Concept Albums: Song Cycles in Popular Music |chapter-url=https://books.google.com/books?id=tVPFUS7FIAQC&pg=PA227}}

b. {{#invoke:cite book||last=McKnight-Trontz |first=Jennifer |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=SRvQ8odl3RYC |title=Exotiquarium: Album Art from the Space Age |publisher=St. Martin's Press |year=1999 |isbn=978-0-312-20133-3}}

c. {{cite AV media notes |title=In the Wee Small Hours |first=Pete |last=Welding |publisher=Capitol Records, 1998 CD release.}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Cass Elliot]] (of [[The Mamas & the Papas]]) did not die from choking on a ham sandwich.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news|| url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/entertainment-arts-68949240 | title=Mama Cass 'didn't choke to death on a ham sandwich', daughter says | work=BBC News | date=May 6, 2024 }}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news|| url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/world-news/2024/05/06/mama-cass-didnt-choke-to-death-on-ham-sandwich/ | title=Mama Cass 'didn't choke to death' on ham sandwich | newspaper=The Telegraph | date=May 6, 2024 | vauthors = Barton A }}</ref></noinclude> This falsehood was initiated by her manager who wanted to avoid the implication that her death was associated with substance abuse.<noinclude><ref name="Zoladz">{{#invoke:cite web||last=Zoladz|first=Lindsay|title=Cass Elliot's Death Spawned a Horrible Myth. She Deserves Better.|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2024/05/09/arts/music/cass-elliot-mamas-and-the-papas-death.html|work=New York Times|date=May 9, 2024}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Phil Collins]] did not write his 1981 hit "[[In the Air Tonight]]" about witnessing someone drowning and then confronting the person in the audience who let it happen. According to Collins himself, it was about his emotions when divorcing from his first wife.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||title=Fact Check: In the Air Tonight |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/in-the-air-tonight/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20211226154058/https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/in-the-air-tonight/ |archive-date=December 26, 2021 |access-date=August 8, 2019 |website=[[Snopes]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* Popular musicians are not more likely to die at the age of 27. The notion of a "[[27 Club]]" arose after the deaths, in a ten-month period, of [[Jimi Hendrix]], [[Janis Joplin]], and [[Jim Morrison]], and later the deaths of [[Kurt Cobain]] and [[Amy Winehouse]]. Statistical studies have shown that there is no scientific basis for this idea.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||first=Jack |last=Butler |date=July 7, 2021 |url=https://www.nationalreview.com/2021/07/the-myth-of-the-27-club/ |title=The Myth of the 27 Club |work=National Review |access-date=July 4, 2024}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||first=Kelsey |last=McKinney |date=May 23, 2015 |url=https://www.vox.com/2015/3/23/8277271/27-club-real-myth |title=Despite the Huge Myth, Musicians Don't Die at 27 — They Die at 56 |work=Vox |access-date=July 4, 2024}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||first=Arun |last=Starkey |date=October 4, 2021 |url=https://faroutmagazine.co.uk/debunking-the-myths-of-the-27-club/ |title=Debunking the Central Myths of the '27 Club' |work=Far Out Magazine |access-date=July 4, 2024}}</ref></noinclude>
* The song "[[Puff, the Magic Dragon]]" is not about drugs. Both of the song's co-writers consistently and emphatically denied this interpretation throughout their lives, stating that the song is solely about the loss of childhood innocence.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url = http://www.chronogram.com/hudsonvalley/puff-still-not-a-drug-song/Content?oid=2169725 |title = Puff: Still Not a Drug Song |work = Chronogram }}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url = https://www.cnn.com/2025/01/07/entertainment/peter-yarrow-dies-at-86/index.html |title = Peter Yarrow of folk-music trio Peter, Paul and Mary dies at 86 |agency = Associated Press |publisher = CNN |date = January 7, 2025 |access-date = January 7, 2025 }}</ref></noinclude>

=== Religion ===
==== Buddhism ====
{{#invoke:multiple image||
| align             = right
| direction         = horizontal
| image1            = Buddha in Sarnath Museum (Dhammajak Mutra).jpg
| caption1          = Statue of the [[Buddha]] (Siddhartha Gautama)
| image2            = Budai Heshang (37007250780).jpg
