| image3            = Emaciated Siddhartha Fasting Gautama Buddha.jpg
| caption3          = Statue of emaciated [[Siddhartha Gautama]] ascetic, often incorrectly referred to as the "Buddha"
}}
* The chubby, bald monk with lengthened ears who is often depicted laughing, known as the "fat Buddha" or "laughing Buddha" in the West, is not the actual Buddha, but a 10th-century Chinese Buddhist folk hero by the name of [[Budai]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last1=Peterson |first1=Christopher |title=When Did the Buddha Become Fat? |url=https://www.psychologytoday.com/us/blog/the-good-life/201207/when-did-the-buddha-become-fat |website=Psychology Today |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240523005739/https://www.psychologytoday.com/us/blog/the-good-life/201207/when-did-the-buddha-become-fat |archive-date=May 23, 2024 |access-date=November 1, 2018}}</ref></noinclude> The [[Gautama Buddha|historical Buddha]], Siddhartha Gautama, who lived in the 5th century BC, is most often depicted in normal weight and concentrated in meditation.


==== Christianity ====
* Jesus was most likely not born on December 25, when [[nativity of Jesus|his birth]] is traditionally celebrated as Christmas. It is more likely that his birth was in either the season of spring or perhaps summer. Although the [[Common Era]] ostensibly counts the years since the birth of Jesus,<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Bromiley |first=Geoffrey W. |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=BW_1mt4oebQC&q=jesus+birth+year+before&pg=PA686 |title=The International Standard Bible Encyclopedia |publisher=Wm. B. Eerdmans Publishing |year=1995 |isbn=978-0-8028-3781-3 |access-date=May 18, 2011 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240523010259/https://books.google.com/books?id=BW_1mt4oebQC&q=jesus+birth+year+before&pg=PA686#v=snippet&q=jesus%20birth%20year%20before&f=false |archive-date=May 23, 2024 |url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude> it is unlikely that he was born in either AD 1 or 1 BC, as such a numbering system would imply. Modern historians estimate a date closer to between 6 BC and 4 BC.<noinclude><ref name="JDG324">{{#invoke:cite book||last=Dunn |first=James DG |year=2003 |title=Jesus Remembered |url=https://archive.org/details/jesusrememberedc00jame |url-access=limited |publisher=Eerdmans Publishing |page=[https://archive.org/details/jesusrememberedc00jame/page/n342 324]}}</ref></noinclude>
* The Bible does not say that exactly three [[Biblical Magi|magi]] came to visit the baby Jesus, nor that they were kings, or rode on camels, or that their names were [[Caspar (magus)|Caspar]], [[Melchior (magus)|Melchior]], and [[Balthazar (magus)|Balthazar]], nor what color their skin was.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Boyle |first=Alan |date=December 19, 2006 |title=Revisiting the gospel truth |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/science/cosmic-log/revisiting-gospel-truth-flna6c10405991 |access-date=June 22, 2024 |work=[[NBC News]]}}</ref><ref>{{Cite magazine |last=Waxman |first=Olivia |date=December 29, 2020 |title=Here's What History Can Tell Us About the Magi |url=https://time.com/5923009/three-kings-wisemen-history-magi-bible/ |access-date=June 22, 2024 |magazine=[[Time (magazine)|Time]] |archive-date=February 6, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240206011530/https://time.com/5923009/three-kings-wisemen-history-magi-bible/ |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=David |date=November 7, 2000 |title=Fact Check: Three Wise Men |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/three-wise-men/ |access-date=June 22, 2024 |website=[[Snopes]]}}</ref></noinclude>{{Citation needed|date=June 2024|reason=Skin color not in sources}} Three magi are inferred because three gifts are described, but the Bible says only that there was more than one magus.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||author=Schiller, G. |title=Iconography of Christian Art (English translation from German) |date=1971 |publisher=Lund Humphries |isbn=978-0-85331-270-3 |volume=I |page=96}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Calvin |first=John |author-link=John Calvin |url=http://www.sacred-texts.com/chr/calvin/cc31/cc31027.htm |title=Calvin's Commentaries, Vol. 31: Matthew, Mark and Luke, Part I, tr. by John King |access-date=May 15, 2010 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080906104902/http://sacred-texts.com/chr/calvin/cc31/cc31027.htm |archive-date=September 6, 2008 |url-status=live}} Quote from Commentary on Matthew 2:1–6</ref><ref>Ashby, Chad. "[http://www.christianitytoday.com/history/holidays/christmas/magi-wise-men-or-kings-its-complicated.html Magi, Wise Men, or Kings? It's Complicated] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240523010219/https://www.christianitytoday.com/history/2016/december/magi-wise-men-or-kings-its-complicated.html |date=May 23, 2024 }}." ''Christianity Today'', December 16, 2016.</ref></noinclude>
[[File:Régnier Penitent Mary Magdalene.jpg|thumb|upright|No evidence supports [[Mary Magdalene]] having been a prostitute.<noinclude><ref name="Ehrman2006">{{#invoke:cite book||url=https://books.google.com/books?id=Tlvgp7WggvEC&q=Ehrman+%22to+you+as+apostles%22&pg=PA253|title=Peter, Paul, and Mary Magdalene: The Followers of Jesus in History and Legend|last=Ehrman|first=Bart D.|date=2006|publisher=Oxford University Press|isbn=978-0-19-530013-0|location=Oxford, England|pages=189–90|author-link=Bart D. Ehrman|access-date=October 18, 2020|archive-date=January 19, 2023|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230119174748/https://books.google.com/books?id=Tlvgp7WggvEC&q=Ehrman+%22to+you+as+apostles%22&pg=PA253|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="Spong 2006">{{#invoke:cite book||last=Spong |first=John Shelby |url=https://archive.org/details/B-001-024-524-ALL |title=The Sins of Scripture: Exposing the Bible's Texts of Hate to Reveal the God of Love |publisher=HarperOne |date=March 14, 2006 |isbn=978-0-06-077840-8 |page=108 |language=en}}</ref></noinclude>]]
* The idea that [[Mary Magdalene]] was a prostitute before she met Jesus is not found in the Bible or in any of the other earliest Christian writings. It has been a disputed doctrine in several theological traditions whether Mary Magdalene, [[Mary of Bethany]] (who [[Anointing of Jesus|anoints Jesus' feet]] in John 11:1–12),<noinclude><ref>{{bibleverse|John|11:1–12}}</ref></noinclude> and the unnamed "[[Jesus and the woman taken in adultery|sinful woman]]" who anoints Jesus' feet in Luke 7:36–50<noinclude><ref>{{bibleverse|Luke|7:36–50}}</ref></noinclude> were the same woman.<noinclude><ref name="Ehrman2006" /><ref name="Spong 2006" /></noinclude>
* [[Paul the Apostle]]'s name was not changed from Saul. He was born a Jew, with [[Roman citizenship]] inherited from his father, and thus carried both a Hebrew and a Greco-Roman name from birth, as mentioned by [[Luke the Evangelist|Luke]] in Acts 13:9:<noinclude><ref>{{Bibleverse|Acts|13:9}}</ref></noinclude> "...Saul, who also is called Paul...".<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last1=Marrow |first1=Stanley B. |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=RPu1qx50HmgC&pg=PA5 |title=Paul: His Letters and His Theology: an Introduction to Paul's Epistles |publisher=Paulist Press |year=1986 |isbn=978-0-8091-2744-3 |pages=5, 7 |access-date=June 3, 2016 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230801152547/https://books.google.com/books?id=RPu1qx50HmgC&pg=PA5 |archive-date=August 1, 2023 |url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Why did God change Saul's name to Paul? |url=http://www.catholic.com/quickquestions/why-did-god-change-sauls-name-to-paul |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121030000303/http://www.catholic.com/quickquestions/why-did-god-change-sauls-name-to-paul |archive-date=October 30, 2012 |access-date=August 31, 2014 |website=Catholic Answers}}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[Catholic Church|Roman Catholic]] [[dogma]] of the [[Immaculate Conception]] is unrelated to the Christian doctrine that [[Mary, mother of Jesus|Mary]] [[Fertilisation|conceived]] and [[Virgin birth of Jesus|gave birth to Jesus while remaining a virgin]]. The Immaculate Conception is the belief that {{em|Mary}} was free of [[original sin]] from the moment of her own conception by her parents, [[Joachim]] and [[Saint Anne|Anne]]. A less common mistake is to think that the Immaculate Conception means that Mary herself was conceived without sexual intercourse.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=2009 |title=Religion & Ethics – Beliefs: The Immaculate Conception |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/christianity/beliefs/immaculateconception.shtml |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120124033136/http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/christianity/beliefs/immaculateconception.shtml |archive-date=January 24, 2012 |access-date=January 5, 2011 |publisher=BBC}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Hopko, Thomas. ''The Winter Pascha'' Chapter 9, Antiochian Orthodox Christian Archdiocese of North America |url=http://ww1.antiochian.org/node/18597 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210302142848/http://ww1.antiochian.org/node/18597 |archive-date=March 2, 2021 |access-date=May 23, 2024}}</ref></noinclude>
* Roman Catholic dogma does not say that the pope is either [[Impeccability#Impeccability and the Pope|sinless]] (as is commonly believed among non-Catholic Christians)<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Papal Infallibility |url=http://www.catholic.com/library/Papal_Infallibility.asp |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090606133529/http://www.catholic.com/library/Papal_Infallibility.asp |archive-date=June 6, 2009 |access-date=June 23, 2024 |website=[[Catholic Answers]]}}</ref></noinclude> or always infallible.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last1=MacDonald |first1=David |last2=Bonocore |first2=Mark |title=Is the Pope Sinless? |url=http://www.davidmacd.com/catholic/orthodox/pope_bishop_of_rome_primacy.htm#sinless |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110615202522/http://www.davidmacd.com/catholic/orthodox/pope_bishop_of_rome_primacy.htm#sinless |archive-date=June 15, 2011 |access-date=June 17, 2011 |work=The Pope, Bishop of Rome Catholic and Orthodox relations |publisher=CatholicBridge.com}}</ref></noinclude> Catholic dogma since 1870 does state that a [[divine revelation]] by the pope (generally called {{lang|la|[[ex cathedra]]}}) is free from error, but it does not hold that he is always free from error, even when speaking in his official capacity.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Catholic Encyclopedia: Beatification and Canonization |url=http://www.newadvent.org/cathen/02364b.htm |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180724145034/http://www.newadvent.org/cathen/02364b.htm |archive-date=July 24, 2018 |access-date=August 22, 2016 |website=www.newadvent.org}}</ref></noinclude>
* Members of [[the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints]] (LDS Church) [[Mormonism and polygamy|no longer practice polygamy]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||title=Utah Local News – Salt Lake City News, Sports, Archive |url=http://www.sltrib.com/sltrib/news/54959212-78/believe-bible-church-god.html.csp |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141006070652/http://www.sltrib.com/sltrib/news/54959212-78/believe-bible-church-god.html.csp |archive-date=October 6, 2014 |access-date=October 1, 2014 |newspaper=The Salt Lake Tribune}}
</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Religions – Mormon: Polygamy |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/mormon/socialvalues/polygamy.shtml |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141113021127/http://www.bbc.co.uk/religion/religions/mormon/socialvalues/polygamy.shtml |archive-date=November 13, 2014 |access-date=October 1, 2014 |publisher=BBC}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Mormon church explains polygamy in early days |url=http://bigstory.ap.org/article/mormon-church-explains-polygamy-early-days |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141006140330/http://bigstory.ap.org/article/mormon-church-explains-polygamy-early-days |archive-date=October 6, 2014 |access-date=October 1, 2014 |work=The Big Story}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Mormon Polygamy Misconceptions about Mormon Polygamy |url=http://mormon-polygamy.org/ |archive-url=https://archive.today/20130113111735/http://mormon-polygamy.org/ |archive-date=January 13, 2013 |access-date=October 1, 2014 |work=Mormon Polygamy}}</ref></noinclude> The Church excommunicates any members who practice polygamy within the organization.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||author=The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-Day Saints |title=Do Mormons practice polygamy? |url=http://www.mormon.org/faq/practice-of-polygamy |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141006084722/http://www.mormon.org/faq/practice-of-polygamy |archive-date=October 6, 2014 |access-date=October 1, 2014 |work=mormon.org}}</ref></noinclude> Some [[Mormon fundamentalist]] [[List of sects in the Latter Day Saint movement#Additional churches claiming lineage through Brigham Young and/or founded in the U.S. Intermountain West|sects]] do practice polygamy.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Current practice of polygamy in the Mormon movement |url=http://www.religioustolerance.org/lds_poly2.htm |url-status=live |archive-url=http://arquivo.pt/wayback/20090629085048/http://www.religioustolerance.org/lds_poly2.htm |archive-date=June 29, 2009 |access-date=October 1, 2014}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=March 14, 2014 |title=Modern Polygamy: Arizona Mormon Fundamentalists Seek to Shed Stereotypes |url=https://abcnews.go.com/US/modern-polygamy-arizona-mormon-fundamentalists-seek-shed-stereotypes/story?id=19322087 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141006124406/http://abcnews.go.com/US/modern-polygamy-arizona-mormon-fundamentalists-seek-shed-stereotypes/story?id=19322087 |archive-date=October 6, 2014 |access-date=October 1, 2014 |work=ABC News}}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[First Council of Nicaea]] did not establish the books of the Bible. The Old Testament had likely already been [[Development of the Hebrew Bible canon|established]] by Hebrew scribes before Christ. The [[development of the New Testament canon|development]] of the New Testament canon was mostly completed in the third century before the Nicaea Council was convened in 325;<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Roos |first=Dave |date=February 24, 2020 |title=Who Decided Which Books to Include in the Bible? |url=https://people.howstuffworks.com/books-of-bible.htm |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220829150311/https://people.howstuffworks.com/books-of-bible.htm |archive-date=August 29, 2022 |access-date=August 29, 2022 |website=HowStuffWorks |publisher=InfoSpace Holdings}}</ref></noinclude> it was finalized, along with the [[deuterocanon]], at the [[Council of Rome]] in 382.<noinclude><ref name="councilofrome">{{#invoke:cite book||url=http://www.oxfordreference.com/view/10.1093/acref/9780192802903.001.0001/acref-9780192802903 |title=The Oxford Dictionary of the Christian Church |date=2005-01-01 |publisher=Oxford University Press |isbn=978-0-19-280290-3 |editor-last=Cross |editor-first=F. L. |edition=3rd |page=282 |language=en |chapter=canon of Scripture |doi=10.1093/acref/9780192802903.001.0001 |access-date=September 5, 2022 |editor-last2=Livingstone |editor-first2=E. A. |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121001050958/http://www.oxfordreference.com/view/10.1093/acref/9780192802903.001.0001/acref-9780192802903 |archive-date=October 1, 2012 |url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Constantine the Great]] did not make Christianity the official religion of the Roman Empire. While he was the first Christian emperor and promoted religious tolerance with the [[Edict of Milan]], Christianity was not declared the official religion of the Roman Empire until AD 380, some 43 years after Constantine's death.<noinclude><ref name="Constantine Rhodes">{{#invoke:cite web|| url=https://sites.rhodes.edu/coins/romes-conversion-christianity-and-its-lasting-legacy | title=Rome's Conversion to Christianity and its Lasting Legacy &#124; Rhodes Sites | access-date=May 23, 2024 | archive-date=May 5, 2024 | archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240505182513/https://sites.rhodes.edu/coins/romes-conversion-christianity-and-its-lasting-legacy | url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="Constantine Cambridge">The Cambridge History of Christianity – Cambridge University Press "Christianity did not become the official religion of the empire under Constantine, as is often mistakenly claimed..." https://www.cambridge.org/core/books/abs/cambridge-history-of-christianity/constantine-and-the-peace-of-the-church/1D6492CD5ECB96174AAE1221F48DC56F {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240505174616/https://www.cambridge.org/core/books/abs/cambridge-history-of-christianity/constantine-and-the-peace-of-the-church/1D6492CD5ECB96174AAE1221F48DC56F |date=May 5, 2024 }}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[Seven Deadly Sins]] are never listed in the Bible. The concept originated with [[Tertullian]], and originally consisted of nine vices.<noinclude><ref>{{Cite web |title=The Seven Deadly Sins |url=https://www.catholic.com/magazine/print-edition/the-seven-deadly-sins |access-date=2023-09-30 |website=Catholic Answers |archive-date=August 8, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240808052301/https://www.catholic.com/magazine/print-edition/the-seven-deadly-sins |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude> This was later reduced to seven by [[Pope Gregory I|Gregory I]].<noinclude><ref>"For pride is the root of all evil, of which it is said, as Scripture bears witness; Pride is the beginning of all sin. [Ecclus. 10, 1] But seven principal vices, as its first progeny, spring doubtless from this poisonous root, namely, vain glory, envy, anger, melancholy, avarice, gluttony, lust." '''Gregory the Great, [http://www.lectionarycentral.com/GregoryMoralia/Book31.html Moralia in Iob, book XXXI] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210612234814/http://www.lectionarycentral.com/GregoryMoralia/Book31.html |date=June 12, 2021 }}'''</ref></noinclude>

==== Islam ====
{{#invoke:multiple image||
| align             = right
| direction         = vertical
| image1            = Group of Women Wearing Burkas.jpg
| caption1          = Afghan women wearing [[burqa]]s
| image2            = Niqab.jpg
| caption2          = Turkish women wearing [[niqāb]]s
| image3            = Turkish women 2x.jpg
| caption3          = Turkish women wearing [[hijab]]s
}}
* The [[burqa]] (also transliterated as burka or burkha) is often confused with other types of head-wear worn by Muslim women, particularly the [[niqāb]] and the [[hijab]]. A burqa covers the body, head, and face, with a mesh grille to see through. A niqab covers the hair and face, excluding the eyes. A hijab covers the hair and chest but not the face.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Vyver |first=James |date=March 7, 2014 |title=Explainer: Why do Muslim women wear a burka, niqab or hijab? |url=https://www.abc.net.au/news/2014-09-24/why-do-muslim-women-wear-a-burka-niqab-or-hijab/5761510 |access-date=June 17, 2024 |work=[[Australian Broadcasting Corporation]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* Not all Muslim women wear face or head coverings.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=July 26, 2017 |title=U.S. Muslims Concerned About Their Place in Society, But Continue to Belief in the American Dream |url=https://www.pewresearch.org/religion/2017/07/26/religious-beliefs-and-practices/ |access-date=June 17, 2024 |website=[[Pew Research Center]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* A [[fatwa]] is a generally non-binding legal opinion issued by an [[Ulama|Islamic scholar]] under [[Sharia|Islamic law]]; it is therefore commonplace for fatawa from different authors to disagree. The misconception that it is a death sentence stems from a decree issued by Ayatollah [[Ruhollah Khomeini]] of Iran in 1989 where he said that the author [[Salman Rushdie]] had earned a death sentence for [[blasphemy]]. It is debated whether this was a fatwa.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Isbister |first=William H. |date=November 23, 2002 |title=A "good" fatwa |journal=[[British Medical Journal]] |volume=325 |issue=7374 |page=1227 |doi=10.1136/bmj.325.7374.1227 |pmc=1124693}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Vultee |first=Fred |date=October 2006 |title=Fatwa on the Bunny |journal=Journal of Communication Inquiry |volume=30 |issue=4 |pages=319–336 |doi=10.1177/0196859906290919 |s2cid=143612009}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||title=In Depth: Islam, Fatwa FAQ |url=http://www.cbc.ca/news/background/islam/fatwa.html |publisher=CBC News Online |date=June 15, 2006|access-date=April 8, 2009 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110714091706/http://www.cbc.ca/news/background/islam/fatwa.html |archive-date=July 14, 2011 }}</ref></noinclude>
* The word ''[[jihad]]'' does not always mean '[[Religious war|holy war]]'; its literal meaning in Arabic is 'struggle'. While there is such a thing as [[Jihad#Greater and lesser jihad|jihad by the sword]], ''jihad'' can be any spiritual or moral effort or struggle,<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||first=Luke|last=Buckles|title=The Complete Idiot's Guide to World Religions|edition=3rd|page=157|publisher=Alpha|date=2004|isbn=978-1-59257-222-9|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=ZPokHByS3N0C|access-date=September 21, 2016|archive-date=November 1, 2023|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20231101145503/https://books.google.com/books?id=ZPokHByS3N0C|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||url=http://www.kuna.net.kw/NewsAgenciesPublicSite/ArticleDetails.aspx?id=1719934&Language=en|title=Western definition of "jihad" must be corrected – Italian expert|date=March 29, 2007|newspaper=[[Kuwait News Agency]] (KUNA)|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20111015041410/http://www.kuna.net.kw/NewsAgenciesPublicSite/ArticleDetails.aspx?id=1719934&Language=en|archive-date=October 15, 2011|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||title=Peace and the Limits of War: Transcending the Classical Conception of Jihad |first=Louay M. |last=Safi |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=1_PFEicd5LkC&pg=PP9 |publisher=[[International Institute of Islamic Thought]] |date=2003 |page=preface |isbn=978-1-56564-402-1 |access-date=September 21, 2016 |archive-date=January 21, 2023 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20230121033602/https://books.google.com/books?id=1_PFEicd5LkC&pg=PP9 |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude> such as seeking knowledge, putting others before oneself, and inviting others to Islam.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Hoque |first1=M. |last2=Jaim |first2=M. S. |last3=Mohamed |first3=Y. |title=The concept of jihad for education |journal=International Journal of Language and Education |date=30 March 2023 |volume=2 |issue=1 |pages=83–95 |doi=10.33102/alazkiyaa43 |url=https://azkiyaa.usim.edu.my/index.php/jurnal/article/view/43 |access-date=21 January 2024 |doi-access=free |archive-date=May 23, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240523010227/https://azkiyaa.usim.edu.my/index.php/jurnal/article/view/43 |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[Quran]] does not promise martyrs 72 virgins in heaven. It does mention that virgin female companions, [[houri]], are given to all people, martyr or not, in heaven, but no number is specified.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||author=al-Jalalayn|title=Tafsir Ar-Rahman|url=https://www.altafsir.com/Tafasir.asp?tMadhNo=1&tTafsirNo=74&tSoraNo=55&tAyahNo=74&tDisplay=yes&UserProfile=0&LanguageId=2|access-date=April 30, 2020|work=[[Tafsir al-Jalalayn]]|archive-date=March 8, 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210308002106/https://www.altafsir.com/Tafasir.asp?tMadhNo=1&tTafsirNo=74&tSoraNo=55&tAyahNo=74&tDisplay=yes&UserProfile=0&LanguageId=2|url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude> The source for the 72 virgins is a [[hadith]] in [[Sunan al-Tirmidhi]] by [[Imam Tirmidhi]].<noinclude><ref name="guardian72virgins">{{#invoke:cite news|| url=https://www.theguardian.com/books/2002/jan/12/books.guardianreview5|location=London |work=The Guardian|first=Ibn|last=Warraq|title=Virgins? What virgins?|date=January 12, 2002|archive-url =https://web.archive.org/web/20130622000632/http://www.guardian.co.uk/books/2002/jan/12/books.guardianreview5|archive-date=June 22, 2013| url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||title=Urban Terrorism: Myths and Realities|page= 33 |author=Anjali Nirmal |publisher=Pointer Publishers |date=2009 |isbn=978-81-7132-598-6|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=8EqWnqdsgZMC&pg=PA33}}</ref></noinclude> Hadiths are sayings and acts of [[Muhammad]] as reported by others, not part of the Quran itself.<noinclude><ref name="Salahuddin Yusuf">Salahuddin Yusuf, ''Riyadhus Salihin'', commentary on Nawawi, Chapter 372, Dar-us-Salam Publications (1999), {{ISBN|978-1-59144-053-6}}</ref><ref name="guardian72virgins" /></noinclude>

==== Judaism ====
[[File:Jan Brueghel de Oude en Peter Paul Rubens - Het aards paradijs met de zondeval van Adam en Eva.jpg|thumb|The fruit in the [[Garden of Eden]] is not named in the [[Book of Genesis]].]]
* The [[forbidden fruit]] mentioned in the [[Book of Genesis]] is never identified as an apple,<noinclude><ref name="Szpek">{{#invoke:cite book||author=Szpek, Heidi|title=Voices from the University: The Legacy of the Hebrew Bible|publisher=iUniverse|year=2002|isbn=978-0-595-25619-8|page=92}}</ref></noinclude> as widely depicted in Western art. The original Hebrew texts mention only ''fruit''.<noinclude><ref>[[Babylonian Talmud]], [[Berakhot (Talmud)|Berakhot]], 40a</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Adams |first=Cecil |date=November 24, 2006 |title=Was the forbidden fruit in the Garden of Eden an apple? |url=http://www.straightdope.com/columns/read/2682/was-the-forbidden-fruit-in-the-garden-of-eden-an-apple |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140401002830/http://www.straightdope.com/columns/read/2682/was-the-forbidden-fruit-in-the-garden-of-eden-an-apple |archive-date=April 1, 2014 |access-date=February 9, 2012 |website=The Straight Dope}}</ref></noinclude>
* While tattoos are forbidden by the [[Book of Leviticus]], Jews with tattoos are not [[Religious perspectives on tattooing#Judaism|barred from being buried in a Jewish cemetery]], just as violators of other prohibitions are not barred, as is commonly believed among American Jews.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Levine |first=Rabbi Menachem |date=October 7, 2018 |title=Judaism and Tattoos |work=aishcom |url=http://www.aish.com/jw/s/Judaism-and-Tattoos.html?s=authorart |access-date=December 12, 2018 |publisher=aish.com |archive-date=October 7, 2018 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181007223358/http://www.aish.com/jw/s/Judaism-and-Tattoos.html?s=authorart |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude>

=== Sports ===
* [[Artificial turf]] is not maintenance free. It requires regular maintenance, such as raking and patching, to keep it functional and safe.<noinclude><ref>{{cite journal |vauthors=Jastifer JR, McNitt AS, Mack CD, Kent RW, McCullough KA, Coughlin MJ, Anderson RB |title=Synthetic Turf: History, Design, Maintenance, and Athlete Safety |journal=Sports Health |volume=11 |issue=1 |pages=84–90 |date=2019 |pmid=30096021 |pmc=6299344 |doi=10.1177/1941738118793378 |type=Review}}</ref></noinclude>
* The name ''[[golf]]'' is not an acronym for "Gentlemen Only, Ladies Forbidden".<noinclude><ref name="golfsnopes">{{#invoke:cite news||last=Mikkelson |first=Barbara |date=May 18, 2010 |title=Golf: Gentlemen Only, Ladies Forbidden? |work=[[Snopes]] |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/golf-carte-2/ |access-date=June 23, 2022 |archive-date=June 23, 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220623214025/https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/golf-carte-2/ |url-status=live }}</ref><ref name="usga">{{#invoke:cite news||last=Jerris |first=Rand |title=FAQ – Golf History Questions |work=[[United States Golf Association]] |url=https://www.usga.org/history/faq--golf-history-questions-232994f0.html |access-date=June 23, 2022 |archive-date=September 4, 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220904025029/https://www.usga.org/history/faq--golf-history-questions-232994f0.html |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude> It may have come from the Dutch word ''kolf'' or ''kolve'', meaning "club",<noinclude><ref name="usga" /> or from the Scottish word ''goulf'' or ''gowf'' meaning "to strike or cuff".<noinclude><ref name="golfsnopes" />
* [[Origins of baseball|Baseball was not invented]] by [[Doubleday myth|Abner Doubleday]], nor did it originate in [[Cooperstown, New York]]. It is believed to have evolved from the bat-and-ball game [[rounders]] and first [[Knickerbocker Rules|took its modern form]] in New York City.<noinclude><ref>a. {{cite magazine |last=Cole |first=Diane |url=https://www.usnews.com/usnews/news/articles/060806/14ball.htm |title=Contrary to myth, baseball may have had no single inventor |magazine=U.S. News & World Report |date=October 4, 1990 |access-date=August 6, 2009 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131214105928/http://www.usnews.com/usnews/news/articles/060806/14ball.htm |archive-date=December 14, 2013}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite news||last=Fox|first=Butterfield|url=https://www.nytimes.com/1990/10/04/nyregion/cooperstown-hoboken-try-new-york-city.html|title=Cooperstown? Hoboken? Try New York City|work=The New York Times|date=October 4, 1990|access-date=April 3, 2009|archive-date=January 9, 2011|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110109170603/http://www.nytimes.com/1990/10/04/nyregion/cooperstown-hoboken-try-new-york-city.html|url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude>
[[File:Marcos black belt.jpg|thumb|150px|A [[BJJ belt|BJJ black belt]] with a red bar indicating first degree]]
* The [[black belt (martial arts)|black belt in martial arts]] does not necessarily indicate expert level.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=VanBlaricum |first=Michael |date=August 29, 2010 |title=Black Belt Realities |url=https://www.usadojo.com/black-belt-realities/ |access-date=June 24, 2024 |website=USADojo.com}}</ref></noinclude> It was introduced for [[judo]] in the 1880s to indicate competency at all of the basic techniques of the sport. Promotion beyond 1st [[dan (rank)|dan]] (the first black belt rank) varies among different martial arts.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://r25.jp/magazine/ranking_review/10002000/1112008051512.html|script-title=ja:柔道帯の最高位は、何と紅!? "紅帯"所持者に投げられてきた!|language=ja|publisher=R25.jp|date=May 15, 2008|access-date=November 11, 2008 |archive-url = https://archive.today/20080519163156/http://r25.jp/magazine/ranking_review/10002000/1112008051512.html |archive-date = May 19, 2008}}</ref></noinclude>
* The use of [[triangular corner flags in English football]] is not a privilege reserved for those teams that have won an [[FA Cup]] in the past, as depicted in a scene in the film ''[[Twin Town]]''. The [[Football Association]]'s rules are silent on the subject, and the decision over what shape flag to use has been up to the individual club's groundskeepers.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||first=Jack |last=Williams |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/02/17/sports/soccer/corner-flags-english-premier-league-champion.html |title=You Can Tell an F.A. Cup Champion by Its Corner Flags. Or Not. |newspaper=The New York Times |date=February 17, 2017 |access-date=April 8, 2018 |archive-date=January 25, 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200125100113/https://www.nytimes.com/2017/02/17/sports/soccer/corner-flags-english-premier-league-champion.html |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude>
* [[India men's national football team|India]] did not withdraw from the [[1950 FIFA World Cup]] because their squad wanted to play barefoot. In reality, India withdrew because the country's managing body, the [[All India Football Federation]] (AIFF), was insufficiently prepared for the team's participation.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last1=Adhikari |first1=Somak |title=No, India Did Not Withdraw From The 1950 FIFA World Cup Because They Did Not Want To Wear Shoes |url=https://www.indiatimes.com/sports/kick-off/why-did-india-withdraw-from-the-1950-world-cup-no-it-wasn-t-because-they-had-to-wear-shoes-258199.html |website=The Times of India |publisher=The Times Group |access-date=December 2, 2019 |date=June 6, 2018 |archive-date=January 25, 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200125100007/https://www.indiatimes.com/sports/kick-off/why-did-india-withdraw-from-the-1950-world-cup-no-it-wasn-t-because-they-had-to-wear-shoes-258199.html |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude>

=== Video games ===
* There is no definitive proof that [[Violence and video games#Scientific debate|violent video games cause people to become violent]]. Some studies have found no link between aggression and violent video games,<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=February 13, 2019 |title=Violent video games found not to be associated with adolescent aggression |url=https://www.ox.ac.uk/news/2019-02-13-violent-video-games-found-not-be-associated-adolescent-aggression |access-date=June 25, 2022 |website=[[University of Oxford]] |language=en |archive-date=June 25, 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220625163510/https://www.ox.ac.uk/news/2019-02-13-violent-video-games-found-not-be-associated-adolescent-aggression |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last1=Etchells |first1=Pete |date=April 6, 2019 |title=Five damaging myths about video games – let's shoot 'em up |work=[[The Guardian]] |url=https://www.theguardian.com/games/2019/apr/06/five-damaging-myths-about-video-games-lets-shoot-em-up |access-date=December 23, 2020}}</ref></noinclude> and the popularity of gaming has coincided with a ''decrease'' in youth violence.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Henry |first=Jenkins |title=Reality Bytes: Eight Myths About Video Games Debunked |url=https://www.pbs.org/kcts/videogamerevolution/impact/myths.html |access-date=December 23, 2020 |website=[[PBS]] |archive-date=August 26, 2004 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20040826014153/http://www.pbs.org/kcts/videogamerevolution/impact/myths.html |url-status=live }}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Misconceptions – Video Game Dissection |url=https://sites.psu.edu/videogamebreakdown/stereotypes/ |access-date=December 23, 2020 |website=[[Pennsylvania State University]]}}</ref></noinclude> The [[moral panic]] surrounding video games in the 1980s through to the 2020s, alongside several studies and incidents of violence and legislation in many countries, likely contributed to proliferating this idea.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Markey |first1=Patrick M. |last2=Ferguson |first2=Christopher J. |date=October 1, 2017 |title=Teaching Us to Fear: The Violent Video Game Moral Panic and the Politics of Game Research |url=https://www.journalofplay.org/sites/www.journalofplay.org/files/pdf-articles/10-1-Article-4-Teaching-us-to-fear.pdf |journal=[[American Journal of Play]] |pages=99–115 |access-date=December 23, 2020 |archive-date=June 29, 2021 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210629065109/https://www.journalofplay.org/sites/www.journalofplay.org/files/pdf-articles/10-1-Article-4-Teaching-us-to-fear.pdf }}</ref><ref name="NYTimes 20190805">{{#invoke:cite web||last=Draper |first=Kevin |date=August 5, 2019 |title=Video Games Aren't Why Shootings Happen. Politicians Still Blame Them. |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/08/05/sports/trump-violent-video-games-studies.html |access-date=August 22, 2019 |work=[[The New York Times]] |archive-date=April 26, 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200426031749/https://www.nytimes.com/2019/08/05/sports/trump-violent-video-games-studies.html |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude>
* The so-called "[[Nuclear Gandhi]]" glitch, in which peaceful leader [[Mahatma Gandhi]] would become unusually aggressive if [[democracy]] was adopted,<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Plunkett |first=Luke |title=Why Gandhi Is Such An Asshole In Civilization |url=https://kotaku.com/why-gandhi-is-such-an-asshole-in-civilization-1653818245 |website=[[Kotaku]] |date=February 3, 2016 |access-date=June 22, 2022 |language=en |archive-date=September 18, 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200918192554/https://kotaku.com/why-gandhi-is-such-an-asshole-in-civilization-1653818245 |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude> did not exist in either the original ''[[Civilization (video game)|Civilization]]'' game or ''[[Civilization II]]''. The games' designer [[Sid Meier]] attributed the origins of the rumor to both a [[TV Tropes]] thread and a [[Know Your Meme]] entry,<noinclude><ref name="memoir!">{{#invoke:cite book|| author = [[Sid Meier|Meier, Sid]] | chapter = Funny Business| chapter-url = | url = | title = Sid Meier's Memoir!: A Life in Computer Games|date = 2020 |publisher= [[W. W. Norton & Company|W. W. Norton]] | pages = 261–266| isbn = 978-1-324-00587-2}}</ref></noinclude> while [[Reddit]] and a ''[[Kotaku]]'' article helped popularize it.<noinclude><ref name="dtf probably myth">{{#invoke:cite web||url=https://dtf.ru/games/67979-pochemu-istoriya-o-bage-s-yadernym-gandi-v-civilization-skoree-vsego-vydumana |script-title=ru:Почему история о баге с «ядерным Ганди» в Civilization, скорее всего, выдумана |trans-title=Why the story about the "Nuclear Gandhi" bug in Civilization is likely fictional |author=Артемий Леонов |website={{ill|DTF (website)|lt=DTF.ru|ru|DTF}} |date=September 5, 2019 |language=ru |access-date=June 22, 2022 |archive-date=September 26, 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200926050823/https://dtf.ru/games/67979-pochemu-istoriya-o-bage-s-yadernym-gandi-v-civilization-skoree-vsego-vydumana |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude> Gandhi's supposed behavior did appear in the 2010 ''[[Civilization V]]''<noinclude><ref name="memoir!" /> as a joke, and in 2016's ''[[Civilization VI|VI]]''<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Jackson |first=Gina |url=https://kotaku.com/gandhi-is-still-an-asshole-in-civilization-vi-1788710568 |title=Gandhi Is Still An Asshole In Civilization VI |website=[[Kotaku]] |date=August 11, 2016 |access-date=June 22, 2022 |language=en |archive-date=September 18, 2020 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200918192556/https://kotaku.com/gandhi-is-still-an-asshole-in-civilization-vi-1788710568 |url-status=live }}</ref></noinclude> as a reference to the legend.
* The Japanese government did not pass a law banning [[Square Enix]] from releasing the ''[[Dragon Quest]]'' games on weekdays due to it causing too many schoolchildren to cut class. This rule is self-imposed by the developers themselves.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||first=Skrebels|last=Joe|date=April 22, 2020|title=How Dragon Quest Spawned an Urban Legend|url=https://www.ign.com/articles/how-dragon-quest-spawned-an-urban-myth|website=[[IGN]]|access-date=June 26, 2022|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220414195652/https://www.ign.com/articles/how-dragon-quest-spawned-an-urban-myth|archive-date=April 14, 2022}}</ref></noinclude>
* The release of ''[[Space Invaders]]'' in 1978 did not cause a shortage of [[100 yen coin|¥100 coins]] in [[Japan]]. An advertising campaign by [[Taito]] and an erroneous 1980 article in ''[[New Scientist]]'' are the sources of this claim.<noinclude><ref name="Numismatist">{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Paradis|first=Charles|date=March 2014|title=Insert Coin to Play: Space Invaders and the 100-Yen Myth|journal=[[The Numismatist]]|pages=46–48|publisher=[[American Numismatic Association]]|url=https://www.academia.edu/3672374|access-date=June 26, 2022|archive-date=October 21, 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221021083122/https://www.academia.edu/3672374|url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude>

=== Astronomy and spaceflight ===  <!-- NOTE: Headers are done this way so that the transclusion works. Please do not "fix" them. -->
* There is no scientific evidence that the motion of stars, planets, and other celestial bodies influences the fates of humans, and  [[Astrology and science|astrology]] has repeatedly been shown to have no explanatory power in predicting future events.<noinclude><ref name="Cosmic">{{#invoke:cite book||author1=Jeffrey Bennett |url=https://archive.org/details/astronomymediawo04lopr |title=The cosmic perspective |author2=Megan Donohue |author3=Nicholas Schneider |author4=Mark Voit |publisher=Pearson/Addison-Wesley |year=2007 |isbn=978-0-8053-9283-8 |edition=4th |location=San Francisco, CA |pages=[https://archive.org/details/astronomymediawo04lopr/page/82 82–84] |url-access=registration}}</ref><ref name="Carlson">{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Carlson |first=Shawn |year=1985 |title=A double-blind test of astrology |url=http://muller.lbl.gov/papers/Astrology-Carlson.pdf |journal=Nature |volume=318 |issue=6045 |pages=419–425 |bibcode=1985Natur.318..419C |doi=10.1038/318419a0 |s2cid=5135208}}</ref><ref name="Zarka">{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Zarka |first=Philippe |year=2011 |title=Astronomy and astrology |url=https://zenodo.org/record/890932 |journal=Proceedings of the International Astronomical Union |volume=5 |issue=S260 |pages=420–425 |bibcode=2011IAUS..260..420Z |doi=10.1017/S1743921311002602 |doi-access=free}}</ref></noinclude>
* Astronauts in orbit have the sensation of being [[weightlessness|weightless]] because they are in [[free fall]] around the Earth,<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web|| title=freefall | date=December 11, 2023 | quote=An astronaut orbiting Earth in a spacecraft experiences a condition of weightlessness because both the spacecraft and the astronaut are in free fall. |url=https://www.britannica.com/science/freefall-physics}}</ref></noinclude> not because they are so far away from the Earth that its gravitational pull is negligible. For example, on the [[International Space Station]] the Earth's gravity is nearly 90% as strong as at the surface. Objects orbiting in space would not remain in orbit if not for the gravitational force, and gravitational fields extend even into the depths of intergalactic space.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Oberg|first=James|author-link=James Oberg|date=May 1993|title=Space myths and misconceptions|url=http://www.jamesoberg.com/myth.html|url-status=live|journal=Omni|volume=15|issue=7|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20070927005829/http://www.jamesoberg.com/myth.html|archive-date=September 27, 2007|access-date=May 2, 2007}}</ref><ref name="nature1">{{#invoke:cite journal ||last1=Cowen |first1=Ron |title=Andromeda on collision course with the Milky Way |journal=Nature |date=31 May 2012 |doi=10.1038/nature.2012.10765 |s2cid=124815138 }}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||author=Chandler, David|date=May 1991|title=Weightlessness and Microgravity|url=http://www.lcurve.org/writings/PT-WeightlessnessAndMicrogravity.pdf|journal=The Physics Teacher|volume=29|issue=5|pages=312–13|bibcode=1991PhTea..29..312C|doi=10.1119/1.2343327}}</ref></noinclude>
[[File:Back side of the Moon AS16-3021.jpg|thumb|right|The [[Far side of the Moon|dark side of the Moon]] illuminated by the Sun.]]
* The [[Far side of the Moon|dark (far) side of the Moon]] receives about the same amount of light from the [[Sun]] as the [[near side of the Moon|near side]]. It is called "dark" not because it never receives light but because it had never been seen until humans [[Luna 3|sent spacecraft]] around the Moon, since the same side of the Moon always faces the Earth due to [[tidal locking]].<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Sigurdsson|first=Steinn|date=June 9, 2014|title=The Dark Side of the Moon: a Short History|url=http://scienceblogs.com/catdynamics/2014/06/09/the-dark-side-of-the-moon-a-short-history/|access-date=September 16, 2017}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite news||last=Messer|first=A'ndrea Elyse|date=June 9, 2014|title=55-year-old dark side of the moon mystery solved|publisher=Penn State News|url=http://news.psu.edu/story/317841/2014/06/09/research/55-year-old-dark-side-moon-mystery-solved|access-date=September 16, 2017}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Falin|first=Lee|date=January 5, 2015|title=What's on the Dark Side of the Moon?|url=http://www.quickanddirtytips.com/education/science/what%E2%80%99s-on-the-dark-side-of-the-moon|access-date=September 16, 2017|archive-date=November 30, 2018|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20181130124604/https://www.quickanddirtytips.com/education/science/what%E2%80%99s-on-the-dark-side-of-the-moon}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Black hole]]s have the same gravitational effects as any other equal mass in their place. They will draw objects nearby towards them, just as any other celestial body does, except at very close distances to the black hole, comparable to its [[Schwarzschild radius]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Wolfson|first=Richard|title=Simply Einstein: relativity demystified|publisher=W.W. Norton & Co.|date=2002|page=261|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=OUJWKdlFKeQC&pg=PA219|isbn=978-0-393-05154-4}}</ref></noinclude> If, for example, the Sun were replaced by a black hole of equal mass, the orbits of the planets would be essentially unaffected. A [[stellar mass black hole]] ''can'' pull in a substantial inflow of surrounding matter, but only if the star from which it formed was already doing so.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://oyc.yale.edu/astronomy/astr-160/lecture-9#transcript |title=Frontiers And Controversies In Astrophysics Lecture 9 |publisher=[[Yale University]] |access-date=April 26, 2011 }}</ref></noinclude>
[[File:Earth seasons seen as terminator motion.gif|thumb|The Earth's [[equator]] does not line up with the [[Orbital plane (astronomy)|plane of the Earth's orbit]], so for half of the year the [[Northern Hemisphere]] is tilted more towards the [[Sun]] and for the other half the Northern Hemisphere is tilted more away, causing seasonal temperature variation.]]
* Seasons are not caused by the Earth being [[Orbital eccentricity|closer to the Sun in the summer than in the winter]], but by the [[Effect of Sun angle on climate|effects of Earth's 23.4-degree axial tilt]]. Each hemisphere is tilted towards the Sun in its respective summer (July in the Northern Hemisphere and January in the Southern Hemisphere), resulting in longer days and more direct sunlight, with the opposite being true in the winter. Earth reaches [[Perihelion|the point in its orbit closest to the Sun]] in January, and it reaches [[Apsis|the point farthest from the Sun]] in July, so the [[Season#Elliptical Earth orbit|slight contribution of orbital eccentricity]] opposes the temperature trends of the seasons in the Northern Hemisphere.<noinclude><ref name="Science@NASA">{{#invoke:cite web||last=Phillips|first=Tony|date=July 4, 2003|title=The Distant Sun|url=http://science.nasa.gov/science-news/science-at-nasa/2002/02jul_aphelion|access-date=April 21, 2021|website=[[NASA]]|archive-date=December 5, 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221205153902/https://science.nasa.gov/science-news/science-at-nasa/2002/02jul_aphelion/}}</ref></noinclude> Orbital eccentricity can influence temperatures, but on Earth, this effect is small and is more than counteracted by other factors.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.adlerplanetarium.org/education/resources/sunearth/section06i.shtml|publisher=Adler Planetarium |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20071216004548/http://www.adlerplanetarium.org/education/resources/sunearth/section06i.shtml|archive-date=December 16, 2007|title=Sun-Earth Connection|access-date=May 8, 2009}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://istp.gsfc.nasa.gov/istp/outreach/sunearthmiscons.html|title=Ten Things You Thought You Knew about Sun-Earth Science|publisher=NASA|access-date=May 8, 2009 | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20130221092931/http://istp.gsfc.nasa.gov/istp/outreach/sunearthmiscons.html | archive-date = February 21, 2013| url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude>
* When a meteor or spacecraft enters the atmosphere, [[Atmospheric entry#Real (equilibrium) gas model|the heat of entry]] is not primarily caused by friction, but by [[Adiabatic heating|adiabatic compression of air]] in front of the object.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.nasa.gov/centers/ames/research/2007/faq-shuttleglass_prt.htm |title=NASA – Spacecraft Design |access-date=January 7, 2013 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090709055746/http://www.nasa.gov/centers/ames/research/2007/faq-shuttleglass_prt.htm |archive-date=July 9, 2009 }}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://blogs.discovermagazine.com/badastronomy/2009/03/30/more-booming-fireballs/ |title=More booming fireballs |work=Bad Astronomy |access-date=January 7, 2013 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131215231308/http://blogs.discovermagazine.com/badastronomy/2009/03/30/more-booming-fireballs/ |archive-date=December 15, 2013 |date=March 30, 2009 }}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://blogs.discovermagazine.com/badastronomy/2008/12/14/meteor-propter-hoc/ |title=Meteor propter hoc |author=Phil Plait |date=December 14, 2008 |work=Bad Astronomy |publisher=Discover |access-date=January 19, 2014| archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20140203034517/http://blogs.discovermagazine.com/badastronomy/2008/12/14/meteor-propter-hoc/ | archive-date = February 3, 2014| url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Egg balancing]] is possible on every day of the year, not just the [[March equinox|vernal equinox]],<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web|| url=http://www.snopes.com/science/equinox.asp | title=Infernal Egguinox | work=[[Snopes]] | date=March 6, 2012 | access-date=January 29, 2014}}</ref></noinclude> and there is no relationship between any astronomical phenomenon and the ability to balance an egg.<noinclude><ref name="AP">{{#invoke:cite news||url=https://apnews.com/0cf1b28fd3bb7e0efa8f91da775ea6e8|title=Equinox Returns and Eggs Keep Balancing|author=Schmid, Randolph|date=September 20, 1987|access-date=January 29, 2014|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140427084100/http://www.apnewsarchive.com/1987/Equinox-Returns-and-Eggs-Keep-Balancing/id-0cf1b28fd3bb7e0efa8f91da775ea6e8|archive-date=April 27, 2014|url-status=live|work=Associated Press News}}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[Fisher Space Pen]] was not commissioned by NASA at a cost of millions of dollars, while the Soviets used pencils. It was independently developed by Paul C. Fisher, founder of the Fisher Pen Company, with $1 million of his own funds.<noinclude><ref>[https://www.spacepen.com/about-us.aspx "Fisher Space Pen – Our story"] Retrieved on February 4, 2019</ref></noinclude> NASA tested and approved the pen for space use, then purchased 400 pens at $6 per pen.<noinclude><ref>[https://history.nasa.gov/spacepen.html "NASA – The Fisher Space Pen"] {{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220111230216/https://history.nasa.gov/spacepen.html |date=January 11, 2022 }} Retrieved on February 4, 2019</ref></noinclude> The Soviet Union subsequently also purchased the Space Pen for its [[Soyuz (spacecraft)|Soyuz]] spaceflights.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Curtin |first=Ciara |title=Fact or Fiction?: NASA Spent Millions to Develop a Pen that Would Write in Space, whereas the Soviet Cosmonauts Used a Pencil |url=https://www.scientificamerican.com/article/fact-or-fiction-nasa-spen/ |access-date=May 18, 2022 |website=Scientific American |language=en}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Tang (drink)|Tang]], [[Velcro]], and [[Teflon]] were not [[NASA spinoff technologies|spun off from technology originally developed by NASA]] for spaceflight, though many other products (such as [[memory foam]] and [[space blanket]]s) were.<noinclude><ref name="spinfaq">{{#invoke:cite web||url=https://spinoff.nasa.gov/faq|title=Spinoff Frequently Asked Questions |work=NASA.gov|access-date=February 28, 2021}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||title=Boomers collect artifacts, memories of NASA's heyday |last=Courter |first=Barry |newspaper=[[Times Free Press]] |date=May 13, 2007 |url=http://www.timesfreepress.com/news/2007/may/13/Boomers-collect-artifacts-memories-of-NASAs/ |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110930222247/http://www.timesfreepress.com/news/2007/may/13/Boomers-collect-artifacts-memories-of-NASAs/ |archive-date=September 30, 2011 }}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[Sun]] is not yellow; rather, it emits light across the full [[Visible spectrum|spectrum of visible colors]], and this combined light appears white when outside of Earth's atmosphere. Earth's atmosphere [[Rayleigh scattering|scatters]] shorter wavelengths of light, particularly blues and violets, more than longer wavelengths like reds and yellows, and this scattering is why the Sun appears yellow during the day or orange or red during sunrise and sunset. The scattered blue/violet light, appearing to come from all directions, is what makes the rest of the sky look blue.<noinclude><ref name="SunStanford">{{#invoke:cite web||last1=Scherrer |first1=Deborah |display-authors=etal |title=What Color do YOU think the Sun is? |url=http://solar-center.stanford.edu/SID/activities/GreenSun.html |website=Stanford SOLAR Center |access-date=June 1, 2021}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=https://eclipse2017.nasa.gov/what-color-sun |title=What Color is the Sun? |author=Lou Mayo |website=NASA Eclipse2017 |access-date=2024-01-24}}</ref></noinclude>
[[File:Great Wall of China, Satellite image.jpeg|thumb|right|A satellite image of a section of the [[Great Wall of China]], running diagonally from lower left to upper right (not to be confused with the much more prominent river running from upper left to lower right).]]
* The [[Great Wall of China]] is not the only [[Artificial structures visible from space|human-made object visible from space]] or from the Moon.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||date=April 2, 2009 |url=https://www.nasa.gov/image-article/great-wall/ |title=Great Wall |work=NASA |access-date=July 5, 2024}}</ref></noinclude> None of the [[List of Apollo astronauts|Apollo astronauts]] reported seeing ''any'' specific human-made object from the Moon, and even Earth-orbiting astronauts can see it only with magnification. City lights, however, are easily visible on the night side of Earth from orbit.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=https://science.nasa.gov/science-news/science-at-nasa/2003/24mar_noseprints/ |title=Space Station Astrophotography |publisher=NASA|date=March 24, 2003|access-date=January 13, 2011|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140404162248/https://science.nasa.gov/science-news/science-at-nasa/2003/24mar_noseprints/|archive-date=April 4, 2014|url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[Big Bang]] model does not fully explain the [[origin of the universe]]. It does not describe how energy, time, and space were caused, but rather it describes the emergence of the present universe from an ultra-dense and high-temperature initial state.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=https://lweb.cfa.harvard.edu/seuforum/faq.htm#m12 |url-status=live |title=Brief Answers to Cosmic Questions |author=<!--Not stated--> |website=Universe Forum |publisher=[[Harvard–Smithsonian Center for Astrophysics]] |location=Cambridge, MA |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160413195349/https://www.cfa.harvard.edu/seuforum/faq.htm |archive-date=April 13, 2016 |access-date=December 18, 2019}} Archival site: "The Universe Forum's role as part of NASA's Education Support Network concluded in September, 2009."</ref></noinclude>

=== Biology ===
{{See also|Common misunderstandings of genetics}}

==== Mammals ====
* Old elephants near death do not leave their herd to go to an "[[elephants' graveyard]]" to die.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite news ||last=Spanney |first=Laura |date=January 28, 1995 |title=Not many people know that |url=http://www.newscientist.com/article/mg14519625.100-not-many-people-know-that.html |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080325155037/http://www.newscientist.com/article/mg14519625.100-not-many-people-know-that.html |archive-date=March 25, 2008 |access-date=June 16, 2024 |work=[[New Scientist]]}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||url=https://planetwild.com/blog/african-savanna-elephant|date=December 6, 2023|title=Are elephants afraid of mice? Facts and myths about the African savanna elephant|access-date=June 25, 2024 |quote=Mythbusting: Popular myths about the African elephant... Myth: Elephants go to elephant graveyards to die}}</ref></noinclude>
[[File:10 - Cristina Sánchez.jpg|thumb|The color of a red cape does not enrage a bull.]]
* Bulls are not enraged by the color red, used in capes by [[Bullfighter|professional bullfighters]]. Cattle are [[Dichromacy|dichromats]], so red does not stand out as a bright color. It is not the color of the cape, but the perceived threat by the bullfighter that incites it to charge.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.itla.net/index.cfm?sec=Longhorn_Information&con=handling|title=Longhorn_Information – handling|first=Larry|last=Smith II|publisher=International Texas Longhorn Association|date=2007|access-date=June 23, 2010|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20100511090201/http://www.itla.net/index.cfm?sec=Longhorn_Information&con=handling|archive-date=May 11, 2010}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||url=http://iacuc.tennessee.edu/pdf/Policies-AnimalCare/Cattle-BasicCare.pdf|title=Cattle – Basic Care|first=A.|last=Dario|date=September 12, 2003|publisher=[[IACUC]], University of Tennessee|access-date=June 23, 2010|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080625012822/http://iacuc.tennessee.edu/pdf/Policies-AnimalCare/Cattle-BasicCare.pdf|archive-date=June 25, 2008}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite book||chapter-url=https://books.google.com/books?id=GhmrNYJhcrIC&pg=PA45|title=The Biology of Animal Stress|editor=Moberg, Gary|editor2=Mench, Joy A.|chapter=Behavioral Principles of Handling Cattle and Other Grazing Animals under Extensive Conditions|first=Temple|last=Grandin|page=45|publisher=[[CAB International|CABI]]|date=2007|isbn=978-1-84593-219-0}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Cat|Domestic cats']] behavioral and personality traits cannot be predicted from their coat color. Rather, these traits depend on a complex interplay between genetic and environmental factors.<noinclude><ref>{{cite journal | last1=Udell | first1=Monique | last2=Delgado | first2=Mikel | last3=Ekenstedt | first3=Kari | last4=Shoveller | first4=Anna Kate | last5=Croney | first5=Candace | title=CATastrophic myths part 2: Common misconceptions about the environmental, nutritional, and genetic management of domestic cats and their welfare implications | journal=The Veterinary Journal | volume=300-302 | date=2023 | doi=10.1016/j.tvjl.2023.106029 | page=106029| pmid=37683762 | doi-access=free }}</ref></noinclude>
*Not all cats are attracted and intoxicated by [[catnip]], which only affects about two thirds of them. Alternatives exist, such as [[valerian root]] and leaves.<noinclude><ref name="bmcvetres.biomedcentral.com">{{cite journal |last1=Bol |first1=Sebastiaan |title=Responsiveness of cats (Felidae) to silver vine (''Actinidia polygama''), Tatarian honeysuckle (''Lonicera tatarica''), valerian (''Valeriana officinalis'') and catnip (''Nepeta cataria'') |journal=BMC Veterinary Research |date=16 March 2017 |doi=10.1186/s12917-017-0987-6 |pmid=28302120 |volume=13 |issue=1 |pmc=5356310 |page=70 |doi-access=free}}</ref><ref name="Cat World">{{Cite web|title=Catnip (Nepeta cataria) – Everything You Need to Know About Catnip!|url= http://www.cat-world.com.au/all-about-catnip|website=Cat-World.com.au|publisher=Cat World |date=2014 |access-date=2 January 2015 |archive-url= https://web.archive.org/web/20150206132508/http://www.cat-world.com.au/all-about-catnip |archive-date=6 February 2015 |url-status=dead}}</ref></noinclude>
* Lemmings do not engage in mass suicidal dives off cliffs when migrating. The scenes of [[Lemming#Misconceptions|lemming suicides]] in the 1958 [[Disney]] documentary film ''[[White Wilderness (film)|White Wilderness]]'', which popularized this idea, were completely fabricated. The lemmings in the film were actually purchased from [[Inuit]] children, transported to the filming location in Canada and repeatedly shoved off a nearby cliff by the filmmakers to create the illusion of a mass suicide.<noinclude><ref name="Mikkelson 2007">{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.snopes.com/disney/films/lemmings.asp|title=White Wilderness Lemmings Suicide|website=[[Snopes]]|date=August 19, 2007 |first=Barbara and David P. |last=Mikkelson|access-date=August 29, 2009 }}</ref><ref name="TotalLemmingDeath">{{#invoke:cite web||last1=Smith |first1=Nadine |title=How Disney Tricked the World Into Believing Lemmings Commit Mass Suicide |url=https://hyperallergic.com/545742/white-wilderness-disney-nature-documentary/ |website=Hyperallergic |date=March 13, 2020 |access-date=23 August 2022}}</ref></noinclude> The misconception itself is much older, dating back to at least the late 19th century, though its exact origins are uncertain.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Scott|first=W.|journal=The Monthly Chronicle of North-country Lore and Legend|date=November 1891|title=The Monthly chronicle of North-country lore and legend: v. 1–5; Mar. 1887–Dec. 1891|volume=5|page=523|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=W8rUAAAAMAAJ&pg=PA523}}</ref><ref name="Mikkelson 2007" /></noinclude>
* Dogs do not sweat by [[salivation|salivating]].<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||title=Dog noses – myths and facts about your dog's nose – weekly pet tips by Pets.ca|url=http://www.pets.ca/dogs/tips/dog-noses-facts-and-myths-pet-tip-115/|access-date=May 22, 2011}}
<br />b. {{harvnb|Varasdi|1996|loc=p. 81: "Dogs do not sweat with their tongues as most people believe. They do have some sweat glands, but the ones of most importance are on the pads, or soles, of their feet."}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Segaloff|first=Nat|title=The Everything tall tales, legends & outrageous lies book|date=2001|publisher=Adams Media Corp.|isbn=978-1-58062-514-2|page=265|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=03vYAAAAMAAJ|quote=Of course, dogs sweat. You would, too, if you had to wear a fur coat in hot weather. Dogs excrete moisture through the pads on their paws.}}
<br />d. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Olien|first=Michael D.|title=The human myth: an introduction to anthropology|date=1978|publisher=Harper & Row|location=New York|isbn=978-0-06-044918-6|page=568|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=mvFKAAAAYAAJ|quote=It is another folk tale that dogs do not sweat except through the tongue. This is an incorrect belief as dogs possess sweat glands all over the body.}}
<br />e. {{#invoke:cite journal||last=Aoki|first=T.|author2=Wada, M.|title=Functional Activity of the Sweat Glands in the Hairy Skin of the Dog|journal=Science|date=August 2, 1951|volume=114|issue=2953|pages=123–24|doi=10.1126/science.114.2953.123|bibcode=1951Sci...114..123A|pmid=14854926}}
<br />f. {{#invoke:cite journal||title=British Medical Journal 1899 April 15|pmc=2462491 |quote=SOME time ago we received from a correspondent an inquiry as to whether the very prevalent belief that a dog perspires through the tongue was a vulgar error or well founded. ...whether the dog exudes fluid from the tongue of the some kind as that exuded from the human skin. To this question the answer is, No. The skin of the dog is abundantly furnished with glands, having the characteristic disposition and structure of those which in man produce sweat, ... in other words, the dog does not sweat by the tongue.|pages=921–28|volume=1|issue=1998|journal=British Medical Journal|doi=10.1136/bmj.1.1998.921|year=1899 }}</ref></noinclude> Dogs actually do have [[sweat gland]]s and not only on their tongues; they sweat mainly through their footpads. However, dogs do primarily regulate their body temperature through [[thermoregulation|panting]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.petplace.com/dogs/how-do-dogs-sweat/page1.aspx |title=How Do Dogs Sweat|page=1|publisher=Petplace.com |access-date=February 9, 2012 | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20131214113342/http://www.petplace.com/dogs/how-do-dogs-sweat/page1.aspx | archive-date = December 14, 2013|url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude> (See also: [[Dog anatomy#Temperature regulation|Dog <span class="nowrap">Anatomy{{tsp}}§{{tsp}}Temperature</span> regulation]])
* Dogs do not consistently age seven times as quickly as humans. [[Aging in dogs]] varies widely depending on the breed; certain breeds, such as [[giant dog breeds]] and [[English bulldog]]s, have much shorter lifespans than average.<noinclude><ref>{{Cite web |last=Cara |first=Ed |date=2023-11-26 |title=The Unhealthiest Dog Breeds |url=https://gizmodo.com.au/2023/11/the-unhealthiest-dog-breeds-2/ |access-date=2024-08-23 |website=Gizmodo Australia |language=en-AU}}</ref></noinclude> Most dogs reach adolescence by one year old; smaller and medium-sized breeds begin to age more slowly in adulthood.<noinclude><ref>a. Spadafori, Gina (1996). ''Dogs for Dummies''. IDG Books. {{ISBN|978-1-56884-861-7}}
<br />b. Siegal, Mordecai (Ed.; 1995). ''UC Davis School of Veterinary Medicine Book of the Dogs''; Chapter 5, "Geriatrics", by Aldrich, Janet. Harper Collins. {{ISBN|978-0-06-270136-7}}.
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Wang|first1=Tina|last2=Ma|first2=Jianzhu|last3=Hogan|first3=Andrew N.|last4=Fong|first4=Samson|last5=Licon|first5=Katherine|last6=Tsui|first6=Brian|last7=Kreisberg|first7=Jason F.|last8=Adams|first8=Peter D.|last9=Carvunis|first9=Anne-Ruxandra|last10=Bannasch|first10=Danika L.|last11=Ostrander|first11=Elaine A.|date=July 2, 2020|title=Quantitative Translation of Dog-to-Human Aging by Conserved Remodeling of the DNA Methylome|url= |journal=Cell Systems|volume=11|language=en|issue=2|pages=176–185.e6|doi=10.1016/j.cels.2020.06.006|pmid=32619550|pmc=7484147|issn=2405-4712|doi-access=free}}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[Lunar phase|phases of the Moon]] have no effect on the [[Wolf communication|vocalizations of wolves]], and wolves do not howl at the Moon.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last1=Busch|first1=R. H.|title=Wolf Almanac, New and Revised: A Celebration Of Wolves And Their World|publisher=[[Rowman & Littlefield]]|edition=3rd|year=2007|isbn=978-1-59921-069-8|url={{Google books|plainurl=yes|id=svbnCwAAQBAJ}}}}, p. 59</ref></noinclude> Wolves howl to assemble the pack usually before and after hunts, to pass on an alarm particularly at a den site, to locate each other during a storm, while crossing unfamiliar territory, and to communicate across great distances.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Lopez |first=Barry H. |title=Of Wolves and Men |publisher=J. M. Dent and Sons Limited |year=1978 |isbn=978-0-7432-4936-2 |url={{Google books|plainurl=yes|id=sz8gAQAAIAAJ}}}}, p. 38</ref></noinclude>
* There is no such thing as an "[[alpha (ethology)|alpha]]" in a wolf pack. An early study that coined the term "alpha wolf" had only observed unrelated adult wolves living in captivity. In the wild, wolf packs operate like families: parents are in charge until the young grow up and start their own families, and younger wolves do not overthrow an "alpha" to become the new leader.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=https://apdt.com/pet-owners/choosing-a-trainer/dominance/ |title=Dominance and Dog Training|access-date=January 30, 2017 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170202064934/https://apdt.com/pet-owners/choosing-a-trainer/dominance/ |archive-date=February 2, 2017}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||url=http://io9.gizmodo.com/why-everything-you-know-about-wolf-packs-is-wrong-502754629|title=Why everything you know about wolf packs is wrong|last=Davis|first=Lauren|work=io9|access-date=October 13, 2017|language=en-US}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Bat#Vision|Bats are not blind]]. While about 70% of bat species, mainly in the [[microbat]] family, use [[animal echolocation|echolocation]] to navigate, all bat species have eyes and are capable of sight. In addition, almost all bats in the [[megabat]] or fruit bat family cannot echolocate and have excellent night vision.<noinclude><ref name="bats">a. {{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.nwf.org/News-and-Magazines/National-Wildlife/Animals/Archives/2003/American-Heritage-Animal-Cliches.aspx|title=The Truth About Animal Clichés|date=February 1, 2003|first=Roger|last=Di Silvestro|publisher=National Wildlife Federation|access-date=October 31, 2011}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||title=Blind as a Bat?|format=Press release|publisher=[[Hobart and William Smith Colleges]]|location=Geneva, New York|date=June 12, 2003|url=http://www.collegenews.org/x2682.xml|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080607080055/http://www.collegenews.org/x2682.xml|archive-date=June 7, 2008|access-date=April 7, 2009}}</ref></noinclude>
* Tomato juice and sauce are ineffective at neutralizing the odor of a skunk.<noinclude><ref>[http://scienceline.org/2006/07/ask-cosier-skunk/ Is it true that tomato sauce will get rid of the smell of a skunk?]. Scienceline. Retrieved on April 5, 2012.</ref></noinclude> [[Skunk#Mitigation|Effective treatments]] for skunk odor involve artificial compounds rather than household remedies.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web|| url = http://www.humanesociety.org/animals/dogs/tips/de-skunking_dog.html | title = De-skunking your dog | publisher = [[The Humane Society of the United States]] | access-date = August 8, 2019 | archive-date = December 10, 2016 | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20161210154906/http://www.humanesociety.org/animals/dogs/tips/de-skunking_dog.html }}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Porcupine#Quills|Porcupines do not shoot their quills]]. They can detach, and porcupines will deliberately back into attackers to impale them, but their quills do not project.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||title=Encyclopædia Britannica: Or, A Dictionary of Arts, Sciences, and Miscellaneous Literature, Enlarged and Improved|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=Is0nAAAAMAAJ&pg=PA501|year=1823|publisher=Archibald Constable|pages=501–}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||author=Shepard, Thomas Goodwin|title=The natural history of secession|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=MTA5AAAAMAAJ&pg=PA78|year=1865|publisher=Derby & Miller|pages=78–}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=https://tpwd.texas.gov/publications/nonpwdpubs/introducing_mammals/porcupines/|title=Porcupines|date=n.d.|website=Texas Parks & Wildlife|language=en|access-date=October 14, 2022}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Mouse#Diet|Mice do not have a special appetite for cheese]], and will eat it only for lack of better options; they actually favor sweet, sugary foods. The myth may have come from the fact that before the advent of refrigeration, cheese was usually stored outside and was therefore an easy food for mice to reach.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=https://animals.howstuffworks.com/animal-facts/do-mice-really-love-cheese.htm|title=Do mice really love cheese?|date=April 15, 2015|website=HowStuffWorks|language=en|access-date=February 27, 2020}}</ref></noinclude>
* The hippopotamus does not produce pink milk, nor does it sweat blood. The skin secretions of the hippopotamus are red due to the presence of [[hipposudoric acid]], a red pigment which acts as a natural sunscreen, and is neither sweat nor blood. It does not affect the color of their milk, which is white or beige.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=FACT CHECK: Is Hippopotamus Milk Pink?|url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/false-hippopotamus-milk-pink/|date=January 6, 2016|website=[[Snopes]]|language=en-US}|access-date=February 16, 2022}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Rabbit#Folklore and mythology|Rabbits are not especially partial to carrots]]. Their diet in the wild primarily consists of dark green vegetables such as grasses and clovers, and excessive carrot consumption is unhealthy for them due to containing high levels of sugar. This misconception originated from [[Bugs Bunny]] cartoons, whose carrot-chomping habit was meant as a reference to the character played by [[Clark Gable]] in ''[[It Happened One Night]]''.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Bittel|first=Jason|title=Think you know what bunnies and bears eat? Their diets may surprise you. |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/lifestyle/kidspost/think-you-know-what-bunnies-and-bears-eat-their-diets-may-surprise-you/2019/09/20/bac528ea-ce5d-11e9-87fa-8501a456c003_story.html |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190926235234/https://www.washingtonpost.com/lifestyle/kidspost/think-you-know-what-bunnies-and-bears-eat-their-diets-may-surprise-you/2019/09/20/bac528ea-ce5d-11e9-87fa-8501a456c003_story.html |newspaper=Washington Post|date= September 22, 2019 |archive-date=September 26, 2019|url-status=live|quote=In the wild, rabbits aren't in the habit of digging up root vegetables such as carrots, potatoes and beets. They much prefer wild greens, such as grasses and clover. In fact, carrots may actually be bad for rabbits, because although the vegetables are high in good nutrients, including beta carotene, they are also relatively high in sugar. This means that feeding a rabbit lots of carrots could lead to tooth decay or other health issues.}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||editor1-last=George|editor1-first=Amber E.|editor2-last=Schatz|editor2-first=J.L.|title=Screening the Nonhuman: Representations of Animal Others in the Media|chapter=Chapter 5: Would Bugs Bunny Have Diabetes? The Realistic Consequences of Cartoons for Non-Human Animals|year=2016|isbn=978-1-4985-1375-3|pages=63–67|publisher=Lexington Books}}</ref></noinclude>

==== Birds ====
* A human touching or handling eggs or baby birds will not cause the adult birds to abandon them.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/a-bird-in-the-hand/ |title=Fact Check: Will Baby Birds Be Rejected by Their Mother If You Handle Them? |first=Barbara |last=Mikkelson |date=August 26, 2001 |website=[[Snopes]] }}</ref></noinclude> The same is generally true for other animals having their young touched by humans as well, with the possible exception of rabbits (as rabbits will sometimes abandon their nest after an event they perceive as traumatizing).<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=https://www.scientificamerican.com/article/fact-or-fiction-birds-abandon-young-at-human-touch/ |magazine=[[Scientific American]] |title=Fact or Fiction?: Birds (and Other Critters) Abandon Their Young at the Slightest Human Touch |first=Robynne |last=Boyd |date=July 26, 2007}}</ref></noinclude>
* Eating rice, yeast, or [[Alka-Seltzer]] does not cause birds to explode and is rarely fatal. Birds can [[flatulate]] and [[Regurgitation (digestion)|regurgitate]] to expel gas, and some birds even include wild rice as part of their diet.<noinclude><ref name="Mikkelson 2000" /><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=David |date=2020-05-10 |title=Duck Eats Yeast, Quacks, Explodes; Man Loses Eye |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/duck-eats-yeast-quacks-explodes-man-loses-eye/ |access-date=2023-12-06 |website=[[Snopes]] |language=en}}</ref></noinclude> The misconception has often led to weddings using [[millet]], [[confetti]], or other materials to shower the newlyweds as they leave the ceremony, instead of the [[Wedding customs by country|throwing of rice]] that is traditional in some places.<noinclude><ref name="Mikkelson 2000">{{cite web |last1=Mikkelson |first1=Barbara |title=Is Throwing Rice at Weddings Bad for Birds? |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/against-the-grain/ |website=Snopes |access-date=29 July 2024 |date=14 May 2000}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=https://www.livescience.com/32624-does-wedding-rice-make-birds-explode.html |title=Does Wedding Rice Make Birds Explode? |date=June 4, 2010 |website=[[Live Science]] |access-date=April 17, 2021}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||url=https://www.jacksonville.com/story/news/reason/2016/10/19/fact-check-birds-really-can-eat-rice-safely/15728451007/ |work=[[The Florida Times-Union]] |date=October 19, 2016 |title=Fact Check: Birds really can eat rice safely |first=Carole |last=Fader}}</ref></noinclude>

* The bold, powerful cry commonly associated with the [[bald eagle]] in popular culture is actually that of a [[red-tailed hawk]]. [[Bald eagle#Popular culture|Bald eagle vocalizations]] are much softer and chirpier, and bear far more resemblance to the calls of [[gulls]].<noinclude><ref>Jessica Robinson, "[https://www.npr.org/templates/story/story.php?storyId=156187375 Bald Eagle: A Mighty Symbol, With A Not-So-Mighty Voice]"; [[NPR]], July 2, 2012; accessed 2019.08.23.</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||year=2001|title=Raptors of the World| publisher=[[Helm Identification Guides|Christopher Helm]]|location=London|pages=717–19|isbn=978-0-7136-8026-3|author1=Ferguson-Lees, J. |author2=Christie, D.}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Common ostrich#"Head in the sand" myth|Ostriches do not stick their heads in the sand]] to hide from enemies or to sleep.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||author=Kruszelnicki, Karl S. |date=November 2, 2006 |title=Ostrich head in sand |url=http://www.abc.net.au/science/articles/2006/11/02/1777947.htm |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140427082637/http://www.abc.net.au/science/articles/2006/11/02/1777947.htm |archive-date=April 27, 2014 |access-date=October 7, 2011 |work=Australian Broadcasting Corporation}}</ref></noinclude> This misconception's origins are uncertain but it was probably popularized by [[Pliny the Elder]] (23–79 CE), who wrote that ostriches "imagine, when they have thrust their head and neck into a bush, that the whole of their body is concealed".<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||author=Smith, Rex |date=May 8, 2011 |title=Maybe ostriches are smarter |url=http://www.timesunion.com/opinion/article/Maybe-ostriches-are-smarter-1370503.php |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140427082414/http://www.timesunion.com/opinion/article/Maybe-ostriches-are-smarter-1370503.php |archive-date=April 27, 2014 |access-date=October 7, 2011 |work=Albany Times-Union}}</ref></noinclude>
* A duck's quack actually does [[Duck's quack|echo]],<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Alcatraz Escape: Does a Duck's Quack Echo? |url=http://dsc.discovery.com/fansites/mythbusters/episode/episode-tab-08.html |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121003151210/http://dsc.discovery.com/fansites/mythbusters/episode/episode-tab-08.html |archive-date=October 3, 2012}} [[MythBusters (2003 season)#Does a Duck's Quack Echo?|(Season 1, Episode 8)]]. ''[[MythBusters]]''. Discovery Channel. December 12, 2003.</ref></noinclude> although the echo may be difficult to hear for humans under some circumstances.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=A Duck's Quack Doesn't Echo, and no-one knows the reason why? |url=http://www.acoustics.salford.ac.uk/acoustics_info/duck/ |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131011174434/http://www.acoustics.salford.ac.uk/acoustics_info/duck/ |archive-date=October 11, 2013 |access-date=January 13, 2010 |work=Acoustics.salford.ac.uk |publisher=University of Salford Acoustics}}</ref></noinclude> Despite this, a British panel show compiling interesting facts has been given the name ''[[Duck Quacks Don't Echo]]''.

[[File:Dodo head Dinkel.jpg|thumb|The dodo was intelligent and inedible despite popular belief]]

* Despite the saying "dumb as dodo," the [[dodo|dodo's]] intelligence was above average for an avian, as it was a member of the family [[Columbidae]] (pigeons).
