d. {{Cite report |url=http://www.loc.gov/law/help/restrictions-on-gmos/usa.php#Opinion |title=Restrictions on Genetically Modified Organisms: United States |date=March 2014 |access-date=July 7, 2024 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160206104730/http://www.loc.gov/law/help/restrictions-on-gmos/usa.php#Opinion |archive-date=February 6, 2016 }}</ref></noinclude>
* Reading in dim light causes [[eye strain]] rather than permanent damage to the eye.<noinclude><ref name="Vreeman 2007" /></noinclude>
* [[Color blindness]] cannot be significantly alleviated by [[color blind glasses|glasses or lenses]]. While there are lenses marketed towards the colorblind, their efficacy is doubted by professionals, and they do not enable wearers to see new colors.<noinclude><ref name=":22">{{Cite web |author1=Almutairi, Nawaf |author2=Kundart, James |author3=Muthuramalingam, Naganathan |author4=Hayes, John |author5=Citek, Karl |author6=Aljohani, Saad |date=2017 |title=Assessment of EnChroma Filter for Correcting Color Vision Deficiency |url=https://core.ac.uk/download/pdf/141726688.pdf |access-date=24 November 2018 |website=Pacific University}}</ref></noinclude>
* A [[fever]] from infection does not cause brain damage by itself.<noinclude><ref>{{cite web |title=Fever – Myths Versus Facts |url=https://www.seattlechildrens.org/conditions/a-z/fever-myths-versus-facts/ |website=[[Seattle Children's Hospital]] |access-date=29 November 2024 |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Top five fever myths and facts |url=https://www.texaschildrens.org/content/wellness/top-five-fever-myths-and-facts |website=[[Texas Children's]] |access-date=29 November 2024 |language=en |date=8 November 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Fever – Facts Versus Myths |url=https://www.childrensmercy.org/siteassets/media-documents-for-depts-section/documents-for-health-and-safety/fever-facts-versus-myths.pdf |website=[[Children's Mercy Kansas City]] |access-date=29 November 2024}}</ref></noinclude> The myth has been linked to the association between fevers and typically non-serious [[febrile seizures]].<noinclude><ref>{{cite web |last1=Pulliam |first1=Dr Patrick |title=Fever myths and facts |url=https://www.covenantcarepediatrics.com/fever-myths-and-facts/ |website=Covenant Care Pediatrics |access-date=29 November 2024 |date=20 February 2024}}</ref></noinclude>

==== Nutrition, food, and drink ====
* [[Diet (nutrition)|Diet]] has little influence on the body's [[detoxification]], and there is no evidence that [[Detoxification (alternative medicine)|detoxification diets]] rid the body of toxins.<noinclude><ref name="Mayo Clinic Website">Compare: {{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.mayoclinic.com/health/detox-diets/AN01334|title=Do detox diets offer any health benefits?|publisher=[[Mayo Clinic]]|last=Zeratsky|first=Katherine|date=April 21, 2012|access-date=May 9, 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191216032647/https://www.mayoclinic.org/healthy-lifestyle/nutrition-and-healthy-eating/expert-answers/detox-diets/faq-20058040|archive-date=December 16, 2019|quote=[...T]here's little evidence that detox diets actually remove toxins from the body. Indeed, the kidneys and liver are generally quite effective at filtering and eliminating most ingested toxins.}}</ref><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.quackwatch.org/01QuackeryRelatedTopics/detox_overview.html| title="Detoxification" schemes and scams|last=Barrett|first=Stephen|author-link=Stephen Barrett|publisher=[[Quackwatch]]|access-date = June 18, 2014|date=June 8, 2011}}
<br />b.
{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.webmd.com/diet/features/detox-diets-cleansing-body-feature | title = Detox Diets: Cleansing the Body|website = [[WebMD]]| access-date = June 23, 2010 }}</ref></noinclude> Toxins are metabolized and removed from the bloodstream by the liver and kidneys, and they are primarily removed from the body in urine and bile (excreted with the feces).<noinclude><ref name="Mayo Clinic Website" /></noinclude>
* Drinking milk or consuming other [[dairy products]] does not increase [[mucus]] production.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Pinnock |first1=CB |last2=Graham |first2=NM |last3=Mylvaganam |first3=A |last4=Douglas |first4=RM |title=Relationship between milk intake and mucus production in adult volunteers challenged with rhinovirus-2 |journal=The American Review of Respiratory Disease |volume=141 |issue=2 |pages=352–56 |date=1990 |pmid=2154152 |doi=10.1164/ajrccm/141.2.352}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite book||title=Handbook of pediatric nutrition |author1=Patricia Queen Samour |author2=Kathy King Helm |publisher=Jones & Bartlett Learning |date=2005 |isbn=978-0-7637-8356-3 |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=J8Xgyvr9038C&pg=PA337}}</ref></noinclude> As a result, they do not need to be avoided by those with the flu or cold [[Nasal congestion|congestion]]. However, milk and saliva in one's mouth mix to create a thick liquid that can briefly coat the mouth and throat. The sensation that lingers may be mistaken for increased [[phlegm]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Cold symptoms: Does drinking milk increase phlegm? |url=https://www.mayoclinic.org/diseases-conditions/common-cold/expert-answers/phlegm/faq-20058015 |access-date=2022-07-31 |website=Mayo Clinic |language=en}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Daily_consumption_of_drinking_water|Drinking eight glasses (2–3 liters) of water a day]] is not needed to maintain health.<noinclude><ref name="Eightglasses">a. {{#invoke:cite journal||last=Valtin|first=Heinz|title="Drink at least eight glasses of water a day." Really? Is there scientific evidence for "8 × 8"?|journal=American Journal of Physiology. Regulatory, Integrative and Comparative Physiology|volume=283|issue=5|date=2002|pages=R993–R1004|doi=10.1152/ajpregu.00365.2002|pmid=12376390}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite news||title=Über den Durst|publisher=Die Zeit|url=http://www.zeit.de/2009/04/Stimmts|language=de|access-date=April 7, 2012}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite web||title=Muss ich wirklich 3&nbsp;Liter Wasser am Tag trinken|url=http://www.medipresse.de/muss-ich-wirklich-3-liter-wasser-am-tag-trinken-049.html|language=de|access-date=April 7, 2012|archive-date=September 3, 2012|archive-url=https://archive.today/20120903173518/http://www.medipresse.de/muss-ich-wirklich-3-liter-wasser-am-tag-trinken-049.html}}</ref></noinclude> The amount of water needed varies by person, weight, diet, activity level, clothing, and the ambient heat and humidity. Water does not actually need to be drunk in pure form, and can be derived from liquids such as juices, tea, milk, soups, etc., and from foods including fruits and vegetables.<noinclude><ref name="Eightglasses" /><ref name="NPRHydrationMyths">{{#invoke:cite web|| url=https://www.npr.org/2022/09/21/1124371309/busting-common-hydration-water-myths | title=Busting 5 common myths about water and hydration: Life Kit | website=NPR }}</ref></noinclude>
* Drinking coffee and other caffeinated beverages does not cause dehydration for regular drinkers, although it can for occasional drinkers.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite journal|| author1 = Sophie C. Killer | author2 = Andrew K. Blannin | author3 = Asker E. Jeukendrup | s2cid = 18643248 | title = No Evidence of Dehydration with Moderate Daily Coffee Intake: A Counterbalanced Cross-Over Study in a Free-Living Population | journal = PLOS ONE | volume = 9 | issue = 1 | pages = e84154 | date = January 2014 | pmid = 24416202 | doi = 10.1371/journal.pone.0084154| pmc = 3886980 | bibcode = 2014PLoSO...984154K | doi-access = free }}
<br />b. {{cite magazine |first=Alexa |last=Erickson |date=May 11, 2017 |url=https://www.rd.com/article/is-coffee-a-diuretic/ |title=Science Just Debunked a Coffee Myth That's Been Around Since 1928 |magazine=Reader's Digest}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite journal||first1=Ronald J.|last1=Maughan|first2=Phillip|last2=Watson|first3=Philip A.A.|last3=Cordery|first4=Neil P.|last4=Walsh|first5=Samuel J.|last5=Oliver|first6=Alberto|last6=Dolci|first7=Nidia|last7=Rodriguez-Sanchez|first8=Stuart|last8=Galloway|s2cid = 378245|title=A randomized trial to assess the potential of different beverages to affect hydration status: development of a beverage hydration index | journal = The American Journal of Clinical Nutrition|volume=103|issue=3|pages=717–23|date=December 23, 2015|pmid = 26702122|doi = 10.3945/ajcn.115.114769|doi-access=free|hdl=1893/22892|hdl-access=free}}</ref><ref name="NPRHydrationMyths" /></noinclude>
* [[Eating disorder]]s do not exclusively affect women: women are merely more likely than men to suffer from eating disorders.<noinclude><ref>{{cite book |vauthors=El Hayek R, Sfeir M, AlMutairi MS, Alqadheeb B, El Hayek S |year=2024 |pages=347–372 |chapter=Chapter 16: Myths about diet and mental health |veditors=Mohamed W, Kobeissy F |title=Nutrition and Psychiatric Disorders |publisher=Springer |doi=10.1007/978-981-97-2681-3_16}}</ref></noinclude>
* Neither spicy food nor coffee has a significant effect on the development of [[peptic ulcers]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||editor=Raphael Rubin|editor2=David S. Strayer|editor3=Emanuel Rubin|editor4=Gonzalo Aponte|title=Rubin's pathology: clinicopathologic foundations of medicine|date=2012|publisher=Wolters Kluwer Health/Lippincott Williams & Wilkins|location=Philadelphia, PA|isbn=978-1-60547-968-2|page=623|edition=6th|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=wb2TzY9AgJ0C&pg=PA623}}</ref></noinclude>
* Sugar does not cause [[Sugar and hyperactivity|hyperactivity]] in children.<noinclude><ref>{{anchor|Sugar does not cause hyperactivity in children}}
a. {{#invoke:cite journal||author=Vreeman R. C. |author2=Carroll A.E.|title=Festive medical myths|journal=BMJ|volume=337|page=a2769|date=2008|pmid=19091758|doi=10.1136/bmj.a2769|s2cid=29006871}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.uamshealth.com/?id=877&sid=1|title=Medical Myths |publisher=[[University of Arkansas for Medical Sciences]]|access-date=February 10, 2011 |archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20140109065139/http://www.uamshealth.com/?id=877&sid=1 | archive-date = January 9, 2014| url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude> Double-blind trials have shown no difference in behavior between children given sugar-full or sugar-free diets, even in studies specifically looking at children with [[attention deficit hyperactivity disorder]] or those considered sensitive to sugar.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Fullerton-Smith|first=Jill|title=The Truth About Food|publisher=Bloomsbury|date=2007|pages=115–17|isbn=978-0-7475-8685-2|quote=Most parents assume that children plus sugary foods equals raucous and uncontrollable behaviour.&nbsp;... according to nutrition experts, the belief that children experience a 'sugar high' is a myth.}}</ref></noinclude> A 2019 meta-analysis found no positive effect of sugar consumption on [[mood (psychology)|mood]] but did find an association with lower alertness and increased fatigue within an hour of consumption, known as a [[sugar crash]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Mantantzis|first1=Konstantinos|last2=Schlaghecken|first2=Friederike|last3=Sünram-Lea|first3=Sandra I.|last4=Maylor|first4=Elizabeth A.|date=June 1, 2019|title=Sugar rush or sugar crash? A meta-analysis of carbohydrate effects on mood|journal=Neuroscience and Biobehavioral Reviews|language=en|volume=101|pages=45–67|doi=10.1016/j.neubiorev.2019.03.016|pmid=30951762|s2cid=92575160|url=http://wrap.warwick.ac.uk/115618/1/WRAP-Sugar-rush-crash-meta-analysis-carbohydrate-effects-mood-Maylor-2019.pdf}}</ref></noinclude> Sugar can however lead to jump in blood sugar levels, causing temporary hyperactivity even if it does not cause clinical hyperactivity. <noinclude><ref>{{cite web | url=https://medlineplus.gov/ency/article/002426.htm | title=Hyperactivity and sugar: MedlinePlus Medical Encyclopedia }}</ref></noinclude>
* Eating nuts, popcorn, or seeds does not increase the risk of [[diverticulitis]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Atkins|first=William|title=Diverticulitis isn't anti-nut any more|url=http://discuss.itwire.com/viewtopic.php?f=30&t=6493|access-date=July 1, 2011| archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20120404030039/http://discuss.itwire.com/viewtopic.php?f=30&t=6493 | archive-date = April 4, 2012}}</ref></noinclude> These foods may actually have a protective effect.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Weisberger|first=L|author2=Jamieson, B |title=Clinical inquiries: How can you help prevent a recurrence of diverticulitis?|journal=The Journal of Family Practice|date=July 2009|volume=58|issue=7|pages=381–82|pmid=19607778}}</ref></noinclude>
* Eating less than an hour before swimming does not significantly increase the risk of experiencing muscle cramps, and does not increase the risk of drowning. One study shows a correlation between alcohol consumption and drowning, but not between eating and stomach cramps.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||url=https://www.nytimes.com/2005/06/28/health/28real.html|title=The Claim: Never Swim After Eating |work=[[The New York Times]]|date=June 28, 2005|access-date=January 16, 2011|first=Anahad|last=O'Connor}}; {{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.snopes.com/oldwives/hourwait.asp|title=Hour Missed Brooks|website=[[Snopes]]|date=January 3, 2005|access-date=January 16, 2011 }}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Vegan nutrition|Vegan]] and [[Vegetarian nutrition|vegetarian]] diets can provide enough protein for adequate nutrition.<noinclude><ref name="DefendingVeganDiet">a. {{#invoke:cite journal||last=Webb|first = Densie|title=Defending Vegan Diets – RDs Aim to Clear Up Common Misconceptions About Vegan Diets|journal = Today's Dietician|page = 20|date = September 2010|url=http://www.todaysdietitian.com/newarchives/082510p20.shtml|access-date =March 9, 2011|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131214120735/http://www.todaysdietitian.com/newarchives/082510p20.shtml|archive-date=December 14, 2013|url-status=live}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.acefitness.org/blog/86/are-vegetarian-diets-safe/|title=Are vegetarian diets safe?|last=Matthews|first=Jessica|publisher=American Council on Exercise|date=November 4, 2009|access-date=March 9, 2011|website=Ask the Expert|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130106231722/http://www.acefitness.org/blog/86/are-vegetarian-diets-safe|archive-date=January 6, 2013|url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude> In fact, typical protein intakes of [[Ovo-lacto vegetarianism|ovo-lacto vegetarians]] meet or exceed requirements.<noinclude><ref name="DieticiansGuide">{{#invoke:cite book||title=The dietitian's guide to vegetarian diets |last=Messina |first=Virginia |author2=Reed Mangles |author3=Mark Messina |date=2004 |publisher=Jones and Bartlett Publishers |location=Sudbury, MA |isbn=978-0-7637-3241-7}}</ref></noinclude> The American Dietetic Association maintains that appropriately planned vegetarian diets are healthful.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||title=Position of the American Dietetic Association: vegetarian diets |journal=Journal of the American Dietetic Association|year=2009 |pmid=19562864 |last1=Craig |first1=W. J. |last2=Mangels |first2=A. R. |author3=American Dietetic Association |volume=109 |issue=7 |pages=1266–1282 |doi=10.1016/j.jada.2009.05.027 |s2cid=7906168 |url=https://digitalcommons.andrews.edu/pubs/1954 }}</ref></noinclude> However, a vegan diet does require [[Dietary supplements|supplementation]] of [[vitamin B12|vitamin B<sub>12</sub>]],<noinclude><ref name="DefendingVeganDiet" /></noinclude> and [[Vitamin B12 deficiency|vitamin B<sub>12</sub> deficiency]] occurs in up to 80% of vegans that do not supplement their diet.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Woo |first1=Kam |last2=Kwok |first2=Timothy |last3=Celermajer |first3=David |date=19 August 2014 |title=Vegan Diet, Subnormal Vitamin B-12 Status and Cardiovascular Health |journal=Nutrients |volume=6 |issue=8 |pages=3259–3273 |doi=10.3390/nu6083259 |pmc=4145307 |pmid=25195560 |doi-access=free}}</ref></noinclude> Consuming no animal products increases the risk of deficiencies of vitamins B<sub>12</sub> and [[Vitamin D|D]], [[Calcium in biology|calcium]], [[Iron in biology|iron]], [[omega-3 fatty acid]]s,<noinclude><ref name="nutsoc">{{#invoke:cite journal||vauthors=Zampelas A, Magriplis E |date=February 2020 |title=Dietary patterns and risk of cardiovascular diseases: a review of the evidence |journal=Proc Nutr Soc |type=Review |volume=79 |issue=1 |pages=68–75 |doi=10.1017/S0029665119000946 |pmid=31250769 |s2cid=195757764 |quote=Few studies have reported the health benefits of vegan diets and therefore no conclusive evidence can be proposed|doi-access=free }}</ref></noinclude> and sometimes [[Iodine in biology|iodine]].<noinclude><ref name="ReferenceB">{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Eveleigh |first1=Elizabeth R. |last2=Coneyworth |first2=Lisa J. |last3=Avery |first3=Amanda |last4=Welham |first4=Simon J. M. |date=2020-05-29 |title=Vegans, Vegetarians, and Omnivores: How Does Dietary Choice Influence Iodine Intake? A Systematic Review |journal=Nutrients |volume=12 |issue=6 |pages=E1606 |doi=10.3390/nu12061606 |issn=2072-6643 |pmc=7352501 |pmid=32486114 |doi-access=free}}</ref></noinclude> Vegans are also at risk of low [[bone mineral density]] without supplementation for the aforementioned nutrients.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Iguacel |first1=Isabel |last2=Miguel-Berges |first2=María L |last3=Gómez-Bruton |first3=Alejandro |last4=Moreno |first4=Luis A |last5=Julián |first5=Cristina |date=January 2019 |title=Veganism, vegetarianism, bone mineral density, and fracture risk: a systematic review and meta-analysis |url=http://zaguan.unizar.es/record/84310 |journal=Nutrition Reviews |volume=77 |issue=1 |pages=1–18 |doi=10.1093/nutrit/nuy045 |pmid=30376075 |s2cid=53111636 |doi-access=free}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Swallowed chewing gum]] does not take seven years to digest. Chewing gum is mostly indigestible, and passes through the digestive system at the same rate as other matter.<noinclude><ref>a. {{cite magazine |url=http://www.scientificamerican.com/article.cfm?id=fact-or-fiction-chewing-gum-takes-seven-years-to-digest |title=Fact or Fiction?: Chewing Gum Takes Seven Years to Digest |magazine=Scientific American |first=John |last=Matson |date=October 11, 2007 |access-date=February 4, 2011 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140109065142/http://www.scientificamerican.com/article.cfm?id=fact-or-fiction-chewing-gum-takes-seven-years-to-digest |archive-date=January 9, 2014 |url-status=live}}
<br />b. [http://www.snopes.com/oldwives/chewgum.asp Claim: Chewing gum takes seven years to pass through the digestive system; FALSE]</ref></noinclude>
* The [[beta-Carotene|beta carotene]] in carrots does not enhance [[night vision]] beyond normal levels for people receiving an adequate amount, only in those with a [[Vitamin A deficiency|deficiency of vitamin A]].<noinclude><ref name="Carrots and vitamin A">{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.dietary-supplements.info.nih.gov/factsheets/vitamina.asp |title=Fact sheet for health professionals: Vitamin A |date=June 3, 2013 |access-date=December 29, 2016 |website=Office of Dietary Supplements, National Institutes of Health |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20080517093019/http://dietary-supplements.info.nih.gov/factsheets/vitamina.asp |archive-date=May 17, 2008 }}</ref></noinclude> The belief that it does may have originated from [[World War II]] British [[disinformation]] meant to explain the [[Royal Air Force]]'s improved success in night battles, which was actually due to radar and the use of red lights on instrument panels.<noinclude><ref name="Carrots and British propaganda">{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.scientificamerican.com/article/fact-or-fiction-carrots-improve-your-vision/ |title=Fact or Fiction?: Carrots Improve Your Vision |website=[[Scientific American]] |author=Maron DF|date=June 23, 2014|access-date=December 29, 2016}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Spinach#Nutrients|Spinach]] is not a particularly good source of [[Human iron metabolism|dietary iron]]. While it does contain more iron than many vegetables such as asparagus, Swiss chard, kale, or arugula, it contains only about one-third to one-fifth of the iron in lima beans, chickpeas, apricots, or wheat germ. Additionally, the [[Non-heme iron protein|non-heme]] iron found in spinach and other vegetables is not as readily absorbed as the [[heme]] iron found in meats and fish.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Dunkin |first=Mary Anne |title=Top Iron-Rich Foods List |url=https://www.webmd.com/diet/iron-rich-foods |access-date=2022-10-21 |website=WebMD |language=en}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=High Iron Content of Spinach – More Than a Myth? |url=https://www.healwithfood.org/articles/spinach-iron-content.php |access-date=2022-10-21 |website=www.healwithfood.org}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Mielewczik |first1=M. |last2=Moll |first2=J. |date=2016 |title=Spinach in Blunderland: How the myth that spinach is rich in iron became an urban academic legend |url=https://repository.rothamsted.ac.uk/item/8wq15/spinach-in-blunderland-how-the-myth-that-spinach-is-rich-in-iron-became-an-urban-academic-legend |journal=Annals of the History and Philosophy of Biology |volume=21 |pages=61–142 |doi=10.17875/gup2018-1125|doi-access=free }}</ref></noinclude>
* Most cases of [[obesity]] are not related to slower [[Basal metabolic rate|resting metabolism]]. Resting metabolic rate does not vary much between people. Overweight people tend to underestimate the amount of food they eat, and underweight people tend to overestimate. In fact, overweight people tend to have faster metabolic rates due to the increased energy required by the larger body.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite news||title=Does metabolism vary between two people?|url=https://examine.com/nutrition/does-metabolism-vary-between-two-people|newspaper=Examine.com|date=January 28, 2013}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite journal||first1=Kevin D.|last1=Hall|first2=Steven B.|last2=Heymsfield|first3=Joseph W.|last3=Kemnitz|first4=Samuel|last4=Klein|first5=Dale A.|last5=Schoeller|first6=John R.|last6=Speakman|title=Energy balance and its components: implications for body weight regulation|journal=The American Journal of Clinical Nutrition|date=April 1, 2012|issn=1938-3207|pages=989–94|volume=95|issue=4|pmid=22434603|doi=10.3945/ajcn.112.036350|pmc=3302369}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite news||title=The truth about slow metabolism|url=https://www.mayoclinic.org/healthy-lifestyle/weight-loss/expert-answers/slow-metabolism/faq-20058480|newspaper=Mayo Clinic}}
<br />d. {{#invoke:cite news||first1=Tim|last1=Crowe|title=Monday's medical myth: 'my slow metabolism makes me fat'|url=http://theconversation.com/mondays-medical-myth-my-slow-metabolism-makes-me-fat-4962|newspaper=The Conversation}}
<br />e. {{#invoke:cite journal||first1=Catharine|last1=Wang|first2=Elliot J.|last2=Coups|title=Causal beliefs about obesity and associated health behaviors: results from a population-based survey|journal=International Journal of Behavioral Nutrition and Physical Activity|date=March 3, 2010|issn=1479-5868|page=19|volume=7|doi=10.1186/1479-5868-7-19|pmid=20199677|pmc=2842229 |doi-access=free }}
<br />f. {{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Barry|first1=Colleen L.|last2=Brescoll|first2=Victoria L.|last3=Brownell |first3=Kelly D.|last4=Schlesinger|first4=Mark|title=Obesity Metaphors: How Beliefs about the Causes of Obesity Affect Support for Public Policy|journal=The Milbank Quarterly|date=2009|volume=87|issue=1|pages=7–47|pmid=19298414|doi=10.1111/j.1468-0009.2009.00546.x|pmc=2879183|citeseerx=10.1.1.175.4460}}
<br />g. {{#invoke:cite journal||first1=J. Eric|last1=Oliver|first2=Taeku|last2=Lee|title=Public Opinion and the Politics of Obesity in America|journal=Journal of Health Politics, Policy and Law|date=October 1, 2005|issn=0361-6878 |pages=923–954|volume=30|issue=5|pmid=16477792|doi=10.1215/03616878-30-5-923}}
<br />h. {{#invoke:cite journal||first1=C. R.|last1=Hankey|first2=S.|last2=Eley|first3=W. S.|last3=Leslie|first4=C. M.|last4=Hunter|first5=M. E. J.|last5=Lean|title=Eating habits, beliefs, attitudes and knowledge among health professionals regarding the links between obesity, nutrition and health|journal=Public Health Nutrition|date=2004|issn=1368-9800|pages=337–43|volume=7|issue=2|pmid=15003142|doi=10.1079/PHN2003526|doi-access=free}}
<br />i. {{#invoke:cite web||url=https://www.nhs.uk/live-well/healthy-weight/metabolism-and-weight-loss/|title=How can I speed up my metabolism?|date=April 26, 2018|website=nhs.uk|language=en|access-date=August 16, 2019}}</ref></noinclude>
* Eating normal amounts of soy does not cause [[Hormone|hormonal]] [[Endocrine disease|imbalance]].<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||url=https://ucdintegrativemedicine.com/2015/06/the-startling-truth-about-soy/|title=The Startling Truth About Soy|first=Rosane|last=Oliveira|work=UC Davis Integrative Medicine |date=June 9, 2015|access-date=February 28, 2019|archive-date=March 31, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190331193006/https://ucdintegrativemedicine.com/2015/06/the-startling-truth-about-soy/}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite news||url=https://www.independent.co.uk/life-style/health-and-families/soya-male-body-health-side-effects-truth-milk-sexual-function-a8382976.html|title=The truth about what soya does to men's bodies|date=June 12, 2018|website=The Independent}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite journal||title=Misconception and Concerns about Bioidentical Hormones Used for Custom-Compounded Hormone Therapy|first1=Frank Z.|last1=Stanczyk|first2=Bhagu R.|last2=Bhavnani|date=March 1, 2012|journal=The Journal of Clinical Endocrinology & Metabolism|volume=97|issue=3|pages=756–59|doi=10.1210/jc.2011-2492|pmid=22205711|doi-access=free}}
<br />d. {{#invoke:cite web||url=https://www.huhs.edu/sites/default/files/files/Soy%20protein%20article.pdf |title=Soy |website=www.huhs.edu }}
<br />e. {{#invoke:cite news||url=https://www.nytimes.com/2018/07/25/style/sperm-count.html|title=The Dawning of Sperm Awareness|first=Nellie|last=Bowles|work=The New York Times|date=July 25, 2018|via=NYTimes.com}}</ref></noinclude>

====== Alcoholic beverages ======
* [[Alcoholic beverage]]s do not make the entire body warmer.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite news||url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=kG5BAAAAIBAJ&pg=5953,3984482|title=Popular Misconceptions Regarding Intoxication|last=Brandstadt|first=William G.|date=December 19, 1967|work=Middlesboro Daily News|access-date=January 13, 2011}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite news||url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=Y7QOAAAAIBAJ&pg=6314,2739204|title=Hypothermia main outdoors threat|last=Pierson|first=Rebecca|date=December 9, 2004|work=Elizabethton Star|access-date=January 13, 2011}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite news||url=https://news.google.com/newspapers?id=AnRaAAAAIBAJ&pg=6238%2C1782448|title=Writer Tells Of Alcohol Dangers, Misconceptions|last=Seixas|first=Judy|date=April 15, 1977|work=The Virgin Islands Daily News|access-date=January 13, 2011}}</ref></noinclude> Alcoholic drinks create the sensation of warmth because they cause blood vessels to dilate and stimulate nerve endings near the surface of the skin with an influx of warm blood. This can actually result in making the core body temperature lower, as it allows for easier heat exchange with a cold external environment.
* Alcohol does not necessarily kill brain cells.<noinclude><ref name="StudyFindsAlcoholDoesntKillOffBrainCells">{{#invoke:cite news||url=http://www.news.com.au/national/study-finds-alcohol-doesnt-kill-off-brain-cells/story-e6frfkp9-1111113923217|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161129195758/http://www.news.com.au/national/study-finds-alcohol-doesnt-kill-off-brain-cells/story-e6frfkp9-1111113923217|archive-date=November 29, 2016|title=Study finds alcohol doesn't kill off brain cells &#124; News.com.au|access-date=March 10, 2019|date=July 10, 2007 }}</ref></noinclude> Alcohol can, however, lead ''indirectly'' to the death of brain cells in two ways. First, in chronic, heavy alcohol users whose brains have adapted to the effects of alcohol, abrupt ceasing following heavy use can cause [[excitotoxicity]] leading to cellular death in multiple areas of the brain.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||author=Lovinger, D. M.|date=1993| title=Excitotoxicity and Alcohol-Related Brain Damage |journal=Alcoholism: Clinical and Experimental Research |volume=17 |issue=1|pages=19–27 |doi=10.1111/j.1530-0277.1993.tb00720.x|pmid=8383925}}</ref></noinclude> Second, in alcoholics who get most of their daily calories from alcohol, a deficiency of [[thiamine]] can produce [[Korsakoff's syndrome]], which is associated with serious brain damage.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||author=Kopelman M. D.|author2=Thomson A.D.|author3=Guerrini I.|author4=Marshall E.J.|title=The Korsakoff syndrome: clinical aspects, psychology and treatment|journal=Alcohol and Alcoholism |volume=44|issue=2 |pages=148–54 |date=2009 |pmid=19151162|doi=10.1093/alcalc/agn118|doi-access=free}}</ref></noinclude>
* The order in which different types of alcoholic beverages are consumed ("Grape or grain but never the twain" and "Beer before liquor never sicker; liquor before beer in the clear") does not affect intoxication or create adverse side effects.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||title=Grape or grain but never the twain? A randomized controlled multiarm matched-triplet crossover trial of beer and wine|first1=Jöran|last1=Köchling|first2=Berit|last2=Geis|first3=Stefan|last3=Wirth |first4=Kai O.|last4=Hensel|date=February 1, 2019|journal=The American Journal of Clinical Nutrition|volume=109|issue=2|pages=345–52|doi=10.1093/ajcn/nqy309|pmid=30753321|pmc=6410559}}</ref></noinclude>
* Authentic [[absinthe]] has no [[hallucinogen]]ic properties, and is no more dangerous than any other alcoholic beverage of equivalent proof.<noinclude><ref name="sap_absinthism">{{#invoke:cite journal||title=Absinthism: a fictitious 19th century syndrome with present impact|doi=10.1186/1747-597X-1-14 |pmid=16722551 |pmc=1475830 |year=2006 |last1=Padosch |first1=Stephan A |last2=Lachenmeier |first2=Dirk W |last3=Kröner |first3=Lars U |journal=Substance Abuse Treatment, Prevention, and Policy |volume=1 |page=14 |doi-access=free }}</ref></noinclude> This misconception stems from late-19th- and early-20th-century distillers who produced cheap knockoff versions of absinthe, which used [[List of copper salts|copper salts]] to recreate the distinct green color of true absinthe, and some also reportedly adulterated cheap absinthe with poisonous [[antimony trichloride]], reputed to enhance the [[Ouzo effect|louche effect]].<noinclude><ref name="lafeeabsinthe.com">{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.lafeeabsinthe.com/absinthe-news-newsmenu-131/205-class-magazine-may-2009 |title=Class Mag May/June 2009 La Fee |publisher=Lafeeabsinthe.com |access-date=2 December 2016 |archive-date=December 2, 2016 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161202172106/http://www.lafeeabsinthe.com/absinthe-news-newsmenu-131/205-class-magazine-may-2009 }}</ref></noinclude>

==== Sexuality and reproduction ====
* [[Sexuality in older age|Older adults]] are not necessarily sexually inactive nor have they lost interest in sex; although the frequency of sexual activity tends to decline with age, older adults are still sexually active. One survey in [[England]] of people aged 60–69 recorded 86% of men and 60% of women as sexually active.<noinclude><ref name=letstalk>{{cite journal |vauthors=Steckenrider J |title=Sexual activity of older adults: let's talk about it |journal=Lancet Healthy Longev |volume=4 |issue=3 |pages=e96–e97 |date=March 2023 |pmid=36739874 |doi=10.1016/S2666-7568(23)00003-X |url=}}</ref></noinclude>
* "Double bagging", the practice of using two condoms at once, is not an extra-effective method of birth control; instead such use is more likely to cause condom breakage due to friction between the condoms.<noinclude><ref>{{cite journal | vauthors=Kopa Z, Scafa R, Graziani A, Goulis DG, Ferlin A | title=Male contraception: Focus on behavioral and barrier methods | journal=Andrology | date=29 July 2024 | volume=12 | issue=7 | pages=1535–1540 | issn=2047-2919 | doi=10.1111/andr.13722 | pmid=39075932 |type=Review| doi-access=free }}</ref></noinclude>
* It is not possible to get pregnant from semen released in a commercial [[swimming pool]] [[Non-penetrative sex|without penetration]]. The sperm cells would be quickly killed by the [[Swimming pool sanitation|chlorinated water]] and would not survive long enough to reach the vagina.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Mikkelson |first=David |date=2009-07-12 |title=Sperm in Swimming Pool |url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/pool-party/ |access-date=2022-07-23 |website=[[Snopes]] |language=en-US}}<br />b. {{#invoke:cite news||last=Andelane |first=Lana |date=2020-02-26 |title=Family Planning debunks claim women can get pregnant 'without penetration' in pools |language=en |work=[[Newshub]] |url=https://www.newshub.co.nz/home/lifestyle/2020/02/family-planning-debunks-claim-women-can-get-pregnant-without-penetration-in-pools.html |access-date=2022-07-23}}<br />c. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Taylor |first=Magdalene |date=2020-06-13 |title=Fact-Checking the Urban Legends About Getting Pregnant in Swimming Pools |url=https://melmagazine.com/en-us/story/swimming-pool-pregnancy-sperm |access-date=2022-07-23 |website=[[MEL Magazine]] |language=en-US}}<br />d. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Ewe |first=Koh |date=2020-02-24 |title=Indonesian Government Official Sitti Hikmawatty Thinks Women Can Get Pregnant From Swimming in Pools With Men |url=https://www.vice.com/en/article/k7enze/strong-sperm-women-pregnant-swimming-pool-indonesian-official |access-date=2022-07-23 |website=[[Vice (magazine)|Vice]] |language=en}}</ref></noinclude>
* An examination of the [[hymen]] is not an accurate or reliable indicator that a woman or girl has had penetrative [[Sexual intercourse|sex]], because the tearing of the hymen may have been the result of some other event, and some women are born without one.<noinclude><ref name="Hymen">{{#invoke:cite book||last1=Perlman |first1=Sally E. |url=https://archive.org/details/clinicalprotocol0000perl |title=Clinical protocols in pediatric and adolescent gynecology |last2=Nakajyma |first2=Steven T. |last3=Hertweck |first3=S. Paige |publisher=Parthenon |year=2004 |isbn=978-1-84214-199-1 |page=[https://archive.org/details/clinicalprotocol0000perl/page/131 131] |url-access=registration}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=https://nerdfighteria.info/v/CnRCI2cjg9U/|title=The Hymen Doesn't Tell You Anything About a Person|date=December 14, 2019|work=SciShow|last=Green |first=Hank |author-link=Hank Green}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Mishori |first1=R. |last2=Ferdowsian |first2=H. |last3=Naimer |first3=K. |last4=Volpellier |first4=M. |last5=McHale |first5=T. |date=2019-06-03 |title=The little tissue that couldn't – dispelling myths about the Hymen's role in determining sexual history and assault |journal=Reproductive Health |volume=16 |issue=1 |page=74 |doi=10.1186/s12978-019-0731-8 |pmc=6547601 |pmid=31159818 |doi-access=free}}</ref></noinclude> [[Virginity test]]s, such as the [[Virginity test#Two-finger test|"two-finger" test]], are widely considered to be unscientific.<noinclude><ref name="Perlman">{{#invoke:cite book||last1=Perlman |first1=Sally E. |title=Clinical protocols in pediatric and adolescent gynecology |last2=Nakajyma |first2=Steven T. |last3=Hertweck |first3=S. Paige |publisher=Parthenon |year=2004 |isbn=978-1-84214-199-1 |page=131}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=https://www.who.int/news-room/detail/17-10-2018-united-nations-agencies-call-for-ban-on-virginity-testing|title=United Nations agencies call for ban on virginity testing|date=October 17, 2018|publisher=World Health Organization|access-date=October 22, 2018}}</ref><ref name="ncjrs">[http://www.ncjrs.gov/pdffiles1/ovw/206554.pdf A National Protocol for Sexual Assault Medical Forensic Examinations] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110708172707/http://www.ncjrs.gov/pdffiles1/ovw/206554.pdf|date=July 8, 2011}} National Criminal Justice Reference Service (NCJRS). September 2004</ref></noinclude>
* Hand size<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||url=https://www.cnn.com/2016/03/08/health/trump-small-hands-penis/index.html|title=Trump: Do small hands equal small penis, or a myth?|first=Jen | last=Christensen|publisher=CNN}}</ref></noinclude> and foot size<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Shah |first1=J. |last2=Christopher |first2=N. |title=Can shoe size predict penile length? |journal=BJU International |date=2002 |volume=90 |issue=6 |pages=586–587 |doi=10.1046/j.1464-410X.2002.02974.x |pmid=12230622 |s2cid=20887458 |url=https://bjui-journals.onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1046/j.1464-410X.2002.02974.x |access-date=January 28, 2022 |language=en |issn=1464-410X}}</ref></noinclude> do not correlate with [[human penis size]], but [[digit ratio|finger length ratio]] may.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=https://articles.latimes.com/2011/jul/04/news/la-heb-finger-ratio-penis-length-20110704|title=Judging penis size by comparing index, ring fingers|first=Thomas H. |last=Maugh II|date=July 4, 2011|newspaper=[[Los Angeles Times]]}}</ref></noinclude>
* While pregnancies from sex between [[cousin marriage|first cousins]] do carry a slightly elevated risk of [[birth defect]]s, this risk is often exaggerated.<noinclude><ref name="kershaw">{{#invoke:cite news||first = Sarah |last = Kershaw |url = https://www.nytimes.com/2009/11/26/garden/26cousins.html |title = Shaking Off the Shame |date = November 26, 2009 | work=The New York Times}}</ref></noinclude> The risk is 5–6% (similar to that of a woman in her early 40s giving birth),<noinclude><ref name="kershaw" /><noinclude><ref name="Bennett">{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Bennett|first1=Robin L.|last2=Motulsky|first2=Arno G.|last3=Bittles|first3=Alan|last4=Hudgins|first4=Louanne|last5=Uhrich|first5=Stefanie|last6=Doyle |first6=Debra Lochner |last7=Silvey|first7=Kerry|last8=Scott|first8=C. Ronald|last9=Cheng|first9=Edith|last10=McGillivray|first10=Barbara|last11=Steiner|first11=Robert D.|last12=Olson|first12=Debra|title=Genetic Counseling and Screening of Consanguineous Couples and Their Offspring|journal=Journal of Genetic Counseling|date=2002|volume=11|issue=2|pages=97–119|doi=10.1023/A:1014593404915|pmid=26141656|s2cid=23922750|doi-access=free}}</ref></noinclude> compared with a baseline risk of 3–4%.<noinclude><ref name="Bennett" /></noinclude> The effects of [[inbreeding depression]], while still relatively small compared to other factors (and thus difficult to control for in a scientific experiment), become more noticeable if isolated and maintained for several generations.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite journal|| pmc = 1377721 | pmid=9915962 | doi=10.1086/302198 | volume=64 | issue=1 | title=Inbreeding effects on fertility in humans: evidence for reproductive compensation | date=January 1999 | journal=Am. J. Hum. Genet. | pages=225–31 | last1 = Ober | first1 = C | last2 = Hyslop | first2 = T | last3 = Hauck | first3 = WW}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite journal|| doi=10.1038/ejhg.2008.237|pmid = 19092776| pmc=2986271| title=Impact of inbreeding on fertility in a pre-industrial population| journal=European Journal of Human Genetics| volume=17| issue=5| pages=673–81| year=2009| last1=Robert| first1=Alexandre| last2=Toupance| first2=Bruno| last3=Tremblay| first3=Marc| last4=Heyer| first4=Evelyne}}</ref></noinclude>
* Having sex before a sporting event or contest is not physiologically detrimental to performance.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||url=http://www.nature.com/news/2006/060609/full/news060605-16.html |title=Sex before the big game? |journal=Nature |date=June 9, 2006 |access-date=January 16, 2011 |archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20121104140935/http://www.nature.com/news/2006/060609/full/news060605-16.html |archive-date= November 4, 2012 |url-status=live |doi=10.1038/news060605-16 |author=Ainsworth Claire |s2cid=179920555}}</ref></noinclude> In fact it has been suggested that sex prior to sports activity can elevate male [[testosterone]] levels, which could potentially enhance performance for male athletes.<noinclude><ref>{{cite magazine |title=Sex and Sports: Should Athletes Abstain Before Big Events? |url=http://news.nationalgeographic.com/news/2006/02/0222_060222_sex.html |magazine=National Geographic |date=February 22, 2006 |access-date=January 16, 2011 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140301110507/http://news.nationalgeographic.com/news/2006/02/0222_060222_sex.html |archive-date=March 1, 2014}}</ref></noinclude>
* The heightened sensitivity some women experience at the [[G-spot]] is not due to it being a distinct anatomical structure, but rather because pressure in that area may stimulate other internal structures, notably the [[Skene's gland]]. Many sexologists take issue with the term, concerned that women who "fail to find their G-spot" may feel abnormal.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite book||first1=Richard |last1=Balon |first2=Robert Taylor |last2=Segraves|title=Clinical Manual of Sexual Disorders |publisher= [[American Psychiatric Association|American Psychiatric Publishing]]|year=2009|access-date=January 24, 2014|page=258|isbn=978-1-58562-905-3|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=YuP3Hb0TMLQC&pg=PA258}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite book||first1=Jerrold S.|last1=Greenberg|first2=Clint E.|last2=Bruess|first3=Sara B. |last3=Oswalt|title=Exploring the Dimensions of Human Sexuality|pages=102–04|isbn=978-1-4496-4851-0|date=2014|access-date=October 30, 2014|publisher=[[Jones & Bartlett Publishers]]|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=hm3aTuANFroC&pg=PA102}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite journal||author=Hines T |s2cid=32381437 |date=August 2001 |title=The G-Spot: A modern gynecologic myth |journal=Am J Obstet Gynecol |volume=185 |issue=2 |pages=359–62 | doi=10.1067/mob.2001.115995 |pmid=11518892}}
<br />d. {{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Kilchevsky |first1=A |last2=Vardi |first2=Y |last3=Lowenstein|first3=L|last4=Gruenwald |first4=I|title=Is the Female G-Spot Truly a Distinct Anatomic Entity?|journal=[[The Journal of Sexual Medicine]]|volume= 9|issue= 3|pages= 719–26|date=January 2012|pmid=22240236|doi=10.1111/j.1743-6109.2011.02623.x}}
<br />e. {{lay source |template=cite news |date=January 19, 2012 |title=G-Spot Does Not Exist, 'Without A Doubt,' Say Researchers |url=http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2012/01/19/g-spot-does-not-exist_n_1215822.html |work=[[Huffington Post]]}}
<br />f. {{#invoke:cite journal||author=Vincenzo Puppo|date=June 6, 2012 |title=Does the G-spot exist? A review of the current literature|journal=International Urogynecology Journal|volume=23 |issue=12 |pages=1665–1669 | doi=10.1007/s00192-012-1831-y |pmid=22669428 |s2cid=1861061 |url=https://rdcu.be/c0ly8|quote="All published scientific data point to the fact that the G-spot does not exist..."}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Closeted]] or [[latent homosexuality]] is not correlated with [[internalized homophobia]]. A 1996 study claiming a connection in men<noinclude><ref name=homophobiastudy>{{#invoke:cite journal||pmid=8772014|year=1996|vauthors=Adams HE, Wright Jr LW, Lohr BA|title=Is homophobia associated with homosexual arousal?|volume=105|issue=3|pages=440–45|journal=Journal of Abnormal Psychology|doi=10.1037/0021-843X.105.3.440|url=http://my.psychologytoday.com/files/u47/Henry_et_al.pdf|access-date=June 14, 2021|archive-date=July 3, 2017|archive-url=https://wayback.archive-it.org/all/20170703071551/http://my.psychologytoday.com/files/u47/Henry_et_al.pdf}}</ref></noinclude> has not been verified by subsequent studies, including a 2013 study that found no correlation.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last1=MacInnis |first1=Cara C. |last2=Hodson |first2=Gordon |title=Is Homophobia Associated with an Implicit Same-Sex Attraction? |journal=Journal of Sex Research |date=November 2013 |volume=50 |issue=8 |pages=777–785 |doi=10.1080/00224499.2012.690111 |pmid=22989040 |s2cid=205442892 }}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[menstrual cycle]]s of women who live together do not [[menstrual synchrony|tend to synchronize]]. A 1971 study made this claim, but subsequent research has not supported it.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.scientificamerican.com/article.cfm?id=do-women-who-live-together-menstruate-together |title=Do Women Who Live Together Menstruate Together? |first=Anna |last=Gosline |date=December 7, 2007 |publisher=Scientific American |access-date=January 2, 2012}}</ref><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||doi=10.1080/00224499.2012.763085 |title=Darwin's Legacy: An Evolutionary View of Women's Reproductive and Sexual Functioning |year=2013 |last1=Harris |first1=Amy L. |last2=Vitzthum |first2=Virginia J. |journal=Journal of Sex Research |volume=50 |issue=3–4 |pages=207–46 |pmid=23480070|s2cid=30229421 }}</ref></noinclude>

==== Skin and hair ====
* [[Prune skin|Water-induced wrinkles]] are not caused by the skin absorbing water and swelling.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||last=Botcharova|first=Maria|title=A gripping tale: scientists claim to have discovered why skin wrinkles in water|url=https://www.theguardian.com/science/2013/jan/09/skin-wrinkle-water-grip?intcmp=239|access-date=January 28, 2013|newspaper=The Guardian|date=January 10, 2013 }}</ref></noinclude> They are caused by the [[autonomic nervous system]], which triggers localized [[vasoconstriction]] in response to wet skin, yielding a wrinkled appearance.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Changizi|first1=Mark |last2=Weber|first2=Romann |last3=Kotecha|first3=Ritesh |last4=Palazzo|first4=Joseph |title=Are Wet-Induced Wrinkled Fingers Primate Rain Treads?|journal=Brain Behav. Evol.|date=2011 |volume=77|pages=286–90|doi=10.1159/000328223|pmid=21701145|issue=4|doi-access=free}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite journal||last=Kareklas|first=Kyriacos|author2=Nettle, Daniel |author3=Smulders, Tom V. |title=Water-induced finger wrinkles improve handling of wet objects|journal=Biol. Lett.|date=April 23, 2013|volume=9|issue=2 |doi=10.1098/rsbl.2012.0999|pmid=23302867|page=20120999|pmc=3639753}}</ref></noinclude>
* A person's hair and fingernails do not continue to [[Human hair growth#Growth cycle|grow after death]]. Rather, the skin dries and shrinks away from the bases of hairs and nails, giving the appearance of growth.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Graham-Brown|first=Robin |author2=Tony Burns |title=Lecture Notes on Dermatology|publisher=Blackwell|date=2007|page=6|isbn=978-1-4051-3977-9}}</ref></noinclude>
* Shaving does not cause [[terminal hair]] to grow back thicker or darker. This belief is thought to be due to the fact that hair that has never been cut has a tapered end, so after cutting, the base of the hair is blunt and appears thicker and feels coarser. That short hairs are less flexible than longer hairs contributes to this effect.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||url=http://snopes.com/oldwives/hairgrow.asp|title=Shaved Hair Grows Darker|website=[[Snopes]]|date=October 2, 2003 |access-date=August 29, 2009|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140101222541/http://www.mayoclinic.com/health/hair-removal/an00638|archive-date=January 1, 2014|url-status=live}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.mayoclinic.com/health/hair-removal/an00638|title=Does shaving make hair grow back thicker?|website=[[Mayo Clinic]]|date=October 26, 2011|access-date=February 9, 2012|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140101222541/http://www.mayoclinic.com/health/hair-removal/an00638|archive-date=January 1, 2014|url-status=live}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.webmd.com/skin-beauty/shaving-tips-girls?page=2|title=Shaving Tips for Teen Girls|website=[[WebMD]]|access-date=February 9, 2012|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140101222541/http://www.mayoclinic.com/health/hair-removal/an00638|archive-date=January 1, 2014|url-status=live}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[MC1R]], the gene mostly responsible for red hair, is not [[red hair#Extinction hoax|becoming extinct]], nor will the [[Disappearing blonde gene|gene for blond hair]] do so, although both are [[recessive gene|recessive]] [[allele]]s. Redheads and blonds may become rarer but will not die out unless everyone who carries those alleles dies without passing their hair color genes on to their children.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||last=Silverman|first=Jacob|title=Are redheads going extinct?|url=http://science.howstuffworks.com/environmental/life/genetic/redhead-extinction.htm|publisher=HowStuffWorks|access-date=July 15, 2011 | archive-url = https://web.archive.org/web/20121203143345/http://science.howstuffworks.com/environmental/life/genetic/redhead-extinction.htm | archive-date = December 3, 2012| url-status=live|date=September 9, 2007}}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Acne#Diet|Acne]] is not caused by a lack of hygiene or eating fatty foods, though certain medication or a [[carbohydrate]]-rich diet may worsen it.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||title=Acne |url=https://www.mayoclinic.org/diseases-conditions/acne/symptoms-causes/syc-20368047 |website=Mayo Clinic |access-date=August 20, 2021}}</ref></noinclude>
* Dandruff is not caused by poor hygiene, though infrequent hair-washing can make it more obvious. The exact [[Dandruff#Causes|causes of dandruff]] are uncertain, but they are believed to be mostly genetic and environmental factors.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||title=How to treat dandruff |url=https://www.aad.org/public/everyday-care/hair-scalp-care/scalp/treat-dandruff |access-date=July 2, 2022 |website=[[American Academy of Dermatology]] |language=en |quote=Many people believe that dandruff is caused by poor hygiene, but this is not true.}}<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Rosenblum |first=Katie |date=September 25, 2019 |title=Dandruff: What It Is and What to Do About It |url=https://www.cedars-sinai.org/blog/what-is-dandruff.html |access-date=July 2, 2022 |website=[[Cedars-Sinai]] |language=en-US |quote=It's often associated with poor hygiene, but that's a misconception—no one's really sure what causes it.}}<br />c. {{#invoke:cite web||date=October 18, 2017 |title=Dandruff |url=https://www.nhs.uk/conditions/dandruff/ |access-date=July 2, 2022 |website=[[NHS]] |language=en |quote=Dandruff is not caused by poor hygiene, although it may be more obvious if you do not wash your hair regularly.}}</ref></noinclude>

=== Inventions ===
* [[James Watt]] did not invent the steam engine,<noinclude><ref name="JamesWatt">a. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Rolt|first=L. T. C.|title=James Watt|date=1962|publisher=Batsford|isbn=978-1-163-47052-7|page=10|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=VNrlAAAAIAAJ}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Carroll|first=John Millar|title=Designing interaction: psychology at the human-computer interface|date=1991|publisher=Cambridge University Press|isbn=978-0-521-40056-5|page=76|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=coY6AAAAIAAJ}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Green|first=Joey|title=Contrary to Popular Belief: More Than 250 False Facts Revealed|date=2005|publisher=Broadway Books|isbn=978-0-7679-1992-0|page=20|url=https://books.google.com/books?id=ew38DByz-DQC}}
<br />d. {{#invoke:cite web||url=http://physicsworldarchive.iop.org/index.cfm?action=summary&doc=3%2F12%2Fphwv3i12a41%40pwa-xml&qt=|title=Invention – Myth and Reality|publisher=Physics World|date=1990}}</ref></noinclude> nor were his ideas on steam engine power inspired by a kettle lid pressured open by steam.<noinclude><ref name="DPMiller">{{#invoke:cite journal||title=True Myths: James Watt's Kettle, His Condenser, and His Chemistry|date=2004|bibcode=2004HisSc..42..333M|last1=Miller|first1=David Philip|volume=42|issue=3|pages=333–60|journal=History of Science|doi=10.1177/007327530404200304|s2cid=161722497}}</ref></noinclude> Watt improved upon the already commercially successful [[Newcomen atmospheric engine]] (invented in 1712) in the 1760s and 1770s, making certain improvements critical to its future usage, particularly the external condenser, increasing its efficiency, and later the mechanism for transforming reciprocating motion into rotary motion; his new steam engine later gained huge fame as a result.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://dspace.dsto.defence.gov.au/dspace/bitstream/1947/3295/1/DSTO-RR-0287%20PR.pdf|title=An Evolutionary Framework for Experimental Innovation|publisher=Australian Government Department of Defence Defence Science and Technology Organisation|access-date=May 1, 2011|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20110815072201/http://dspace.dsto.defence.gov.au/dspace/bitstream/1947/3295/1/DSTO-RR-0287%20PR.pdf|archive-date=August 15, 2011}}</ref></noinclude>
* Although the guillotine was named after the French physician [[Joseph-Ignace Guillotin]], he neither invented nor was executed with this device. He died peacefully in his own bed in 1814. Rather, it was Guillotin's speech favoring beheadings over other forms of execution that led to the device being referred to as "La machine Guillotine" and later simply guillotine.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||access-date=June 5, 2020|title=Origins of the Guillotine|url=https://www.snopes.com/fact-check/head-man/|website=[[Snopes]]|date=September 4, 2011 }}</ref></noinclude>
* [[Thomas Crapper]] did not invent the flush toilet.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.snopes.com/business/names/crapper.asp|title=Thomas Crapper|work=[[Snopes]]|date=February 22, 2007|access-date=December 13, 2008 }}</ref></noinclude> A forerunner of the modern toilet was invented by the Elizabethan courtier [[John Harington (writer)#Invention of the modern toilet|Sir John Harington]] in the 16th century,<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite journal||last=Kinghorn|first=Jonathan| title=A Privvie in Perfection: Sir John Harrington's Water Closet | journal=Bath History | volume=1 | date=1986 | pages=173–88 }} {{ISBN|978-0-86299-294-1}}</ref></noinclude> and in 1775 the Scottish mechanic [[Alexander Cumming]] developed and patented a design for a toilet with an [[Trap (plumbing)|S-trap]] and flushing mechanism.<noinclude><ref name="Cumming">{{#invoke:cite news||title=From Charles Mackintosh's waterproof to Dolly the sheep: 43 innovations Scotland has given the world|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/uk/home-news/charles-mackintosh-chemist-waterproof-google-doodle-scotland-inventions-innovation-bicycles-a7499911.html|work=The independent|date=December 30, 2016}}</ref></noinclude> Crapper, however, did much to increase the popularity of the flush toilet and introduced several innovations in the late 19th century, holding nine patents, including one for the floating [[ballcock]].<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite news||title=Thomas Crapper: Myth & Reality|url=https://theplumber.com/thomas-crapper-myth-reality/|work=Plumbing & Mechanical Magazine|publisher=BNP Media|date=June 1, 1993}}</ref></noinclude>

[[File:Gluehlampe 01 KMJ.png|thumb|upright|A 230-volt incandescent light bulb.]]

* [[Thomas Edison]] did not invent the light bulb.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||last=Robert|first=Friedel|author2=Paul Israel|title=Edison's Electric Light: Biography of an Invention|location=New Brunswick, NJ|publisher=Rutgers University Press|pages=[https://archive.org/details/edisonselectricl00frie/page/115 115–17]|date=1987|isbn=978-0-8135-1118-4|url=https://archive.org/details/edisonselectricl00frie/page/115}}</ref></noinclude> The team of inventors Edison employed at his laboratories in Menlo Park, New Jersey did, however, develop the first ''practical'' light bulb in 1880 (employing a carbonized [[bamboo]] filament), shortly prior to [[Joseph Swan]], who invented an even more efficient bulb in 1881 (which used a cellulose filament).
* [[Henry Ford]] did not invent either the automobile or the assembly line. He did improve the assembly line process substantially, sometimes through his own engineering but more often through sponsoring the work of his employees, and he was the main person behind the introduction of the [[Ford Model T|Model T]], regarded as the first ''affordable'' automobile.<noinclude><ref>a. {{Hounshell1984}}, pp. 15–47.
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite book|| last = Sorensen | first = Charles E. |author2=Williamson, Samuel T. | author-link = Charles E. Sorensen | date = 1956 | title = My Forty Years with Ford | publisher = Norton | location = New York | isbn = 978-0-8143-3279-5 | url=https://books.google.com/books?id=fv9WPvAXpGMC&pg=PA128|page=128 | lccn = 56010854}}</ref></noinclude> [[Karl Benz]] (co-founder of [[Mercedes-Benz]]) is credited with the invention of the first modern automobile,<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite book||title=The Automobile Book| publisher=Paul Hamlyn Ltd| date=1967|
last=Stein|first=Ralph}}</ref></noinclude> and the assembly line has existed [[History of assembly lines|throughout history]].
* [[Al Gore]] never said that he had "invented" the Internet. What Gore actually said was, "During my service in the United States Congress, I took the initiative in creating the Internet", in reference to his political work towards developing the Internet for widespread public use.<noinclude><ref>{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.snopes.com/quotes/internet.asp|title=Al Gore on the invention of the internet|website=[[Snopes]]|date=May 5, 2005 |access-date=August 29, 2009 }}</ref></noinclude> Gore was the original drafter of the [[High Performance Computing and Communication Act of 1991]], which provided significant funding for supercomputing centers,<noinclude><ref name="cautionarytale" /></noinclude> and this in turn led to upgrades of a major part of the already-existing early 1990s Internet backbone, the [[NSFNet]],<noinclude><ref name="motherofgores">{{cite magazine |url=https://www.wired.com/2000/10/the-mother-of-gores-invention/ |title=The Mother of Gore's Invention |magazine=[[Wired (magazine)|Wired]] |date=October 17, 2000}}</ref></noinclude> and development of [[NCSA Mosaic]], the [[web browser|browser]] that popularized the [[World Wide Web]].<noinclude><ref name="cautionarytale">{{#invoke:cite news|| last = Kessler| first = Glenn| title = A cautionary tale for politicians: Al Gore and the 'invention' of the Internet| newspaper = Washington Post| date = November 4, 2013}}</ref></noinclude> (See also: [[Al Gore and information technology]])
* [[Kodak]] did not refuse to invest in digital cameras, but was rather a pioneer in the field,<noinclude><ref>{{cite web |last1=Aldred |first1=John |title=Kodak could have dominated digital photography |url=https://www.diyphotography.net/kodak-could-have-dominated-digital-photography/ |website=DIY Photography |access-date=4 January 2025}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |last1=Ries |first1=Al |title=Marketing Myth-Busting: Kodak Wasn't Slow to Digital; It Was the First One In |url=https://adage.com/article/al-ries/marketing-myth-busting-kodak-digital/232226 |website=Ad Age |publisher=Crain Communications, Inc |access-date=4 January 2025}}</ref></noinclude> and at one point was the market leader in digital camera sales in the United States.<noinclude><ref name="businessweek12">{{cite web |last1=Hamm |first1=Steve |last2=Symonds |first2=William C. |date=November 27, 2006 |title=Mistakes Made On The Road To Innovation |url=http://www.businessweek.com/magazine/content/06_48/b4011421.htm |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20061206024326/http://www.businessweek.com/magazine/content/06_48/b4011421.htm |archive-date=December 6, 2006 |access-date=January 19, 2012 |website=[[Businessweek]] |publisher=}}</ref></noinclude>

=== Mathematics ===
{{See also|All horses are the same color|Mathematical fallacy}}
[[File:Kapitolinischer Pythagoras adjusted.jpg|thumb|upright|alt=Marble bust of a man with a long, pointed beard, wearing a taenia, a kind of ancient Greek head covering in this case resembling a turban. The face is somewhat gaunt and has prominent, but thin, eyebrows, which seem halfway fixed into a scowl. The ends of his mustache are long a trail halfway down the length of his beard to about where the bottom of his chin would be if we could see it. None of the hair on his head is visible, since it is completely covered by the taenia.|Classical historians dispute whether [[Pythagoras]] made any mathematical discoveries.
<noinclude><ref>{{citation |last=Burkert |first=Walter |author-link=Walter Burkert |date=June 1, 1972 |title=Lore and Science in Ancient Pythagoreanism |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=0qqp4Vk1zG0C |location=Cambridge, Massachusetts |publisher=Harvard University Press |isbn=978-0-674-53918-1 |pages=428–33}}</ref>{{sfn|Kahn|2001|pages=2–3}}</noinclude>]]

* The Greek philosopher [[Pythagoras]] was not the first to discover the equation expressed in the [[Pythagorean theorem]], as it was known and used by the [[Babylonian mathematics|Babylonians]] and [[Indian mathematics|Indians]] centuries before him.<noinclude>{{sfn|Burkert|1972|pages=429, 462}}<ref>{{citation |last=Riedweg |first=Christoph |date=2005 |orig-date=2002 |title=Pythagoras: His Life, Teachings, and Influence |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=A8ixyQJA7_MC&q=Pythagoras |location=Ithaca, New York |publisher=Cornell University Press |isbn=978-0-8014-7452-1 |page=27}}</ref>{{sfn|Kahn|2001|page=32}}<noinclude><ref>{{citation |last=Ferguson |first=Kitty |date=2008 |title=The Music of Pythagoras: How an Ancient Brotherhood Cracked the Code of the Universe and Lit the Path from Antiquity to Outer Space |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=h83m1i3QhhYC&q=Pythagoras+Theano&pg=PA59 |location=New York City, New York |publisher=Walker & Company |isbn=978-0-8027-1631-6 |pages=6–7}}</ref><ref>{{citation |last=Joost-Gaugier |first=Christiane L. |title=Measuring Heaven: Pythagoras and his Influence on Thought and Art in Antiquity and the Middle Ages |date=2006 |page=143 |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=Cf9Rj_ADZU4C&q=Pythagoreanism&pg=PA116 |location=Ithaca, New York |publisher=Cornell University Press |isbn=978-0-8014-7409-5 |author-link=Christiane Joost-Gaugier}}</ref></noinclude> Pythagoras may have been [[Multiple discovery|the first to introduce it to the Greeks]],<noinclude>{{sfn|Burkert|1972|page=429}}{{sfn|Kahn|2001|page=32}}</noinclude> but the first record of it being [[mathematical proof|mathematically proven]] as a [[theorem]] is in [[Euclid's Elements|Euclid's ''Elements'']] which was published some 200 years after Pythagoras.
* There is no evidence that the ancient Greeks deliberately designed the [[Parthenon]] to match the [[golden ratio]].<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||author=Jesse Galef|url=http://measureofdoubt.com/2011/08/29/lies-and-legends-about-the-golden-ratio/|title=Lies and Debunked Legends about the Golden Ratio|date=August 29, 2011|access-date=April 10, 2013|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140427083317/http://measureofdoubt.com/2011/08/29/lies-and-legends-about-the-golden-ratio/|archive-date=April 27, 2014}}
<br />b. "Two other beliefs about [the golden ratio] are often mentioned in magazines and books: that the ancient Greeks believed it was the proportion of the rectangle the eye finds most pleasing and that they accordingly incorporated the rectangle in many of their buildings, including the famous Parthenon. These two equally persistent beliefs are likewise assuredly false and, in any case, are completely without any evidence." {{#invoke:cite book||last=Devlin|first=Keith|title=The Unfinished Game: Pascal, Fermat, and the Seventeenth-Century Letter that Made the World Modern|date=2008|publisher=Basic Books|page=35}}</ref></noinclude> The Parthenon was completed in 438&nbsp;BCE, more than a century before the first recorded mention of the ratio by [[Euclid]]. Similarly, [[Leonardo da Vinci]]'s ''[[Vitruvian Man]]'' makes no mention of the golden ratio in its text, although it describes many other proportions.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||author=Donald E. Simanek |url=http://www.lhup.edu/~dsimanek/pseudo/fibonacc.htm |title=Fibonacci Flim-Flam |access-date=April 9, 2013 |archive-url=https://www.webcitation.org/5nDtkyeKW?url=http://www.lhup.edu/~dsimanek/pseudo/fibonacc.htm |archive-date=February 1, 2010 }}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||first=Keith|last=Devlin|url=http://www.maa.org/devlin/devlin_05_07.html|title=The Myth That Will Not Go Away|access-date=April 10, 2013|date=May 2007|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130701231044/http://www.maa.org/devlin/devlin_05_07.html|archive-date =July 1, 2013|quote=Part of the process of becoming a mathematics writer is, it appears, learning that you cannot refer to the golden ratio without following the first mention by a phrase that goes something like 'which the ancient Greeks and others believed to have divine and mystical properties.' Almost as compulsive is the urge to add a second factoid along the lines of 'Leonardo Da Vinci believed that the human form displays the golden ratio.' There is not a shred of evidence to back up either claim, and every reason to assume they are both false. Yet both claims, along with various others in a similar vein, live on.}}</ref></noinclude>
* The repeating decimal commonly written as [[0.999...]] represents exactly the same quantity as the number [[1 (number)|one]]. Despite having the appearance of representing a smaller number, 0.999... is a symbol for the number [[1 (number)|1]] in exactly the same way that 0.333... is an equivalent notation for the number represented by the fraction {{frac|1|3}}.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite book||first=John |last=Stillwell |author-link=John Stillwell |title=Elements of algebra: geometry, numbers, equations|year=1994|publisher=Springer |page=42 }}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Bunch |first=Bryan H. |title=Mathematical fallacies and paradoxes |year=1982 |publisher=Van Nostrand Reinhold |isbn=978-0-442-24905-2|page=119}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Tall|first1=David|author-link1=David Tall |last2=Schwarzenberger|first2=R. L. E.|author-link2=Rolph Ludwig Edward Schwarzenberger |title=Conflicts in the Learning of Real Numbers and Limits|journal=Mathematics Teaching|year=1978|volume=82|pages=6, 44–49|url=http://www.warwick.ac.uk/staff/David.Tall/pdfs/dot1978c-with-rolph.pdf |access-date=May 3, 2009|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20090530043040/http://www.warwick.ac.uk/staff/David.Tall/pdfs/dot1978c-with-rolph.pdf| archive-date=May 30, 2009}}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[p-value|''p''-value]] is not the probability that the [[null hypothesis]] is true, or the probability that the [[alternative hypothesis]] is false; it is the probability of obtaining results at least as extreme as the results actually observed under the assumption that the null hypothesis was correct, which can indicate the incompatibility of results with the specific statistical model assumed in the null hypothesis.<noinclude><ref name="asa2016">{{#invoke:cite journal||vauthors=Wasserstein RL, Lazar NA |year=2016 |title=The ASA's statement on ''p''-values: context, process, and purpose |journal=[[The American Statistician]] |volume=70 |issue=2 |pages=129–33 |doi=10.1080/00031305.2016.1154108|s2cid=124084622 |url=https://www.stat.berkeley.edu/~aldous/Real_World/ASA_statement.pdf |doi-access=free }}</ref></noinclude> This misconception, and similar ones like it, contributes to the common [[misuse of p-values|misuse of ''p''-values]] in education and research.<noinclude><ref name="asa2016" /><ref name="Sterne2001">{{#invoke:cite journal|| vauthors = Sterne JA, Davey Smith G | title = Sifting the evidence-what's wrong with significance tests? | journal = BMJ | volume = 322 | issue = 7280 | pages = 226–31 | date = January 2001 | pmid = 11159626 | pmc = 1119478 | doi = 10.1136/bmj.322.7280.226 }}</ref></noinclude>
* If one were to flip a [[fair coin]] five times and get heads each time, it would not be any more likely for a sixth flip to come up tails. Phrased another way, after a long and/or unlikely [[wikt:streak#:~:text=A continuous series of like events|streak]] of [[Independence (probability theory)|independently]] [[random]] events, the probability of the next event is not influenced by the preceding events. [[Gambler's fallacy|Humans often feel that the underrepresented outcome is more likely]], as if it is due to happen. Such thinking may be attributed to the mistaken belief that gambling, or even chance itself, is a fair process that can correct itself in the event of streaks.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite journal||author=J. Michael Shaughnessy |year=1977 |title=Misconceptions of probability: An experiment with a small-group, activity-based, model building approach to introductory probability at the college level |journal=Educational Studies in Mathematics |volume=8 |issue=3 |pages=295–316 |doi=10.1007/BF00385927|s2cid=120555285 }}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite book||author=Henk&nbsp;Tijms |title=Understanding Probability: Chance Rules in Everyday Life |publisher=Cambridge University Press |year=2007 |isbn=978-0-521-70172-3 |page=79}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite book||author=Maxwell, Nicholas |title=Data Matters: Conceptual Statistics for a Random World |publisher=Key College |year=2004 |isbn=1-930190-89-1 |page=63}}
<br />d. {{#invoke:cite book||title=The Corsini Encyclopedia of Psychology and Behavioral Science |publisher=Wiley |year=2000 |isbn=0-471-24097-4 |editor=W.&nbsp;Edward&nbsp;Craighead, Charles&nbsp;B.&nbsp;Nemeroff |volume=2 |page=617}}
<br />e. Oppenheimer, D.M., & Monin, B. (2009). The retrospective gambler's fallacy: Unlikely events, constructing the past, and multiple universes. ''Judgment and Decision Making, vol. 4, no. 5,'' pp. 326-334
<br />f. {{#invoke:cite web||date=2015-01-02 |title=Why we gamble like monkeys |url=http://www.bbc.com/future/story/20150127-why-we-gamble-like-monkeys |work=BBC.com}}
<br />g. {{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Rogers |first1=Paul |year=1998 |title=The cognitive psychology of lottery gambling: A theoretical review |journal=Journal of Gambling Studies |volume=14 |issue=2 |pages=111–134 |doi=10.1023/A:1023042708217 |issn=1050-5350 |pmid=12766438 |s2cid=21141130}}</ref></noinclude>

=== Physics ===
[[File:Equal transit-time NASA wrong1 en.svg|thumb|upright=1.35|The incorrect equal-transit-time explanation of aerofoil lift]]
* The [[Lift (force)|lift force]] is not generated by the air taking the same time to travel above and below an aircraft's wing.<noinclude><ref name="NASA_Incorrect_Theory1">{{#invoke:cite web||url=http://www.grc.nasa.gov/WWW/K-12/airplane/wrong1.html |title=Incorrect Lift Theory |publisher=NASA Glenn Research Center |work=grc.nasa.gov |date=July 28, 2008 |access-date=January 13, 2011 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140427084226/http://www.grc.nasa.gov/WWW/K-12/airplane/wrong1.html |archive-date=April 27, 2014 }} (Java applet).</ref></noinclude> This misconception, sometimes called the [[equal transit-time fallacy]], is widespread among textbooks and non-technical reference books, and even appears in pilot training materials. In fact, the air moving over the top of an aerofoil generating lift is always moving much faster than the equal transit theory would imply,<noinclude><ref name="NASA_Incorrect_Theory1" /></noinclude> as described in the [[Equal transit-time fallacy|incorrect]] and [[Lift (force)#Simplified physical explanations of lift on an airfoil|correct explanations]] of lift force.
* Blowing over a curved piece of paper does not demonstrate [[Bernoulli's principle#Misapplications of Bernoulli's principle in common classroom demonstrations|Bernoulli's principle]]. Although a common classroom experiment is often explained this way,<noinclude><ref>a. {{cite magazine |title=This occurs because of Bernoulli's principle – fast-moving air has lower pressure than non-moving air |url=http://makeprojects.com/Project/Origami-Flying-Disk/327/1 |archive-url=https://archive.today/20130103152803/http://makeprojects.com/Project/Origami-Flying-Disk/327/1%23.UOWjZ33LdRw |archive-date=January 3, 2013 |access-date=September 5, 2012 |magazine=Make Magazine}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite web||title=Paper Lift |url=https://physicsforce.umn.edu/content/paper-lift-0 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201112021453/https://physicsforce.umn.edu/content/paper-lift-0 |archive-date=November 12, 2020 |access-date=January 7, 2021 |work=Physics Force |publisher=University of Minnesota}}.
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite web||title=Educational Packet |url=http://www.tallshipschannelislands.com/PDFs/Educational_Packet.pdf |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131203014334/http://www.tallshipschannelislands.com/PDFs/Educational_Packet.pdf |archive-date=December 3, 2013 |access-date=June 25, 2012 |work=Tall Ships Festival: Channel Islands Harbor |quote=Bernoulli's Principle states that faster moving air has lower pressure... You can demonstrate Bernoulli's Principle by blowing over a piece of paper held horizontally across your lips."}}</ref></noinclude> Bernoulli's principle only applies within a flow field, and the air above and below the paper is in different flow fields.<noinclude><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Craig |first=Gale M. |title=Physical Principles of Winged Flight |url=http://www.regenpress.com/aerodynamics.pdf |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210307172349/http://regenpress.com/aerodynamics.pdf |archive-date=March 7, 2021 |access-date=September 5, 2012 |quote=If the lift in figure A were caused by "Bernoulli principle," then the paper in figure B should droop further when air is blown beneath it. However, as shown, it raises when the upward pressure gradient in downward-curving flow adds to atmospheric pressure at the paper lower surface.}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite journal||last=Babinsky |first=Holger |year=2003 |title=How Do Wings Work |url=https://www.researchgate.net/publication/230910482 |journal=Physics Education |volume=38 |pages=497–502 |bibcode=2003PhyEd..38..497B |doi=10.1088/0031-9120/38/6/001 |s2cid=1657792 |access-date=January 7, 2021 |number=6}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite journal||last=Eastwell |first=Peter |year=2007 |title=Bernoulli? Perhaps, but What About Viscosity? |url=http://d1vdx9ifs4n5d7.cloudfront.net/s3fs-public/davidson_images/eastwell-bernoulli.pdf |journal=The Science Education Review |volume=6 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180318183632/http://d1vdx9ifs4n5d7.cloudfront.net/s3fs-public/davidson_images/eastwell-bernoulli.pdf |archive-date=March 18, 2018 |access-date=September 10, 2023 |quote=...air does not have a reduced lateral pressure (or static pressure...) simply because it is caused to move, the static pressure of free air does not decrease as the speed of the air increases, it misunderstanding Bernoulli's principle to suggest that this is what it tells us, and the behavior of the curved paper is explained by other reasoning than Bernoulli's principle. ... An explanation based on Bernoulli's principle is not applicable to this situation, because this principle has nothing to say about the interaction of air masses having different speeds... Also, while Bernoulli's principle allows us to compare fluid speeds and pressures along a single streamline and... along two different streamlines that originate under identical fluid conditions, using Bernoulli's principle to compare the air above and below the curved paper in Figure 1 is nonsensical; in this case, there aren't any streamlines at all below the paper!}}
<br />d. {{#invoke:cite web||last=Raskin |first=Jef |title=Coanda Effect: Understanding Why Wings Work |url=http://karmak.org/archive/2003/02/coanda_effect.html}}
<br />e. {{#invoke:cite journal||last=Auerbach |first=David |year=2000 |title=Why Aircraft Fly |url=https://www.researchgate.net/publication/230994575 |journal=European Journal of Physics |volume=21 |issue=4 |pages=292, 295 |bibcode=2000EJPh...21..289A |doi=10.1088/0143-0807/21/4/302 |s2cid=250821727}}
<br />f. {{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Smith |first1=Norman F. |date=November 1972 |title=Bernoulli and Newton in Fluid Mechanics |journal=The Physics Teacher |volume=10 |issue=8 |pages=451–455 |bibcode=1972PhTea..10..451S |doi=10.1119/1.2352317}}</ref></noinclude> The paper rises because the air follows the curve of the paper and a curved [[Streamlines, streaklines, and pathlines|streamline]] will develop pressure differences perpendicular to the airflow.<noinclude><ref name="airflow">a. {{#invoke:cite journal||last=Babinsky |first=Holger |year=2003 |title=How Do Wings Work |url=https://www.researchgate.net/publication/230910482 |journal=Physics Education |volume=38 |issue=6 |pages=497–503 |bibcode=2003PhyEd..38..497B |doi=10.1088/0031-9120/38/6/001 |s2cid=1657792 |access-date=January 7, 2021 |quote=...if a streamline is curved, there must be a pressure gradient across the streamline, with the pressure increasing in the direction away from the centre of curvature.}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite journal||last1=Smith |first1=Norman F. |date=April 1973 |title=Bernoulli, Newton, and Dynamic Lift Part II*: Bernoulli or Newton? |journal=School Science and Mathematics |volume=73 |issue=4 |pages=327–335 |doi=10.1111/j.1949-8594.1973.tb09040.x |quote=The curved paper turns the stream of air downward, and this action produces the lift reaction that lifts the paper.}}
<br />c. {{#invoke:cite web||title=AERONAUTICS: An Educator's Guide with Activities in Science, Mathematics, and Technology Education |url=http://www.nasa.gov/pdf/58152main_Aeronautics.Educator.pdf |access-date=January 7, 2021 |publisher=NASA |page=26 |quote=The curved surface of the tongue creates unequal air pressure and a lifting action. ... Lift is caused by air moving over a curved surface.}}</ref><ref>a. {{#invoke:cite book||last1=Anderson |first1=David F. |url=https://books.google.com/books?id=52Hfn7uEGSoC&pg=PA229 |title=Understanding Flight |last2=Eberhardt |first2=Scott |publisher=McGraw Hill Professional |year=2000 |isbn=978-0-07-138666-1 |page=229 |quote=Demonstrations" of Bernoulli's principle are often given as demonstrations of the physics of lift. They are truly demonstrations of lift, but certainly not of Bernoulli's principle. |via=Google Books}}
<br />b. {{#invoke:cite book||last=Feil |first=Max |title=The Aeronautics File |quote=As an example, take the misleading experiment most often used to "demonstrate" Bernoulli's principle. Hold a piece of paper so that it curves over your finger, then blow across the top. The paper will rise. However most people do not realize that the paper would NOT rise if it was flat, even though you are blowing air across the top of it at a furious rate. Bernoulli's principle does not apply directly in this case. This is because the air on the two sides of the paper did not start out from the same source. The air on the bottom is ambient air from the room, but the air on the top came from your mouth where you actually increased its speed without decreasing its pressure by forcing it out of your mouth. As a result the air on both sides of the flat paper actually has the same pressure, even though the air on the top is moving faster. The reason that a curved piece of paper does rise is that the air from your mouth speeds up even more as it follows the curve of the paper, which in turn lowers the pressure according to Bernoulli.}}</ref></noinclude>
* The [[Coriolis effect]] does not cause water to consistently drain from basins in a clockwise/counter-clockwise direction depending on the hemisphere. The common myth often refers to the draining action of flush toilets and bathtubs.
